Title: Finance Act 2024
Date: 2024-10-18
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2024/3

## Finance Act 2024

      Most Gracious Sovereign           W e  , Your Majesty’s most dutiful and
loyal subjects, the Commons of the United Kingdom in Parliament assembled,
towards raising the necessary supplies to defray Your Majesty’s public
expenses, and making an addition to the public revenue, have freely and
voluntarily resolved to give and to grant unto Your Majesty the several duties
hereinafter mentioned; and do therefore most humbly beseech Your Majesty that
it may be enacted, and be it enacted by the King’s most Excellent Majesty, by
and with the advice and consent of the Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and
Commons, in this present Parliament assembled, and by the authority of the
same, as follows:—

### Income tax and corporation tax

#### Reliefs for businesses etc

##### Capital allowances for companies

###### Permanent full expensing etc for expenditure on plant or machinery

1

1.1

In section 7 of F(No.2)A 2023 (temporary full expensing etc for expenditure on
plant or machinery), in subsection (3), in the inserted section 45S of CAA
2001, in paragraph (a), omit “but before 1 April 2026”.

1.2

In consequence of the provision made by  subsection (1) —

1.2.a

the amendments made by subsections (2) to (6) of section 7 of F(No.2)A 2023
are instead to operate as textual amendments of Part 2 of CAA 2001, and

1.2.b

accordingly, in subsection (1) of that section, for the words from “has
effect” to the end substitute  “is amended as follows” , and, in the italic
heading inserted by subsection (6) of that section, omit “temporary”.

##### Research and development

###### New regime for research and development carried out by companies

2

Schedule 1 —

2.a

replaces the existing scheme for R&D expenditure credit,

2.b

amends the existing scheme for R&D relief, and

2.c

makes related provision.

##### Films, television programmes, video games etc

###### Films, television programmes and video games produced by companies

3

Schedule 2  replaces Parts 15 to 15B of CTA 2009 with a new regime for the
taxation of companies producing films, television programmes and video games,
including relief in the form of payable credits arising from expenditure on
production activities.

###### Theatrical productions made by companies

4

Schedule 3  amends the regime for the taxation of companies producing
theatrical productions in Part 15C of CTA 2009.

###### Orchestral concerts produced by companies

5

Schedule 4  amends the regime for the taxation of companies producing
orchestral concerts in Part 15D of CTA 2009.

###### Museum and gallery exhibitions produced by companies

6

Schedule 5  amends the regime for the taxation of companies producing museum
and gallery exhibitions in Part 15E of CTA 2009.

###### Sections 

7

Schedule 6  amends Schedule 18 to FA 1998 (company tax returns etc) in
relation to the reliefs introduced or amended by sections  3  to  6 .

##### Real Estate Investment Trusts

###### Miscellaneous amendments relating to REITs

8

Schedule 7  makes miscellaneous amendments to the corporation tax regime for
Real Estate Investment Trusts.

##### Tonnage tax

###### Managers of ships

9

Schedule 8  amends Schedule 22 to FA 2000 to make provision to enable
companies, and groups of companies, that manage qualifying ships to make a
tonnage tax election (so that their profits for the purposes of corporation
tax are calculated in accordance with the tonnage tax regime).

###### Increase in capital allowances limit for ship leasing

10

10.1

Paragraph 94 of Schedule 22 to FA 2000 (tonnage tax: restrictions on capital
allowances) is amended as follows.

10.2

In sub-paragraph (3), for “£40 million”, in both places it occurs, substitute
“£100 million” .

10.3

In sub-paragraph (5), for “£80 million” substitute  “£200 million” .

10.4

The amendments made by subsections (2) and (3) have effect in relation to
leases entered into on or after 1 April 2024.

##### Other reliefs

###### Extension of EIS relief and VCT relief to shares issued before 6 April 2035

11

11.1

In—

11.1.a

section 157(1)(aa) of ITA 2007 (which limits EIS relief to shares issued
before 6 April 2025), and

11.1.b

section 261(3)(za) of that Act (which limits VCT relief to shares issued
before that date),

for “2025” substitute  “2035” .

11.2

This section comes into force on such day as the Treasury may by regulations
appoint.

###### Relief for payments of compensation by government etc to companies

12

12.1

FA 2020 is amended as follows.

12.2

After paragraph 5 of Schedule 15 (tax relief for scheme payments) insert—

############ Corporation tax and other related relief

############# Introductory

12.2.6

This Part of this Schedule provides for the following—

12.2.6.a

an exemption from corporation tax for relevant compensation payments, and

12.2.6.b

an exemption from income tax and capital gains tax for relevant onward
payments.

############# Relevant compensation payments

12.2.7

12.2.7.1

In this Part of this Schedule “ relevant compensation payment ” means a
payment made to a company under—

12.2.7.1.a

the GLO Compensation Scheme,

12.2.7.1.b

the Horizon Shortfall Scheme,

12.2.7.1.c

the Suspension Remuneration Review,

12.2.7.1.d

the Post Office Process Review, or

12.2.7.1.e

such other compensation scheme of a description specified in regulations made
by the Treasury.

12.2.7.2

The power under sub-paragraph  (1) (e)  to specify a description of
compensation scheme is exercisable only if the scheme provides for the payment
of compensation to persons by or on behalf of—

12.2.7.2.a

the government of the United Kingdom,

12.2.7.2.b

the government of a part of the United Kingdom,

12.2.7.2.c

the government of any other country or territory,

12.2.7.2.d

a local or other public authority in the United Kingdom, or

12.2.7.2.e

a local or other public authority of a territory outside the United Kingdom.

12.2.7.3

The power under sub-paragraph  (1) (e)  may be exercised so as to provide—

12.2.7.3.a

for the provisions of this Part of this Schedule to apply to all descriptions
of payments made under a compensation scheme or only to such descriptions as
may be specified in the regulations;

12.2.7.3.b

for all provisions of this Part of this Schedule to apply to payments made
under a compensation scheme or only for such provisions to apply as are
specified in the regulations.

12.2.7.4

The power under sub-paragraph  (1) (e)  must be exercised so as to provide
that the reliefs conferred by this Part of this Schedule in respect of the
compensation schemes mentioned in sub-paragraph (1)(a) to (d) are also
conferred in a corresponding or similar way in respect of other relevant
schemes.

12.2.7.5

The reference in sub-paragraph (4) to “ relevant schemes ” is a reference to
any compensation schemes established for the purposes of—

12.2.7.5.a

compensating persons affected by the Horizon system, or

12.2.7.5.b

compensating persons in respect of other matters identified in High Court
judgments given in proceedings relating to the Horizon system.

############# Relevant onward payments

12.2.8

12.2.8.1

For the purposes of this Part of this Schedule a payment is a “relevant onward
payment” if or to the extent that—

12.2.8.1.a

the payment is made by a company to which a relevant compensation payment was
made,

12.2.8.1.b

the payment is to an individual and—

12.2.8.1.b.i

the individual is or was a director or employee of the company, or

12.2.8.1.b.ii

the payment is a distribution by the company to shareholders, and

12.2.8.1.c

it is reasonable to conclude from the circumstances that the payment is made
by the company to the individual for the purpose of passing on all or part of
the compensation payment mentioned in paragraph (a) to the individual.

12.2.8.2

But where sub-paragraph (3) applies to the relevant compensation payment
mentioned in sub-paragraph (1)(a), a payment to an individual is a relevant
onward payment for the purposes of this Part of this Schedule only so far as
it relates to such part of the relevant compensation payment as was made for
the purpose of topping up the amount of compensation paid to account for sums
lost to tax.

12.2.8.3

This sub-paragraph applies to a relevant compensation payment—

12.2.8.3.a

made (at any time) under the Horizon Shortfall Scheme;

12.2.8.3.b

made before 1 January 2024 under the Suspension Remuneration Review.

############# Exemption from corporation tax

12.2.9

12.2.9.1

No liability to corporation tax arises in respect of a relevant compensation
payment.

12.2.9.2

The following are to be ignored for all other corporation tax purposes—

12.2.9.2.a

the receipt by a company of a relevant compensation payment;

12.2.9.2.b

the making by a company of a relevant onward payment.

12.2.9.3

This paragraph has effect—

12.2.9.3.a

in the case of relevant compensation payments falling within paragraph  7
(1)(a), (b), (c) or (d), whenever the payments are received;

12.2.9.3.b

in the case of relevant compensation payments falling within paragraph  7
(1)(e), where the payments are received on or after such date as is specified
in the regulations concerned;

12.2.9.3.c

in the case of relevant onward payments that relate to paragraph  7 (1)(a),
(b), (c) or (d), whenever the payments are made;

12.2.9.3.d

in the case of relevant onward payments that relate to paragraph  7 (1)(e),
where the payments are made on or after such date as is specified in the
regulations concerned.

12.2.9.4

The date specified in regulations as mentioned in sub-paragraph (3)(b) and (d)
may be a date before the regulations are made.

############# Exemption from income tax and capital gains tax

12.2.10

12.2.10.1

Paragraph 3(1) and (2) (exemption from income tax) applies to a relevant
onward payment as it applies to a qualifying payment.

12.2.10.2

Paragraph 4(1) and (2) (exemption from capital gains tax) applies to a
relevant onward payment as it applies to a qualifying payment.

12.2.10.3

Sub-paragraph (1) has effect—

12.2.10.3.a

in the case of relevant onward payments that relate to paragraph  7 (1)(a),
(b), (c) or (d), whenever the payments are received;

12.2.10.3.b

in the case of relevant onward payments that relate to paragraph  7 (1)(e),
where the payments are received on or after such date as is specified in the
regulations concerned.

12.2.10.4

Sub-paragraph (2) has effect—

12.2.10.4.a

in the case of relevant onward payments that relate to paragraph  7 (1)(a),
(b), (c) or (d), in relation to disposals whenever made;

12.2.10.4.b

in the case of relevant onward payments that relate to paragraph  7 (1)(e), in
relation to disposals made on or after such date as is specified in the
regulations concerned.

12.2.10.5

The date specified in regulations as mentioned in sub-paragraph (3)(b) and
(4)(b) may be a date before the regulations are made.

############# Power to make further provision

12.2.11

12.2.11.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision for the purpose of providing
relief from corporation tax, income tax or capital gains tax in relation to
the receipt of payments made under compensation schemes that is supplementary
or incidental to provision contained in this Part of this Schedule.

12.2.11.2

Provision under this paragraph may (among other things)—

12.2.11.2.a

make different provision for different compensation schemes;

12.2.11.2.b

make provision having retrospective effect.

############# Regulations: general

12.2.12

12.2.12.1

A power to make regulations under this Part of this Schedule is exercisable by
statutory instrument.

12.2.12.2

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this Part of this Schedule
is subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of the House of Commons.

############# Interpretation

12.2.13

12.2.13.1

In this Part of this Schedule—

      “ GLO Compensation Scheme ” means the scheme announced by His Majesty’s
Government on 22 March 2022 with the objective of ensuring that persons who
were party to a claim against Post Office Limited in respect of the Horizon
system that was subject to a group litigation order have access to
compensation for losses related to that system;           “ Horizon Shortfall
Scheme ” means the scheme established on 1 May 2020 by Post Office Limited to
compensate persons who were adversely affected by accounting shortfalls
related to the Horizon system;           “ the Horizon system ” means previous
versions of the computer system used by Post Office Limited known as Horizon
(and sometimes referred to as Legacy Horizon, Horizon Online or HNG-X);
“ Post Office Limited ” means the private company limited by shares with the
company number 02154540 whose registered office is 100 Wood Street, London
EC2V 7ER;           “ Post Office Process Review ” means the review
established by Post Office Limited to provide redress to postmasters who were
financially impacted by previous processes or policies in relation to balance
discrepancies unrelated to the Horizon system;           “ Suspension
Remuneration Review ” means the review established by Post Office Limited to
provide redress to postmasters contracted to deliver Post Office services
through branches who were suspended before March 2019 and did not receive
remuneration during their period of suspension.

12.2.13.2

For the purposes of this Part of this Schedule—

12.2.13.2.a

a relevant onward payment “relates” to paragraph  7 (1)(a) if the related
relevant compensation payment mentioned in paragraph  8 (1)(c) falls within
paragraph  7 (1)(a) (and references to payments relating to paragraph  7
(1)(b), (c), (d) or (e) are to be read accordingly);

12.2.13.2.b

references to a compensation scheme include references to any arrangements for
the making of payments of compensation.

12.3

In consequence of the amendment made by subsection (2)—

12.3.a

in section 102—

12.3.a.i

omit “and” after paragraph (b), and

12.3.a.ii

after that paragraph insert—

12.3.a.ii.ba

payments made under or otherwise referable to compensation schemes established
in connection with certain matters relating to Post Office Limited, and

;

12.3.b

before paragraph 1 of Schedule 15 (and the italic heading before it) insert—

  Part 1

  Income tax and other related relief

;

12.3.c

in each of the following provisions of Schedule 15, before “Schedule” insert
“Part of this” —

12.3.c.i

paragraph 1(1);

12.3.c.ii

paragraph 1(2);

12.3.c.iii

paragraph 2(6).”

###### Enterprise management incentives: time limits

13

13.1

Part 7 of Schedule 5 to ITEPA 2003 (enterprise management incentives:
notification of options) is amended as follows.

13.2

In paragraph 44(1) (time within which notice of options must be given to HMRC)
for “within 92 days after the date of the grant of the option” substitute  “on
or before 6 July following the end of the tax year in which the option was
granted” .

13.3

In paragraph 46(5) (time for giving of notices of enquiry)—

13.3.a

for “end of the period of 92 days” substitute  “date” ;

13.3.b

for “period within” substitute  “date by” .

13.4

The amendments made by this section have effect in relation to share options
(within the meaning of the EMI code (see paragraph 59 of Schedule 5 to ITEPA
2003)) granted on or after 6 April 2024.

#### Pensions

##### Provision in connection with abolition of the lifetime allowance charge

14

14.1

Schedule 9  contains amendments in consequence of, or otherwise in connection
with, the provision made by sections 18, 19 and 23 of F(No.2)A 2023 (which
relate to the abolition of the lifetime allowance charge).

14.2

In that Schedule—

14.2.a

Part  1  contains repeals of the provisions of Part 4 of FA 2004 (pension
schemes etc) that impose the lifetime allowance charge, and amendments
relating to those repeals;

14.2.b

Part  2  contains amendments of Part 4 of FA 2004, Part 9 of ITEPA 2003, and
subordinate legislation, relating to the taxation of lump sums paid by
registered pension schemes;

14.2.c

Part  3  contains amendments of Part 4 of FA 2004, Part 9 of ITEPA 2003, and
subordinate legislation, relating to the taxation of lump sums paid by certain
unregistered non-UK pension schemes and to the overseas transfer charge;

14.2.d

Part  4  contains amendments of provisions that confer transitional
protections in relation to the introduction of the lifetime allowance charge
or reductions in the amount of the lifetime allowance;

14.2.e

Part  5  contains amendments of Part 4 of FA 2004 and subordinate legislation
relating to the provision of information;

14.2.f

Part  6  contains provision about commencement and transitional matters, and
powers to make further provision.

14.3

The following provisions of F(No.2)A 2023 (which are superseded by the
amendments contained in Parts 1 and 2 of  Schedule 9 ) are repealed—

      section 18 (abolition of lifetime allowance charge);           section
19 (certain lump sums to be taxed at marginal rate).

14.4

The amendments contained in  Schedule 9  include repeals of provisions that
are spent or are no longer of practical utility.

##### MPs’ pension scheme etc: rectification of discrimination

15

15.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision about the treatment for the
purposes of income tax or capital gains tax of—

15.1.a

rectification payments, or tax redress payments, made to or in respect of a
member of a relevant pension scheme,

15.1.b

tax windfalls resulting from a rectification exercise, or

15.1.c

increases or decreases resulting from a rectification exercise in—

15.1.c.i

the rate of a scheme pension payable by a relevant pension scheme, or

15.1.c.ii

the value of any rights under a relevant pension scheme in respect of a
member.

15.2

“ Relevant pension scheme ” means—

15.2.a

an MPs’ pension scheme,

15.2.b

a Senedd pension scheme, or

15.2.c

an Assembly pension scheme.

15.3

“ Rectification payment ” means—

15.3.a

a payment of pension benefits that—

15.3.a.i

are payable as a result of a rectification exercise, and

15.3.a.ii

would have become payable at an earlier time if the rectification exercise had
been retrospective, or

15.3.b

a refund of pension contributions that is owed as a result of a rectification
exercise.

15.4

“ Tax redress payment ” means a payment made to or in respect of a member of a
relevant pension scheme where—

15.4.a

the member was subject to a rectification exercise, and

15.4.b

the payment represents compensation for an amount paid in respect of an income
tax liability for any tax year that would not have arisen if the rectification
exercise had been retrospective.

15.5

“ Tax windfall ”, in relation to a rectification exercise and a member of a
relevant pension scheme, means—

15.5.a

a liability of the member for the annual allowance charge that would have
arisen in the tax year 2023-24 or any earlier tax year, or

15.5.b

a liability of the member for the lifetime allowance charge that would have
arisen in the tax year 2022-23 or any earlier tax year,

if the rectification exercise had been retrospective.

15.6

“ Rectification exercise ” means an exercise, conducted by a relevant pension
scheme in accordance with the rules of the scheme, under which the benefits
payable to or in respect of a member in respect of the member’s remediable
service (or any part of the member’s remediable service)—

15.6.a

cease to be career average benefits and become instead final salary benefits,
or

15.6.b

cease to be final salary benefits and become instead career average benefits.

15.7

Regulations under this section may—

15.7.a

modify any enactment contained in the Income Tax Acts or relating to capital
gains tax;

15.7.b

impose a charge to income tax in relation to a tax windfall;

15.7.c

make different provision for different cases;

15.7.d

include consequential, incidental, supplemental, transitional, transitory or
saving provision.

15.8

Regulations under this section—

15.8.a

if made before 6 April 2025, may be made so as to have effect in relation to
the tax year 2024-25;

15.8.b

if made on or after 6 April 2025, may include provision that has effect in
relation to times before the regulations are made if that provision does not
increase any person’s liability to tax.

15.9

In this section—

      “ an Assembly pension scheme ” means a pension scheme made under section
48 of the Northern Ireland Act 1998;           “ lifetime allowance charge ”
means the charge to income tax under section 214 of FA 2004, as it had effect
before its repeal by this Act;           “ modify ” includes disapply or
supplement;           “ an MPs’ pension scheme ” means a pension scheme made
under paragraph 12(1) of Schedule 6 to the Constitutional Reform and
Governance Act 2010;           “ remediable service ” means service that is
pensionable service under a relevant pension scheme and—         in the case
of service that is pensionable service under an MPs’ pension scheme, takes
place in the period beginning with 8 May 2015 and ending with 31 March 2023;
in the case of service that is pensionable service under a Senedd pension
scheme or an Assembly pension scheme, takes place in the period beginning with
6 May 2016 and ending with 6 May 2021;                 “ scheme pension ” has
the same meaning as in Part 4 of FA 2004 (pensions etc);           “ a Senedd
pension scheme ” means a pension scheme made under section 20 of the
Government of Wales Act 2006.

#### Other income tax measures

##### Calculation of trade profits etc

###### Provision relating to the cash basis

16

Schedule 10  contains provision about the calculation of the profits of a
trade, profession or vocation on the cash basis, including provision—

16.a

for the cash basis to be the default basis of calculation for certain persons,

16.b

removing eligibility conditions relating to receipts,

16.c

removing restrictions on deductions for loan interest, and

16.d

removing restrictions on the availability of certain loss reliefs.

##### Other

###### PAYE regulations: special types of payer or payee

17

17.1

In Chapter 3 of Part 11 of ITEPA 2003 (pay as you earn: special types of payer
or payee), after section 688AA insert—

############ Workers’ providing services through intermediaries etc: cases where taxes already paid

17.1.688AB

17.1.688AB.1

PAYE regulations may make the following provision.

17.1.688AB.2

Provision for an amount to be treated as having been recovered from the payee,
and for that amount not to be recoverable from the payer (“the deemed
employer”), where—

17.1.688AB.2.a

the deemed employer would otherwise be liable to pay an amount under PAYE
regulations in consequence of being treated under section 61N(3) as having
made a deemed direct payment to a worker (other than by virtue of section
61WA), and

17.1.688AB.2.b

an amount of income tax or corporation tax has already been paid, or assessed,
in respect of income referable to that payment.

17.1.688AB.3

Provision for the amount referred to in the opening words of  subsection (2)
to be the best estimate which can reasonably be made by an officer of Revenue
and Customs (whether generally or specifically) of the amount referred to in
subsection (2) (b) .

17.1.688AB.4

Provision preventing a person specified in PAYE regulations from—

17.1.688AB.4.a

making a claim for the repayment of, or relief in respect of, an amount
referred to in  subsection (2) (b) , or

17.1.688AB.4.b

deducting, or setting off, the amount referred to in that subsection from, or
against, any tax liability of the person,

in a case where an estimate of that amount is treated as having been recovered
from the payee as a result of provision made by virtue of this section.

17.1.688AB.5

In this section, “ payee ” and “ payer ” have the same meaning as in section
684 (see subsection (7C) of that section).

17.2

PAYE Regulations made by virtue of  subsection (1)  may make provision in
relation to deemed direct payments made on or after 6 April 2017.

###### Carer’s allowance supplement: correction of statutory reference

18

18.1

In Table A in section 660 of ITEPA 2003 (taxable UK benefits), in the entry
for carer’s allowance supplement, for “Sections 24 and 28” substitute
“Section 81” .

18.2

The amendment made by  subsection (1)  is treated as having had effect from
the time when section 12 of FA 2019 (tax treatment of social security income)
came into force.

### Other taxes

#### Stamp duty and stamp duty reserve tax

##### Growth market exemption: qualifying UK multilateral trading facilities etc

19

19.1

Section 99A of FA 1986 (meaning of “recognised growth market” etc) is amended
as follows.

19.2

In subsection (5)—

19.2.a

in the words before paragraph (a), after “recognised stock exchange” insert
“or a qualifying UK multilateral trading facility” ;

19.2.b

in paragraph (a), for “£170 million” substitute  “£450 million” .

19.3

In subsection (6), at the end insert

;

      “ UK multilateral trading facility ” has the meaning given by Article
2.1.14A of  Regulation (EU) No.  600/2014  of the European Parliament and of
the Council of 15 May 2014 on markets in financial instruments as it forms
part of assimilated law.

19.4

After subsection (6) insert—

19.4.6A

For the purposes of subsection (5) a UK multilateral trading facility is
“qualifying” if—

19.4.6A.a

it is operated by an investment firm within the meaning given by article 3(1)
of The Financial Services and Markets Act 2000 (Regulated Activities) Order
2001 ( S.I. 2001/544 ), and

19.4.6A.b

the investment firm has permission under Part 4A of the Financial Services and
Markets Act 2000 to carry on the regulated activity (within the meaning of
that Act) of operating a multilateral trading facility.

19.5

The amendments made by this section are treated as having come into force on 1
January 2024.

##### Capital-raising arrangements etc

20

Schedule 11  makes provision for and in connection with ensuring that it
continues to be the case that—

20.a

no 1.5% charge to stamp duty or stamp duty reserve tax arises in relation to—

20.a.i

issues of securities or stock, or

20.a.ii

transfers of securities made in the course of capital-raising arrangements or
qualifying listing arrangements, and

20.b

no charge to stamp duty arises in relation to the issue of bearer instruments.

#### Electricity generator levy

##### New investment exemption

21

21.1

Part 5 of F(No.2)A 2023 (electricity generator levy) is amended as follows.

21.2

In section 280 (key concepts), in subsection (1), in the definition of “
relevant ” (as in relevant generating station)—

21.2.a

omit the “and” after paragraph (a), and

21.2.b

after paragraph (b) insert

, and

21.2.b.c

to the extent it is not comprised of qualifying new generating plant (see
section 311A );

.

21.3

After section 311 insert—

########### Meaning of “qualifying new generating plant”

21.3.311A

21.3.311A.1

Generating plant is “qualifying new generating plant” if it is new generating
plant commissioned as part of a qualifying project that meets the new
investment condition.

21.3.311A.2

The new investment condition is met in relation to a qualifying project if on
21 November 2023 it was reasonable to conclude, having regard to all of the
circumstances, that there is a significant likelihood of the project not
proceeding.

21.3.311A.3

The Treasury may by regulations provide for cases in which qualifying projects
are to be treated as meeting the new investment condition.

21.3.311A.4

“ Qualifying project ” means a project to commission—

21.3.311A.4.a

new generating plant for—

21.3.311A.4.a.i

a new generating station, or

21.3.311A.4.a.ii

an existing generating station which (as a result of the project) is to be
wholly or substantially comprised of new generating plant, or

21.3.311A.4.b

new generating plant that increases the generating capacity of an existing
generating station.

21.3.311A.5

Subsection  (6)  applies where new generating plant that increases the
generating capacity of an existing generating station replaces existing
generating plant.

21.3.311A.6

Only so much of the new generating plant as represents generating capacity in
excess of the capacity of the generating plant it replaces is to be regarded
as qualifying new generating plant.

21.4

In section 313 (definitions in this Part), in the table, at the appropriate
place insert—

    qualifying new generating plant section 311A

.

#### Pillar Two

##### Ensuring consistency of Parts 3 and 4 of F(No.2)A 2023 with OECD rules etc

22

Schedule 12  makes amendments to F(No.2)A 2023 in relation to multinational
top-up tax and in relation to domestic top-up tax.

##### Vehicle excise duty exemption for foreign vehicles

27

After section 5 of VERA 1994 (exempt vehicles) insert—

######### Additional power to exempt foreign vehicles

27.5A

27.5A.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations confer an exemption from vehicle
excise duty in respect of a foreign vehicle.

27.5A.2

The regulations may, for or in connection with conferring the exemption, amend
subordinate legislation made under this Act or the Motor Vehicles
(International Circulation) Act 1952.

27.5A.3

The regulations may provide that the exemption of a foreign vehicle from
vehicle excise duty is—

27.5A.3.a

subject to conditions;

27.5A.3.b

limited to a specified period.

27.5A.4

Regulations under this section may make—

27.5A.4.a

provision which applies generally or for particular purposes;

27.5A.4.b

retrospective provision.

27.5A.5

A provision of regulations under this section that has the effect of removing
the exemption of a foreign vehicle from vehicle excise duty must not be made
so as to have retrospective effect.

27.5A.6

In this section—

      “ foreign vehicle ” means a vehicle that is registered under the law of
any territory outside the United Kingdom;           “ specified ” means
specified in the regulations;           “ subordinate legislation ” means
Orders in Council, orders and regulations (including any regulations made
under an Order in Council).

##### Interpretation of VAT and excise law

28

28.1

This section  makes provision about how—

28.1.a

the European Union (Withdrawal) Act 2018 (“EUWA 2018”), and

28.1.b

the amendments made to that Act by the Retained EU Law (Revocation and Reform)
Act 2023 (“REULA 2023”),

are to apply for the purpose of interpreting enactments relating to value
added tax or any duty of excise ( “VAT and excise law” ).

28.2

Section 4 of EUWA 2018 (retained EU rights, powers, liabilities etc) continues
to have effect (despite the provision made by section 2 of REULA 2023) for the
purpose of interpreting VAT and excise law subject to the following exception.

28.3

The exception is that Articles 110 and 111 of the Treaty on the Functioning of
the European Union (which relate to internal taxation on products) have no
effect for that purpose.

28.4

Section 5(A1) to (A3) of EUWA 2018 (which are inserted by section 3 of REULA
2023 and which abolish the supremacy of EU law) have effect in relation to VAT
and excise law as they have effect in relation to other domestic enactments
but only so far as they relate to the disapplication or quashing of any
enactment as a result of EU law (and, accordingly, the superseded provisions
continue to have effect for the purpose of interpreting VAT and excise law).

28.5

Retained general principles of EU law—

28.5.a

continue to be relevant (despite the provision made by section 4 of REULA
2023) for the purpose of interpreting VAT and excise law in the same way, and
to the same extent, as they were relevant for that purpose before the coming
into force of that section, but

28.5.b

otherwise have effect for that purpose subject to the provision made by that
Act (including, in particular, the amendments made by section 6 of that Act
(role of courts)).

28.6

In  this section —

28.6.a

the reference to any duty of excise is to be read in accordance with section
49 of TCTA 2018,

28.6.b

the reference to the superseded provisions is a reference to section 5(1) to
(3) of EUWA 2018 as those subsections had effect immediately before the
passing of REULA 2023, and

28.6.c

the reference to retained general principles of EU law is to be read in
accordance with EUWA 2018 as that Act had effect immediately before the
passing of REULA 2023.

28.7

This section  needs to be read with sections 42 and 47 of TCTA 2018 (which
make other provision about EU law relating to VAT and excise law and which
continue to have effect for the purpose mentioned in  subsection (1)  above).

28.8

This section is treated as having come into force on 1 January 2024.

##### Promoters of tax avoidance: failure to comply with stop notice etc

34

34.1

In FA 2014, before section 278 (but after the italic heading) insert—

########### Offences relating to stop notices

34.1.277A

34.1.277A.1

A person who, without reasonable excuse, fails to comply with a duty imposed
under section 236B(1) is guilty of an offence.

34.1.277A.2

The recipient of a stop notice (“ R ”) is guilty of an offence if—

34.1.277A.2.a

R fails, without reasonable excuse, to comply with a duty imposed under
section 236B(3)(a), (4)(a) or (5)(a) to give a copy of the notice to another
person (“ P ”),

34.1.277A.2.b

P subsequently fails to comply with a duty imposed under section 236B(1) in
relation to the notice, and

34.1.277A.2.c

at the time of P’s failure the stop notice continues to have effect in
relation to R.

34.1.277A.3

For the purposes of this section—

34.1.277A.3.a

an insufficiency of funds is not a reasonable excuse unless attributable to
events outside the person's control,

34.1.277A.3.b

if the person relies on any other person to do anything, that is not a
reasonable excuse unless the first person took reasonable care to avoid the
failure,

34.1.277A.3.c

if the person had a reasonable excuse for the failure but the excuse has
ceased, the person is to be treated as having continued to have the excuse if
the failure is remedied without unreasonable delay after the excuse ceased,
and

34.1.277A.3.d

reliance on legal advice is to be taken automatically not to constitute a
reasonable excuse where the person is a monitored promoter if either—

34.1.277A.3.d.i

the advice was not based on a full and accurate description of the facts, or

34.1.277A.3.d.ii

the conclusions in the advice that the person relied on were unreasonable.

########### Liability for offences under 

34.1.277B

34.1.277B.1

If an offence under  section 277A  is committed by a body corporate or a
partnership and—

34.1.277B.1.a

is committed with the consent or connivance of a relevant person in relation
to the body or partnership, or

34.1.277B.1.b

is attributable to neglect on the part of such a person,

the person (as well as the body or partnership) commits the offence and is
liable to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

34.1.277B.2

A “relevant person” is—

34.1.277B.2.a

in relation to a body corporate other than one whose affairs are managed by
its members—

34.1.277B.2.a.i

a director, manager, secretary or other similar officer of the body, or a
person purporting to act in such a capacity, or

34.1.277B.2.a.ii

a shadow director within the meaning of section 251 of the Companies Act 2006;

34.1.277B.2.b

in relation to a limited liability partnership or other body corporate whose
affairs are managed by its members—

34.1.277B.2.b.i

a member who exercises functions of management with respect to it, or a person
purporting to act in such a capacity, or

34.1.277B.2.b.ii

in the case of a limited liability partnership, a shadow member within the
meaning of regulation 2 of the Limited Liability Partnerships Regulations 2001
( S.I. 2001/1090 );

34.1.277B.2.c

in relation to a partnership, a partner or a person purporting to act in such
a capacity.

34.2

In section 280(1) of FA 2014 (penalties for offences), after “section” insert
“ 277A ,” .

34.3

The offence under section  277A (1) of FA 2014 (as inserted by subsection (1))
applies in relation to a failure to comply that occurs on or after the date on
which this Act is passed.

34.4

The offence under section  277A (2) of FA 2014 (as inserted by subsection (1))
applies in relation to duties under section 236B(3)(a), (4)(a) or (5)(a)
arising on or after the date on which this Act is passed.

34.5

In section 236B(7) of FA 2014 (effect of stop notices), for “(5)(b)”
substitute  “(5)(a)” .

#### Administration

##### Additional information to be contained in returns under TMA 1970 etc

36

36.1

In section 8 of TMA 1970 (personal return), after subsection (1H) insert—

36.1.1I

Where a person is required to make and deliver a return under this section,
the person may be required by an officer of His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs
to include in the return any information that is specified or described in
regulations made by the Commissioners (whether or not the information is
relevant for the purpose mentioned in subsection (1)).

36.1.1J

The Commissioners may only specify or describe information in regulations
under  subsection (1I)  if the Commissioners consider that the information is
relevant for the purpose of the collection and management of any of the taxes
listed in section 1.

36.1.1K

A person who fails to comply with a requirement imposed on them by virtue of
subsection (1I)  is liable to a penalty of £60.

36.1.1L

Regulations under  subsection (1I)  may make different provision for different
purposes.

36.2

In section 8A of TMA 1970 (trustee’s return), after subsection (1F) insert—

36.2.1G

Where a person is required to make and deliver a return under this section,
the person may be required by an officer of His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs
to include in the return any information that is specified or described in
regulations made by the Commissioners (whether or not the information is
relevant for the purpose mentioned in subsection (1)).

36.2.1H

The Commissioners may only specify or describe information in regulations
under  subsection (1G)  if the Commissioners consider that the information is
relevant for the purpose of the collection and management of any of the taxes
listed in section 1.

36.2.1I

A person who fails to comply with a requirement imposed on them by virtue of
subsection (1G)  is liable to a penalty of £60.

36.2.1J

Regulations under  subsection (1G)  may make different provision for different
purposes.

36.3

In section 12AA of TMA 1970 (partnership return), after subsection (5E)
insert—

36.3.5F

Where a person is required to make and deliver a return under this section,
the person may be required by an officer of His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs

relevant for the purpose mentioned in subsection (1)).

under  subsection (5F)  if the Commissioners consider that the information is
relevant for the purpose of the collection and management of any of the taxes
listed in section 1.

36.3.5H

A person who fails to comply with a requirement imposed on them by virtue of
subsection (5F)  is liable to a penalty of £60.

36.3.5I

Regulations under  subsection (5F)  may make different provision for different
purposes.

36.4

In Chapter 6 of Part 11 of ITEPA 2003 (pay as you earn), before section 708
insert—

########### Provision of additional information to His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs

36.4.707A

36.4.707A.1

PAYE regulations may include provision requiring an employer to provide any
information that is specified or described in regulations made by the
Commissioners (whether or not that information is also relevant to the
assessment, charge, collection and recovery of income tax in respect of PAYE
income).

36.4.707A.2

The Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs may only specify or
describe information in regulations under  subsection (1)  if the
Commissioners consider that the information is relevant for the purpose of the
collection and management of any of the taxes listed in section 1 of TMA 1970.

36.5

The amendments made by this section have effect for the tax year 2025-26 and
subsequent tax years.

##### Commencement of rules imposing penalties for failure to make returns etc

37

37.1

Regulations made by the Treasury under any of the powers in sections 116, 117
or 118 of FA 2021 may provide for any provision of Schedules 24 to 27 to that
Act (penalties for failure to make returns etc or pay tax) to come into force
for the purposes of failures by eligible volunteers.

37.2

An eligible volunteer is an individual in respect of whom an election has
effect under the regulations.

37.3

The regulations may in particular—

37.3.a

provide for an election to take effect only if accepted by an officer of
Revenue and Customs;

37.3.b

provide that an election may not be revoked by the individual;

37.3.c

provide that an election ceases to have effect upon an officer of Revenue and
Customs giving notice to the individual;

37.3.d

make provision about the consequences of an election ceasing to have effect.

37.4

The provision that may be made by virtue of  subsection (3) (d)  includes
provision for an election that ceases to have effect to be treated as never
having had effect, other than for the purposes of any failure in respect of
which His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs have already assessed a penalty.

#### Final

    BGDA 1981 Betting and Gaming Duties Act 1981 CAA 2001 Capital Allowances

Act of that year F(No.2)A followed by a year Finance (No.2) Act of that year
HODA 1979 Hydrocarbon Oil Duties Act 1979 ICTA Income and Corporation Taxes
Act 1988 ITA 2007 Income Tax Act 2007 ITEPA 2003 Income Tax (Earnings and

TCGA 1992 Taxation of Chargeable Gains Act 1992 TCTA 2018 Taxation (Cross-

Products Duty Act 1979 VERA 1994 Vehicle Excise and Registration Act 1994

This Act may be cited as the Finance Act 2024.

## Schedules

Research and development

Section  2

##### Main amendments of CTA 2009

1

CTA 2009 is amended as follows.

2

In Part 3, omit Chapter 6A (R&D expenditure credit).

3

In the heading of Part 13, omit “Additional relief for”.

4

4.1

Chapter 1 of Part 13 is amended as follows.

4.2

For section 1039 (overview of Part) substitute—

########### Overview of Part

4.2.1039

4.2.1039.1

This Part provides relief for companies that invest in research and
development.

4.2.1039.2

Chapter  1A  makes relief available in the form of a credit in respect of
expenditure on research and development, which becomes payable in certain
circumstances.

4.2.1039.3

Chapter 2 makes alternative relief available, in the form of—

4.2.1039.3.a

an additional deduction in calculating trading profits, and

4.2.1039.3.b

a payable credit,

to small or medium-sized enterprises that invest heavily in research and
development and do not make associated trading profits.

4.2.1039.4

Chapter 8 limits the reliefs provided by Chapters  1A  and 2.

4.2.1039.5

Chapter 9 contains definitions and other supplementary provision.

4.3

For section 1040 (relief to be available under more than one Chapter of Part
13) substitute—

########### No overlapping claims under Chapters 

4.3.1040

A company is not entitled to relief under Chapter 2 in respect of expenditure
if it is entitled to, and claims, relief under Chapter  1A  in respect of that
expenditure.

4.4

Omit section 1040A (which refers to the existing R&D expenditure credit).

5

After Chapter 1 of Part 13 insert—

######### R&D expenditure credit

########## Introductory

########### Overview of Chapter

5.1042A

5.1042A.1

This Chapter provides an entitlement to a credit (called an “R&D expenditure
credit”) in respect of certain expenditure on research and development.

5.1042A.2

Section  1042B  and  1042C  make the basic provision setting out what the
entitlement is and how it is to be realised.

5.1042A.3

Sections  1042D  to  1042F  describe the expenditure by reference to which the
entitlement arises.

5.1042A.4

Section  1042G  sets the percentage of that expenditure that is translated
into the credit.

5.1042A.5

Sections  1042H  to  1042N  make provision about what happens when a company
obtains the credit (in particular, about how the credit is to be accounted for
and applied or paid).

5.1042A.6

Section  1042O  makes provision about how the expenditure credit operates in
the context of a basic life assurance and general annuity business carried on
by an insurance company.

5.1042A.7

This Chapter has to be read with Chapter 8, which limits the entitlement given
by this Chapter in various respects.

########## Entitlement and claims

########### Entitlement to credit

5.1042B

5.1042B.1

A company is entitled to an R&D expenditure credit for an accounting period if
it meets conditions A, B and C in this section.

5.1042B.2

Condition A is that the company carries on a trade in the period.

5.1042B.3

Condition B is that the company incurs expenditure that is both—

5.1042B.3.a

allowable as a deduction in calculating for corporation tax purposes the
profits of the trade for the period, and

5.1042B.3.b

qualifying Chapter  1A  expenditure by virtue of section  1042D ,  1042E  or
1042F .

5.1042B.4

Condition C is that the company is not an ineligible company (see section
1142).

5.1042B.5

The amount of the credit is the relevant percentage (see section  1042G ) of
the expenditure that satisfies condition B.

########### Claiming the credit

5.1042C

5.1042C.1

To obtain an R&D expenditure credit the company must make a claim (see Part 9A
of Schedule 18 to the FA 1998).

5.1042C.2

A company may not make the claim (“the RDEC claim”) after the end of the claim
notification period unless—

5.1042C.2.a

the company has made an R&D claim during the period of three years ending with
the last day of the claim notification period,

5.1042C.2.b

the company makes a claim notification in respect of the RDEC claim within the
claim notification period, or

5.1042C.2.c

the accounting period in respect of which the RDEC claim is made falls within
the same period of account as another accounting period in respect of which
the company has made an R&D claim or a claim notification.

5.1042C.3

For the purposes of subsection  (2) (a) , ignore any R&D claim for an
accounting period beginning before 1 April 2023 that is included in the
company’s company tax return only by virtue of an amendment made on or after
that date (see paragraph 83B(2) of Schedule 18 to FA 1998).

########## Qualifying expenditure

########### Qualifying expenditure: in-house R&D

5.1042D

5.1042D.1

Expenditure of a company is qualifying Chapter  1A  expenditure if it meets
each of conditions A to D in this section.

5.1042D.2

Condition A is that the expenditure is attributable to relevant research and
development undertaken by the company itself.

5.1042D.3

Condition B is that the expenditure is—

5.1042D.3.a

incurred on staffing costs (see section 1123),

5.1042D.3.b

incurred on software, data licences, cloud computing services or consumable
items (see section 1125),

5.1042D.3.c

qualifying expenditure on externally provided workers (see section 1127), or

5.1042D.3.d

incurred on relevant payments to the subjects of a clinical trial (see section
1140).

5.1042D.4

Condition C is that the research and development is not contracted out to the
company (see section  1133 ).

5.1042D.5

Condition D is that the expenditure is not attributable to an exempt foreign
permanent establishment (see section  1138B ).

5.1042D.6

See sections 1124, 1126 to 1126B and 1132 for provision about when expenditure
within subsection  (3) (a) ,  (b)  or  (c)  is attributable to relevant
research and development.

########### Qualifying expenditure: payments for contracted out R&D

5.1042E

5.1042E.1

Expenditure of a company is qualifying Chapter  1A  expenditure if it meets
each of conditions A to D in this section.

5.1042E.2

Condition A is that the expenditure is attributable to relevant research and
development contracted out by the company (see section  1133 ).

5.1042E.3

Condition B is that the research and development is not also contracted out to
the company (see section  1133 ).

5.1042E.4

Condition C is that the expenditure is incurred in making the qualifying
element of a contractor payment (see sections 1133 to 1136).

5.1042E.5

Condition D is that the expenditure is not attributable to an exempt foreign
permanent establishment (see section  1138B ).

5.1042E.6

See sections 1124, 1126 to 1126B and 1132 for provision about when particular
kinds of expenditure are attributable to relevant research and development.

########### Qualifying expenditure: activity as contractor for irrelievable client

5.1042F

5.1042F.1

Expenditure of a company is qualifying Chapter  1A  expenditure if it meets
conditions A, B and C in this section.

5.1042F.2

Condition A is that the expenditure is attributable to relevant research and
development contracted out to the company (see section  1133 ).

5.1042F.3

Condition B is that subsection  (4)  is satisfied by each person by whom the
research and development is contracted out to the company.

5.1042F.4

A person satisfies this subsection if—

5.1042F.4.a

the person is an ineligible company (see section 1142), or

5.1042F.4.b

the person is not, in relation to the contracting out of the research and
development by that person, acting in the course of a trade, profession or
vocation within the charge to tax.

5.1042F.5

Condition C is that the expenditure would, but for the fact that the research
and development is contracted out to the company, be qualifying Chapter  1A
expenditure by virtue of section  1042D  or  1042E .

########## Rate of credit

########### Percentage of qualifying expenditure translated into credit

5.1042G

5.1042G.1

The relevant percentage for the purposes of section  1042B (5)  is—

5.1042G.1.a

49%, in the case of a ring fence trade within the meaning given by section 277
of CTA 2010, or

5.1042G.1.b

20%, in any other case.

5.1042G.2

The Treasury may by regulations replace the percentage for the time being
specified in subsection  (1) (a)  or  (b)  with a different percentage.

########## Treatment of credit: main provisions

########### Expenditure credit to count as taxable receipt

5.1042H

If a company is entitled to, and claims, an R&D expenditure credit for an
accounting period, it must bring the amount of the credit into account as a
receipt in calculating for corporation tax purposes the profits for the period
of the trade concerned.

########### Redemption of value of expenditure credit

5.1042I

If a company is entitled to, and claims, an R&D expenditure credit for an
accounting period, the credit is to be dealt with as follows.

Step 1 The amount of the credit is to be applied in discharging any liability
of the company to pay corporation tax for the accounting period. Step 2 If
there is a notional tax deduction (see section  1042K ), it is to be applied
to any amount remaining after step 1. Step 3 If the amount remaining after
step 2 exceeds the cap by reference to the company’s PAYE and NIC liabilities
for the accounting period (see section  1112B ), the excess is to be deducted.
Step 4 Any amount remaining after step 3 is to be applied in discharging any
liability of the company to pay corporation tax for any other accounting
period. Step 5 If the company is a member of a group, it may surrender the
whole or part of any amount remaining after step 4 to any other member of the
group (as to which see section  1042N ). Step 6 Any amount remaining after
step 5 is to be applied in discharging any other liability of the company to
pay a sum to the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs— under or
by virtue of an enactment, or under an agreement made in connection with any
person’s liability to make a payment to the Commissioners under or by virtue
of an enactment. Step 7 Any amount remaining after step 6 is (subject to
sections  1112F  and  1112H ) to be paid to the company by an officer of
Revenue and Customs.

########### Treatment of deduction to comply with PAYE and NIC limit

5.1042J

5.1042J.1

This section applies if an amount is deducted under step 3 in section  1042I .

5.1042J.2

The amount is to be added to the amount of R&D expenditure credit to which the
company is entitled for its next accounting period (including where that
amount would otherwise be nil).

########## Notional tax deduction

########### Amount of notional tax deduction

5.1042K

5.1042K.1

This section determines the amount of the notional tax deduction for the
purposes of step 2 in section  1042I .

5.1042K.2

The amount of the deduction is the amount (if any) by which the amount
remaining after step 1 in section  1042I  exceeds the amount produced by
deducting the notional tax charge from the initial amount of the expenditure
credit (that is, its amount before the application of that step).

5.1042K.3

Subsections  (4)  and  (5)  apply if the trade concerned is not a ring fence
trade.

5.1042K.4

The notional tax charge is the amount of corporation tax that would be
chargeable on the initial amount of the expenditure credit if it were an
amount of profits for the accounting period on which corporation tax was
chargeable at the applicable rate.

5.1042K.5

The applicable rate is—

5.1042K.5.a

the main rate, if the company has profits for the accounting period that—

5.1042K.5.a.i

are chargeable to corporation tax at the main rate, and

5.1042K.5.a.ii

would be so even if they did not include any amount brought into account under
section  1042H ;

5.1042K.5.b

in any other case, the standard small profits rate.

5.1042K.6

Subsections  (7)  and  (8)  apply if the trade concerned is a ring fence
trade.

5.1042K.7

The notional tax charge is the sum of—

5.1042K.7.a

the amount of corporation tax that would be chargeable on the initial amount
of the expenditure credit if it were an amount of ring fence profits for the
accounting period on which corporation tax was chargeable at the applicable
rate, and

5.1042K.7.b

the amount of the supplementary charge that would be chargeable on the initial
amount of the expenditure credit if it were an amount of adjusted ring fence
profits for the accounting period (see Chapters 6 to 9 of Part 8 of CTA 2010).

5.1042K.8

The applicable rate is—

5.1042K.8.a

the main ring fence profits rate, if the company has profits for the
accounting period that—

5.1042K.8.a.i

are chargeable to corporation tax at the main ring fence profits rate, and

5.1042K.8.a.ii

would be so even if they did not include any amount brought into account under
section  1042H ;

5.1042K.8.b

in any other case, the small ring fence profits rate.

5.1042K.9

For the purposes of this section, the initial amount of an expenditure credit
is to be treated as excluding any amount added under section  1042J .

5.1042K.10

In this section—

“ adjusted ring fence profits ” has the meaning given by section 330(2) of CTA
2010; “ main rate ” means the rate referred to in section 3(1) of CTA 2010; “
main ring fence profits rate ” means the rate referred to in section 279A(1)
of CTA 2010; “ ring fence profits ” has the meaning given by section 276 of
CTA 2010; “ ring fence trade ” has the meaning given by section 277 of CTA
2010; “ small ring fence profits rate ” means the rate referred to in section
279A(3) of CTA 2010; “ standard small profits rate ” means the rate referred
to in section 18A(1) of CTA 2010.

########### Treatment of notional tax deduction

5.1042L

5.1042L.1

This section applies if an amount is deducted under step 2 in section  1042I .

5.1042L.2

If the company is a member of a group, it may, in respect of the accounting
period in which the expenditure credit arises, surrender the whole or part of
the deducted amount to any other member of the group (as to which see section
1042N ).

5.1042L.3

To the extent that the deducted amount is not surrendered under subsection
(2) , it is to be applied in discharging any liability of the company to pay
corporation tax for any subsequent accounting period.

########### Priority of discharge

5.1042M

5.1042M.1

An amount within subsection  (2)  is to be applied as described in that
subsection before any amount within subsection  (3)  is applied as described
in that subsection.

5.1042M.2

An amount is within this subsection if it is to be applied under—

5.1042M.2.a

section  1042L (3) , or

5.1042M.2.b

section  1042N (3)  as it applies in relation to an amount surrendered under
section  1042L (2) ,

in discharging the liability of a company to pay corporation tax for an
accounting period.

5.1042M.3

An amount is within this subsection if it is to be (or would but for
subsection  (1)  be) applied under—

5.1042M.3.a

step 4 in section  1042I , or

5.1042M.3.b

section  1042N (3)  as it applies in relation to an amount surrendered under
step 5 in section  1042I ,

in discharging the same liability as an amount within subsection  (2) .

########## Intra-group surrenders

########### Amounts surrendered to other group companies

5.1042N

5.1042N.1

Subsection  (3)  applies if an amount of expenditure credit is surrendered by
the qualifying company to another member of its group under step 5 in section
1042I  or under section  1042L (2) .

5.1042N.2

For the purposes of that subsection—

5.1042N.2.a

the accounting period in respect of which the surrender is made is “the
surrender AP”;

5.1042N.2.b

an accounting period of the other group member is an “overlapping AP” if it
overlaps with the surrender AP to any extent.

5.1042N.3

The surrendered amount is to be dealt with as follows.

Step 1 Select an overlapping AP. Step 2 Calculate the proportion of the
overlapping AP that overlaps with the surrender AP, and apply that proportion
to the amount of corporation tax payable by the other group member for that
overlapping AP. Step 3 Calculate the proportion of the surrender AP that
overlaps with the overlapping AP, and apply that proportion to the surrendered
amount. Step 4 The amount given by step 3 is to be applied in discharging the
liability of the other group member to pay the corporation tax mentioned in
step 2, up to the amount given by that step. Step 5 Select another overlapping
AP, if there is one, and repeat steps 2 to 4. Step 6 If any of the surrendered
amount remains after steps 2 to 4 have been taken in relation to each
overlapping AP, the remainder is to be treated for the purposes of section
1042I  or (as the case may be) section  1042L (2)  as if it had not been
surrendered as mentioned in subsection  (1) .

5.1042N.4

A surrender to which subsection  (3)  applies is not to be—

5.1042N.4.a

taken into account in determining, for corporation tax purposes, the profits
or losses of the qualifying company or the other group member, or

5.1042N.4.b

regarded for corporation tax purposes as the making of a distribution.

########## Basic life assurance and general annuity businesses

########### Adaptation of entitlement for certain insurance businesses

5.1042O

5.1042O.1

This section applies if—

5.1042O.1.a

for an accounting period, an insurance company is charged to tax in respect of
its basic life assurance and general annuity business in accordance with the
I-E rules, and

5.1042O.1.b

the calculation of the company’s charge to tax for the period in respect of
that business does not involve the calculation of any BLAGAB trade profit or
loss of the company.

5.1042O.2

The reference in section  1042B (3) (a)  to expenditure that is allowable as a
deduction in calculating the profits of the trade for an accounting period is
to be read as a reference to expenditure that would be so allowable if the
company were to calculate its BLAGAB trade profit or loss for the period.

5.1042O.3

The reference in section  1042H  to calculating the profits of the trade is to
be read as a reference to calculating the I-E profit of the basic life
assurance and general annuity business carried on by the company.

5.1042O.4

Any receipt to be brought into account by virtue of this section is to be
treated for the purposes of section 92 of FA 2012 (certain BLAGAB trading
receipts to count as deemed I-E receipts) as if it had been taken into account
in calculating the company’s BLAGAB trade profit or loss for the period.

5.1042O.5

In this section, “BLAGAB trade profit” and “BLAGAB trade loss” have the
meanings given by section 136 of FA 2012.

6

6.1

Chapter 2 of Part 13 (relief for SMEs on the cost of R&D) is amended as
follows.

6.2

For the heading substitute  “Relief for loss-making, R&D-intensive SMEs” .

6.3

For section 1043 (overview of Chapter) substitute—

########### Overview of Chapter

6.3.1043

6.3.1043.1

This Chapter provides relief for companies that are small or medium-sized
enterprises, invest heavily in research and development, and do not make
associated trading profits.

6.3.1043.2

Section 1044 provides relief in the form of an additional deduction where the
investment is made in the course of a loss-making trade.

6.3.1043.3

Section 1045 provides relief in the form of a deemed trading loss where the
investment is made the course of activities that do not yet amount to the
carrying on of a trade.

6.3.1043.4

Section  1045ZA  specifies the intensity of spending on research and
development needed for a company to qualify for relief under section 1044 or
1045.

6.3.1043.5

Sections 1047 and 1048 make provision about the procedure for claiming, and
the effect of, relief under section 1045.

6.3.1043.6

Section 1049 restricts consortium relief where relief under section 1044 or
1045 is claimed.

6.3.1043.7

Sections 1051 to 1053 describe the expenditure by reference to which the
entitlement to relief under section 1044 or 1045 arises.

6.3.1043.8

Sections 1054 to 1062 provide further relief in the form of a payable credit
(called an “R&D tax credit”) in respect of trading losses increased or
generated by relief under section 1044 or 1045.

6.3.1043.9

Section  1062A  excludes certain insurance companies.

6.3.1043.10

This Chapter has to be read with Chapter 8, which limits the entitlements
given by this Chapter in various respects.

6.4

6.4.a

after subsection (2) insert—

Condition B is that the company—

6.4.b.2A.a

meets the R&D intensity condition in the period, or

6.4.b.2A.b

obtained relief under this Chapter for its most recent prior accounting period
of 12 months’ duration, having met the R&D intensity condition in that period.

;

6.4.c

after subsection (5) insert—

6.4.c.5A

Condition E is that the company makes a loss in the trade in the period.

6.4.c.5B

Condition F is that the company is not an ineligible company (see section
1142).

;

6.4.d

in subsection (6)—

at the end of the first sentence insert  “(see Part 9A of Schedule 18 to the

omit the second sentence;

The deduction is, in particular, additional to any given under section 87.

omit subsection (9).

6.5.a

in subsection (1), for “conditions A and C” substitute  “each of conditions A

after subsection (2) insert—

6.6

After section 1045 insert—

########### R&D intensity condition

6.6.1045ZA

6.6.1045ZA.1

This section determines whether a company meets the R&D intensity condition in
an accounting period for the purposes of sections 1044 and 1045.

6.6.1045ZA.2

If the company is not connected with another company, the company meets the
condition if its relevant R&D expenditure for the period amounts to at least
30% of its total relevant expenditure for the period.

6.6.1045ZA.3

If the company is connected with at least one other company, the company meets
the condition if the connected companies’ relevant R&D expenditure for the
period amounts to at least 30% of the connected companies’ total relevant
expenditure for the period.

6.6.1045ZA.4

In subsection  (3) , “ the connected companies ” refers to the company to
which this section is being applied and each company with which it is
connected; and the references to their expenditure are to the aggregate of
each of their expenditures.

6.6.1045ZA.5

Expenditure forms part of a company’s total relevant expenditure for an
accounting period if—

6.6.1045ZA.5.a

in accordance with generally accepted accounting practice, it is brought into
account in calculating the profits for the period of any trade carried on by
the company,

6.6.1045ZA.5.b

it is expenditure in respect of which the company is, for the period, entitled
to relief under section 1045, or

6.6.1045ZA.5.c

in reliance on section 1308(2) (expenditure brought into account in
determining value of intangible asset allowable as a deduction), it is brought
into account in calculating the company’s profits for the period for
corporation tax purposes.

6.6.1045ZA.6

But—

6.6.1045ZA.6.a

expenditure of a company is to be ignored for the purposes of subsection  (5)
if it consists of a payment, or other transfer of value, to another company
with which the company is connected, and

6.6.1045ZA.6.b

where expenditure forms part of a company's total relevant expenditure by
virtue of subsection  (5) (c) , a deduction brought into account as mentioned
in subsection  (5) (a)  is to be ignored for the purposes of that provision to
the extent that a corresponding deduction for corporation tax purposes is
prevented by section 1308(5).

6.6.1045ZA.7

Expenditure forms part of a company’s relevant R&D expenditure for an
accounting period if—

6.6.1045ZA.7.a

it forms part of the company’s total relevant expenditure for the period, or
would do but for subsection  (6) (a) , and

6.6.1045ZA.7.b

it is expenditure in respect of which the company would, assuming that it met
the R&D intensity condition, be entitled to relief under this Chapter for the
period.

6.6.1045ZA.8

For the purposes of this section in its application to an accounting period, a
company is to be treated as connected with another company if it is connected
with that company on any day within the period.

6.7

Omit section 1046 (relief only available to going concerns).

6.8

In section 1051 (meaning of “ qualifying Chapter 2 expenditure ”), for the
words from “means” to the end substitute  “is such of its expenditure as is
qualifying Chapter 2 expenditure by virtue of section  1052 ,  1053  or  1053A
.”

6.9

For sections 1052 and 1053 (categories of qualifying Chapter 2 expenditure)
substitute—

########### Qualifying expenditure: in-house R&D

6.9.1052

6.9.1052.1

Expenditure of a company is qualifying Chapter 2 expenditure if it meets each
of conditions A to D in this section.

6.9.1052.2

Condition A is that the expenditure is attributable to relevant research and
development undertaken by the company itself.

6.9.1052.3

Condition B is that the expenditure is—

6.9.1052.3.a

incurred on staffing costs (see section 1123),

6.9.1052.3.b

incurred on software, data licences, cloud computing services or consumable
items (see section 1125),

6.9.1052.3.c

qualifying expenditure on externally provided workers (see section 1127), or

6.9.1052.3.d

incurred on relevant payments to the subjects of a clinical trial (see section
1140).

6.9.1052.4

Condition C is that the research and development is not contracted out to the
company (see section  1133 ).

6.9.1052.5

Condition D is that the expenditure is not attributable to an exempt foreign
permanent establishment (see section  1138B ).

6.9.1052.6

See sections 1124, 1126 to 1126B and 1132 for provision about when expenditure
within subsection  (3) (a) ,  (b)  or  (c)  is attributable to relevant
research and development.

########### Qualifying expenditure: payments for contracted out R&D

6.9.1053

6.9.1053.1

Expenditure of a company is qualifying Chapter 2 expenditure if it meets each
of conditions A to D in this section.

6.9.1053.2

Condition A is that the expenditure is attributable to relevant research and
development contracted out by the company (see section  1133 ).

6.9.1053.3

Condition B is that the research and development is not also contracted out to
the company (see section  1133 ).

6.9.1053.4

Condition C is that the expenditure is incurred in making the qualifying
element of a contractor payment (see sections 1133 to 1136).

6.9.1053.5

Condition D is that the expenditure is not attributable to an exempt foreign
permanent establishment (see section  1138B ).

6.9.1053.6

See sections 1124, 1126 to 1126B and 1132 for provision about when particular
kinds of expenditure are attributable to relevant research and development.

########### Qualifying expenditure: activity as contractor for irrelievable client

6.9.1053A

6.9.1053A.1

Expenditure of a company is qualifying Chapter 2 expenditure if it meets
conditions A, B and C in this section.

6.9.1053A.2

Condition A is that the expenditure is attributable to relevant research and
development contracted out to the company (see section  1133 ).

6.9.1053A.3

Condition B is that subsection  (4)  is satisfied by each person by whom the
research and development is contracted out to the company.

6.9.1053A.4

A person satisfies this subsection if—

6.9.1053A.4.a

the person is an ineligible company (see section 1142), or

6.9.1053A.4.b

the person is not, in relation to the contracting out of the research and
development by that person, acting in the course of a trade, profession or
vocation within the charge to tax.

6.9.1053A.5

Condition C is that the expenditure would, but for the fact that the research
and development is contracted out to the company, be qualifying Chapter 2
expenditure by virtue of section  1052  or  1053 .

########### Insurance company to be treated as large company

6.15.1062A

An insurance company that carries on life assurance business in an accounting
period is not to be treated for the purposes of this Chapter as a small or
medium-sized enterprise in relation to that period.
