For Chapter 8 of Part 13 (cap on aid for R&D) substitute—

######### Restrictions on relief under this Part

########## Introductory

########### Overview of Chapter

8.1112A

8.1112A.1

This Chapter limits the entitlements given by Chapters  1A  and 2.

8.1112A.2

Sections  1112B  to  1112E  provide for the amount of R&D expenditure credit
or R&D tax credit payable to a company to be capped by reference to certain
liabilities of the company in connection with PAYE and national insurance,
except in certain cases.

8.1112A.3

Sections  1112F  and  1112G  provide that payment of an R&D expenditure
credit, and relief under Chapter 2, are available only to companies that are
going concerns.

8.1112A.4

Section  1112H  provides that an R&D expenditure credit or R&D tax credit does
not have to be paid if a tax enquiry into the company is open or the company
has outstanding PAYE or national insurance liabilities.

8.1112A.5

Section  1112I  provides for transactions aimed at obtaining or increasing an
entitlement under Chapter  1A  or 2 not to succeed in doing so.

8.1112A.6

Section  1112J  allows the Treasury to place additional limits on the amount
of relief available under Chapter 2.

########## PAYE and NIC liabilities

########### Cap by reference to PAYE and NIC liabilities

8.1112B

8.1112B.1

This section determines, for the purposes of sections  1042I  and 1058(1), the
amount of the cap by reference to a company’s PAYE and NIC liabilities for an
accounting period.

But see section  1112E  (which provides for there to be no cap in certain
cases).

8.1112B.2

The amount of the cap is the sum of—

8.1112B.2.a

£20,000, and

8.1112B.2.b

the amount produced by multiplying by three (“the multiplier”) the amount of
the company’s relevant PAYE and NIC liabilities for payment periods ending in
the accounting period (see section  1112C ).

8.1112B.3

If the accounting period is less than 12 months, the amount specified in
subsection  (2) (a)  is to be proportionately reduced.

8.1112B.4

If the company claims relief under both Chapters  1A  and 2 for the period,
the amount of the cap for the purposes of section  1042I  is to be reduced by
the amount of any R&D tax credit obtained by the company under Chapter 2.

8.1112B.5

The Treasury may by regulations—

8.1112B.5.a

replace the amount for the time being specified in subsection  (2) (a)  with a
different amount;

8.1112B.5.b

replace the multiplier for the time being specified in subsection  (2) (b)
with a different multiplier.

########### Calculation of relevant PAYE and NIC liabilities

8.1112C

8.1112C.1

This section determines the amount of a company’s relevant PAYE and NIC
liabilities for a payment period for the purposes of section  1112B .

8.1112C.2

The amount is to be calculated as follows.

Step 1 Take the total amount of the company’s PAYE and NIC liabilities for the
payment period (see section  1112D ). Step 2 Add any amount produced by the
application of subsection  (4)  or  (6)  to the company as company A. Step 3
Deduct any amount produced by the application of subsection  (4)  or  (6)  to
the company as company B.

8.1112C.3

An amount is produced by subsection  (4)  where—

8.1112C.3.a

two companies (“ company A ” and “ company B ”) are connected,

8.1112C.3.b

company A incurs expenditure in the payment period on externally provided
workers (see sections 1127 and 1128), and

8.1112C.3.c

company B incurs staffing costs in the payment period in providing any of
those workers for company A.

8.1112C.4

The amount produced is the sum of the amounts given, in relation to each
worker in respect of whom subsection  (3) (c)  is satisfied, by—

X × Y Z where— X is the amount of expenditure that— has been incurred on
staffing costs by company B in providing the worker for company A, and forms
part of the total amount of company B’s PAYE and NIC liabilities for the
payment period (see section  1112D ), Y is the amount of company A’s
expenditure on the externally provided worker that has been taken into account
in calculating the amount of company A’s qualifying expenditure for the
payment period, and Z is the total amount of company A’s qualifying
expenditure on the externally provided worker (see section 1127) for the
payment period.

8.1112C.5

Subsection  (6)  produces an amount where—

8.1112C.5.a

two companies (“ company A ” and “ company B ”) are connected,

8.1112C.5.b

company A incurs qualifying contractor expenditure in the payment period, and

8.1112C.5.c

company B incurs staffing costs in the payment period in undertaking on behalf
of company A any of the research and development to which that expenditure is
attributable.

8.1112C.6

That amount is such amount of those staffing costs as forms part of the total
amount of company B’s PAYE and NIC liabilities for the payment period (see
section  1112D ).

8.1112C.7

In this section as it applies for the purposes of section  1042I —

“ qualifying expenditure ” (except in the expression “ qualifying expenditure
on the externally provided worker ”) means expenditure that is qualifying
Chapter  1A  expenditure by virtue of section  1042D ,  1042E  or  1042F ; “
qualifying contractor expenditure ” means expenditure that is qualifying
Chapter  1A  expenditure by virtue of— section  1042E , or section  1042F  as
it applies by reference to section  1042E .

8.1112C.8

In this section as it applies for the purposes of section 1058(1)—

“ qualifying expenditure ” (except in the expression “ qualifying expenditure
on the externally provided worker ”) means qualifying Chapter 2 expenditure
(see section 1051); “ qualifying contractor expenditure ” means qualifying
expenditure that is qualifying Chapter 2 expenditure by virtue of— section
1053 , or section  1053A  as it applies by reference to section  1053 .

########### Total PAYE and NIC liabilities

8.1112D

8.1112D.1

For the purposes of section  1112C , the total amount of a company’s PAYE and
NIC liabilities for a payment period is the sum of amount A and amount B.

8.1112D.2

Amount A is the total amount of income tax for which the company is required
to account to an officer of Revenue and Customs under PAYE regulations for the
period.

8.1112D.3

In calculating amount A, any deduction the company is authorised to make in
respect of child tax credit or working tax credit is to be disregarded.

8.1112D.4

Amount B is the total amount of Class 1 national insurance contributions for
which the company is required to account to an officer of Revenue and Customs
for the accounting period.

8.1112D.5

In calculating amount B, any deduction the company is authorised to make in
respect of any of the following is to be disregarded—

8.1112D.5.a

statutory maternity pay,

8.1112D.5.b

statutory adoption pay,

8.1112D.5.c

statutory paternity pay,

8.1112D.5.d

statutory shared parental pay,

8.1112D.5.e

statutory parental bereavement pay;

8.1112D.5.f

child tax credit, or

8.1112D.5.g

working tax credit.

8.1112D.6

Subsection  (7)  applies if—

8.1112D.6.a

in determining under section  1112C  the amount of a company’s relevant PAYE
and NIC liabilities for a payment period, it is necessary to determine the
total amount of another company’s PAYE and NIC liabilities for that period,
and

8.1112D.6.b

that period falls within, but is shorter than, a payment period of that other
company.

8.1112D.7

The amount produced by subsection  (1)  in its application to that other
company is to be proportionately reduced.

########### Exception for companies creating or managing intellectual property

8.1112E

8.1112E.1

There is no cap by reference to a company’s PAYE and NIC liabilities for an
accounting period if the company meets conditions A and B.

8.1112E.2

A company meets condition A for an accounting period if, during the period,
the company is engaged in—

8.1112E.2.a

taking, or preparing to take, steps in order that relevant intellectual
property will be created by it,

8.1112E.2.b

creating relevant intellectual property, or

8.1112E.2.c

performing a significant amount of management activity in relation to relevant
intellectual property it holds.

8.1112E.3

For the purposes of subsection  (2) —

8.1112E.3.a

a company is only engaged in an activity mentioned in paragraph  (a) ,  (b)
or  (c)  of subsection  (2)  if the activity is wholly or mainly undertaken by
employees of the company;

8.1112E.3.b

intellectual property is “relevant” intellectual property in relation to a
company if the whole or the greater part (in terms of value) of it is created
by the company;

8.1112E.3.c

intellectual property is created by a company if it is created in
circumstances in which the right to exploit it vests in the company (whether
alone or jointly with others).

8.1112E.4

For the purposes of this section—

“ intellectual property ” means— any patent, trade mark, registered design,
copyright, design right or plant breeder’s right, any rights under the law of
a country or territory outside the United Kingdom which correspond or are
similar to those falling within paragraph (a), or any information or technique
not protected by a right within paragraph (a) or (b) but having industrial,
commercial or other economic value; “ management activity ”, in relation to
intellectual property, means formulating plans and making decisions in
relation to the development or exploitation of the intellectual property.

8.1112E.5

A company meets condition B for an accounting period if the amount (if any)
given by subsection  (6)  does not exceed 15% of the company’s qualifying
expenditure for the period.

8.1112E.6

The amount given by this subsection is the sum of the following incurred by
the company in the period—

8.1112E.6.a

qualifying expenditure on externally provided workers (see section 1127),
where the company, the staff provider and (if different) the staff controller
(or staff controllers)—

8.1112E.6.a.i

are all connected, or

8.1112E.6.a.ii

have jointly elected (under section 1130) that section 1129 is to apply to
them as if they were all connected;

8.1112E.6.b

qualifying contractor expenditure, where the company and the contractor—

8.1112E.6.b.i

are connected, or

8.1112E.6.b.ii

have jointly elected (under section 1135) that section 1134 is to apply to
them as if they were connected.

8.1112E.7

In subsection  (6) (b) , “qualifying contractor expenditure” has whichever of
the meanings given by  1112C (7)  corresponds to the purpose for which this
section is being applied.

8.1112E.8

The Treasury may by regulations replace the percentage for the time being
specified in subsection  (5)  with a different percentage.

########## Going concerns

########### Restriction of credit and relief to companies that are going concerns

8.1112F

8.1112F.1

Subsection  (2)  applies if a company makes a claim under section  1042C
(claims for R&D expenditure credit) at a time when it is not a going concern.

8.1112F.2

No amount is to be paid to the company at step 7 in section  1042I  as a
result of the claim.

8.1112F.3

Subsection  (2)  ceases to apply (and the company accordingly becomes entitled
to be paid) if the company becomes a going concern on or before the last day
on which it would be entitled to amend the claim in accordance with paragraph
83E of Schedule 18 to FA 1998.

8.1112F.4

A company may not make—

8.1112F.4.a

a claim under section 1044 (R&D relief by way of additional deduction),

8.1112F.4.b

an election under section 1045 (R&D relief by way of deemed trading loss), or

8.1112F.4.c

a claim under section 1054 (R&D tax credit),

at a time when it is not a going concern.

8.1112F.5

If a company ceases to be a going concern after making a claim under section
1054, it is treated as if it had not made the claim (and accordingly there is
treated as having been no payment of R&D tax credit to carry interest under
section 826 of ICTA).

8.1112F.6

Subsection  (5)  does not apply so far as the claim relates to an amount that
was paid or applied before the company ceased to be a going concern.

########### Meaning of “going concern”

8.1112G

8.1112G.1

For the purposes of section  1112F , a company is a going concern if—

8.1112G.1.a

its latest published accounts were prepared on a going concern basis, and

8.1112G.1.b

nothing in those accounts indicates that they were prepared on that basis only
because of an entitlement or expected entitlement to a credit or relief under
this Part.

8.1112G.2

But a company is not a going concern if it is in administration or
liquidation.

8.1112G.3

For the purposes of this section, a company is in administration if—

8.1112G.3.a

it is in administration under Part 2 of the Insolvency Act 1986 or Part 3 of
the Insolvency (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 ( S.I. 1989/2405 (N.I. 19)) , or

8.1112G.3.b

a corresponding situation under the law of a country or territory outside the
United Kingdom exists in relation to the company.

8.1112G.4

For the purposes of this section, a company is in liquidation if—

8.1112G.4.a

it is in liquidation within the meaning of section 247 of that Act or Article
6 of that Order, or

8.1112G.4.b

a corresponding situation under the law of a country or territory outside the
United Kingdom exists in relation to the company.

8.1112G.5

If—

8.1112G.5.a

a company transfers its trade and research and development to another company
that is a member of the same group, and

8.1112G.5.b

only by reason of that transfer, the company’s accounts for the period of
account in which the transfer took place are not prepared on a going concern
basis,

the accounts are to be treated for the purposes of this section as if they
were prepared on a going concern basis.

8.1112G.6

Section 436(2) of the Companies Act 2006 (meaning of “publication” of
documents) has effect for the purposes of this section.

########## Outstanding tax matters

########### No credit payable if certain tax matters outstanding

8.1112H

8.1112H.1

This section applies in relation to an amount that a company would, but for
this section, be entitled to be paid—

8.1112H.1.a

at step 7 in section  1042I  (payment of R&D expenditure credit not applied
for other purposes), or

8.1112H.1.b

under section 1054 (payment of R&D tax credit).

8.1112H.2

If the company’s tax return for the accounting period in question is enquired
into by an officer of Revenue or Customs—

8.1112H.2.a

the amount does not have to be paid to the company, but

8.1112H.2.b

an officer of Revenue and Customs may make a payment on a provisional basis of
such amount as the officer thinks fit.

8.1112H.3

If the company has outstanding PAYE or NIC liabilities for the accounting
period in question, the amount does not have to be paid to the company.

8.1112H.4

For the purposes of subsection  (3) , a company has outstanding PAYE or NIC
liabilities for an accounting period if it has not paid to an officer of
Revenue and Customs any amount that it is required to pay—

8.1112H.4.a

under PAYE regulations, or

8.1112H.4.b

in respect of Class 1 national insurance contributions,

for payment periods ending in the accounting period.

########## Artificially inflated claims

########### Transactions aimed at obtaining credit or relief to be disregarded

8.1112I

8.1112I.1

To the extent that a transaction is attributable to arrangements entered into
for a disqualifying purpose, it is to be disregarded in ascertaining a
company’s entitlement to relief under this Part.

8.1112I.2

Arrangements are entered into for a disqualifying purpose if their main
purpose, or one of their main purposes, is to enable a company to obtain
relief under this Part—

8.1112I.2.a

to which it would not otherwise be entitled, or

8.1112I.2.b

of greater amount than that to which it would otherwise be entitled.

########## Additional limits

########### Power to further limit Chapter 2 relief

8.1112J

The Treasury may, by regulations, limit the availability of relief under
Chapter 2 in respect of—

8.1112J.a

companies (or groups of companies) of a prescribed description,

8.1112J.b

research and development projects of a prescribed description, or

8.1112J.c

expenditure of a prescribed description.

9.6

After section 1132 insert—

########### “Qualifying earnings”

9.6.1132A

9.6.1132A.1

This section determines what are “ qualifying earnings ” in relation to an
externally provided worker for the purposes of this Part.

9.6.1132A.2

The worker’s earnings are qualifying earnings if either—

9.6.1132A.2.a

the staff controller, or

9.6.1132A.2.b

the company in relation to which the worker is an externally provided worker,

is, in respect of any part of those earnings, required to account to an
officer of Revenue and Customs both for income tax under PAYE regulations and
for Class 1 national insurance contributions.

9.6.1132A.3

If subsection  (2)  does not apply, the worker’s earnings are qualifying
earnings if and to the extent that they are attributable to relevant research
and development that is undertaken outside the United Kingdom and to which
section  1138A  applies.

9.6.1132A.4

In this section, “ the worker’s earnings ” means the worker’s earnings under
the contract mentioned in section 1128(7).

9.7

For section 1133 and the italic heading preceding it substitute—

########### Contracting out

############ Contracted out research and development

9.7.1133

9.7.1133.1

This section applies for the purposes of this Part.

9.7.1133.2

A person “contracts out” research and development if—

9.7.1133.2.a

the person enters into a contract under which activities are to be undertaken
for it (whether by another party to the contract or by a sub-contractor),

9.7.1133.2.b

the activities undertaken in order to meet the obligations owed to the person
under the contract include research and development, and

9.7.1133.2.c

it is reasonable to assume, having regard to the terms of the contract and any
surrounding circumstances, that the person intended or contemplated when
entering into the contract that research and development of that sort would be
undertaken in order to meet those obligations.

9.7.1133.3

The research and development that is “contracted out” is the research and
development referred to in subsection  (2) (b) , to the extent that subsection
(2) (c)  is satisfied in relation to it.

9.7.1133.4

Research and development contracted out by a person is contracted out “to”—

9.7.1133.4.a

the party to the contract who undertakes the obligations referred to in
subsection  (2) (b) , and

9.7.1133.4.b

any sub-contractor who undertakes contractual responsibility for the
activities needed to meet those obligations.

9.7.1133.5

References to a sub-contractor include any sub-contractor at one or more
removes from the contract referred to in subsection  (2) .

9.7.1133.6

A “contractor payment” is a payment made in respect of contracted out research
and development to a person to whom it is contracted out.

9.7.1133.7

A payment that relates only partly to contracted out research and development
is to be apportioned on a just and reasonable basis for the purposes of
subsection  (6) .

9.7.1133.8

Sections 1134 to 1136 determine the “qualifying element” of a contractor
payment.

9.8

In section 1134 (qualifying element of sub-contractor payment made between
connected persons)—

9.8.a

in the heading, for “sub-contractor” substitute  “contractor” ;

9.8.b

in subsection (1), for paragraphs (a) and (b) (not including the following
“and”) substitute—

9.8.b.a

a company (“ A ”) makes a contractor payment to another person (“ B ”),

9.8.b.b

A and B are connected,

;

9.8.c

in subsection (1)(c)—

9.8.c.i

omit “sub-contractor”;

9.8.c.ii

for “the sub-contractor’s”, in both places it appears, substitute  “B’s” ;

9.8.d

in subsection (2)—

9.8.d.i

in the words before paragraph (a), omit “sub-contractor”;

9.8.d.ii

in paragraph (b), for “the sub-contractor’s” substitute  “B’s” ;

9.8.e

in subsection (3)—

9.8.e.i

in the words before paragraph (a), for “the sub-contractor” substitute  “B” ;

9.8.e.ii

in paragraph (a), for “the sub-contractor”, in the first place it appears,
substitute  “B” ;

9.8.e.iii

also in paragraph (a), omit “sub-contractor” in the second place it appears;

for paragraph (d) substitute—

is incurred in respect of—

also in paragraph (b), for “sub-contractor” substitute  “contractor” ;

In section 1123 (staffing costs) and sections 1127 to 1131 (qualifying

9.10

For section 1136 substitute—

########### Qualifying element of contractor payment: other cases

9.10.1136

9.10.1136.1

This section applies to a contractor payment to which section 1134 does not
apply.

9.10.1136.2

The qualifying element of the payment is 65% of the relevant portion of the
payment.

9.10.1136.3

The relevant portion is the portion that is incurred in respect of—

9.10.1136.3.a

research and development that is undertaken in the United Kingdom, or

9.10.1136.3.b

research and development that is undertaken outside the United Kingdom and to
which section  1138A  applies.

9.10.1136.4

An apportionment of expenditure necessary for the purposes of this section is
to be made on a just and reasonable basis.

9.11

Omit section 1138 (meaning of “ subsidised expenditure ”).

9.12

In place of the omitted section 1138 insert—

########### Externally provided workers and contractors: R&D undertaken abroad

9.12.1138A

9.12.1138A.1

This section applies to research and development undertaken outside the United
Kingdom if—

9.12.1138A.1.a

the research and development is undertaken in the circumstances described in
subsection  (2) , or

9.12.1138A.1.b

regulations made by the Treasury provide for this section to apply.

9.12.1138A.2

The circumstances are that there are conditions necessary for the purposes of
the research and development—

9.12.1138A.2.a

that are not present in the United Kingdom,

9.12.1138A.2.b

that are present in the location in which the research and development is
undertaken, and

9.12.1138A.2.c

that it would be wholly unreasonable for the company to replicate in the
United Kingdom.

9.12.1138A.3

In subsection  (2)  “conditions”—

9.12.1138A.3.a

includes—

9.12.1138A.3.a.i

geographical, environmental or social conditions;

9.12.1138A.3.a.ii

legal or regulatory requirements as a result of which the research and
development may not be undertaken in the United Kingdom, but

9.12.1138A.3.b

does not include conditions so far as relating to—

9.12.1138A.3.b.i

the cost of the research and development;

9.12.1138A.3.b.ii

the availability of workers to carry out the research and development.

9.12.1138A.4

The Treasury may by regulations make provision specifying things that are not
conditions for the purposes of subsection  (2) .

########### Exempt foreign permanent establishments

9.12.1138B

For the purposes of this Part in its application to an accounting period, a
company’s expenditure is “attributable to an exempt foreign permanent
establishment” if—

9.12.1138B.a

an election by the company under section 18A applies to the period, and

9.12.1138B.b

the expenditure is brought into account in calculating a relevant profits
amount or a relevant losses amount for the purposes of that section as it
applies in relation to the period.

9.13

After section 1140 insert—

########### Groups

9.13.1140A

For the purposes of this Part, a company is in the same group as another
company if those companies are in the same group for the purposes of Part 5 of
CTA 2010.

9.14

In section 1142 (meaning of “ qualifying body ”)—

9.14.a

for the heading substitute  “Ineligible companies” ;

9.14.b

in subsection (1), in the words before paragraph (a), for ““ qualifying body ”
means” substitute  “a company is an “ineligible company” if it is” ;

9.14.c

after subsection (4) insert—

9.14.c.5

Two companies that are in the same group may make a joint election the effect
of which is that—

9.14.c.5.a

in respect of any research and development contracted out by one of those
companies to the other, the company contracting it out is to be treated for
the purposes of this Part as an ineligible company, and

9.14.c.5.b

in determining whether activity is research and development for the purposes
of this Part, anything done by one of those companies further to a contract
with the other is to be treated as if done by the other company, in any case
where that results in activity that would not otherwise be research and
development being regarded as such.

9.14.c.6

Such an election—

9.14.c.6.a

must be made by notice in writing to an officer of Revenue and Customs, and

9.14.c.6.b

has effect until—

9.14.c.6.b.i

it is revoked by either company by further such notice, or

9.14.c.6.b.ii

the companies are no longer in the same group.

substitute  “ 1042C ” .

9.16

After section 1142B insert—

########### Right to payment of credit inalienable

9.16.1142C

9.16.1142C.1

The right of a company to be paid an amount of R&D expenditure credit or R&D
tax credit may not be assigned.

9.16.1142C.2

Accordingly, a purported assignment of such a right, or an agreement to assign
such a right, is void.

9.16.1142C.3

References to assignment in this section are to be read in Scotland as
references to assignation.

9.17

After section  1142C  (inserted by sub-paragraph  (16) ) insert—

########### General rule against payments of credit to nominees

9.17.1142D

9.17.1142D.1

Where an amount of R&D expenditure credit or R&D tax credit is owed to a
company, an officer of Revenue and Customs may not pay the amount to a person
other than the company (even on the instruction or at the request of the
company).

9.17.1142D.2

Subsection  (1)  does not apply if—

9.17.1142D.2.a

the company requests that payment be made to a person connected with the
company, or

9.17.1142D.2.b

the officer is satisfied that exceptional circumstances make payment to the
company impracticable or inconvenient.

9.18

After section  1142D  (inserted by sub-paragraph  (17) ) insert—

########### Orders and regulations: ancillary provision

9.18.1142E

Any order or regulations under this Part may—

9.18.1142E.a

contain incidental, supplemental, consequential and transitional provision and
savings;

9.18.1142E.b

make different provision for different purposes or areas.

##### Commencement and transitional and transitory provision

###### General commencement of Parts 1 and 2

16

16.1

The amendments made by this Schedule, except those made by sub-paragraphs
(16)  to  (18)  of paragraph  9 , have effect in relation to accounting
periods beginning on or after the appointed day.

16.2

In this Part, the “appointed day” is a day appointed by the Treasury in
regulations.

###### Assignments and nominations

17

17.1

The amendment made by paragraph  9 (16)  does not have effect in relation to—

17.1.a

an assignment made before 22 November 2023,

17.1.b

an agreement made before that date, or

17.1.c

an assignment made on or after that date to carry out an agreement made before
that date.

17.2

The amendment made by paragraph  9 (17)  has effect only in relation to claims
made on or after 1 April 2024.

###### Avoidance of overlaps and gaps in entitlement during transition

18

18.1

Sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (3)  apply if, but for those sub-paragraphs—

18.1.a

one company (“ company A ”) would be entitled to old R&D relief, and

18.1.b

another company (“ company B ”) would be entitled to new R&D relief,

in respect of expenditure attributable to the same research and development.

18.2

If company B would have been entitled to old R&D relief in respect of its
expenditure had the  Part 1  amendments not been made, only company B is
entitled to the relief.

18.3

In any other case, only company A is entitled to the relief.

18.4

Sub-paragraph  (5)  applies if—

18.4.a

a company incurs pre-commencement expenditure,

18.4.b

the company is not entitled to old R&D relief in respect of the expenditure,
and

18.4.c

had the expenditure been post-commencement expenditure, it would have been—

18.4.c.i

qualifying  Chapter 1A  expenditure by virtue of section  1042E  of CTA 2009
or section  1042F  of that Act as it refers to section  1042E , or

18.4.c.ii

qualifying Chapter 2 expenditure by virtue of section 1053 of CTA 2009 (as it
has effect after the  Part 1  amendments) or section  1053A  of that Act as it
refers to section 1053.

18.5

The company is to be treated as satisfying sections  1042F (4)  and  1053A (4)
of CTA 2009 for the purposes of ascertaining the entitlement of another
company to new R&D relief in respect of expenditure attributable to the same
research and development as the expenditure mentioned in sub-paragraph  (4) .

18.6

Sub-paragraph  (7)  applies if—

18.6.a

in respect of pre-commencement expenditure attributable to research and
development, one company (“ company C ”)—

18.6.a.i

is not entitled to old R&D relief, but

18.6.a.ii

would be so entitled if none of sections 104C(2), 104G(5), 104H(6), 104J(4),
104K(5), 104L(4), 1052(5) and 1053(4) of CTA 2009 (as they have effect before
the  Part 1  amendments) applied, and

18.6.b

in respect of post-commencement expenditure attributable to the same research
and development, another company (“ company D ”) would, had the expenditure
been pre-commencement expenditure, have been entitled to old R&D relief by
virtue of section 1053 of CTA 2009 (as it has effect before the  Part 1
amendments).

18.7

For the purpose of ascertaining the entitlement of company D to new R&D
relief, the research and development is to be treated as contracted out by
company D within the meaning of section  1133  of CTA 2009 (as it has effect
after the  Part 1  amendments).

18.8

In this paragraph—

“ the new R&D provisions ” means Part 13 of CTA 2009 as it has effect after
the  Part 1  amendments; “ new R&D relief ” means relief under the new R&D
provisions; “ the old R&D provisions ” means Chapter 6A of Part 3 or Part 13
of CTA 2009 as that Chapter or Part has effect before the  Part 1  amendments;
“ old R&D relief ” means relief under the old R&D provisions; “ the Part 1
amendments ” means the amendments made by  Part 1  of this Schedule; “ post-
commencement expenditure ” means expenditure incurred in an accounting period
beginning on or after the appointed day; “ pre-commencement expenditure ”
means expenditure incurred in an accounting period beginning before the
appointed day.

###### Transitional provision relating to claim notifications

19

The reference in section 1142B of CTA 2009 (as amended by paragraph  9 (15) )
to claims under section  1042C  of that Act is to be read as including claims
under section 104A of that Act before its repeal by paragraph  2 .

###### Transitional provision relating to the R&D intensity condition

20

The references in sections 1044 (2A) (b)  and 1045 (2A) (b)  of CTA 2009
(inserted by paragraph  6 (4)  and  (5) ) to having met the R&D intensity
condition in an accounting period—

20.a

include having met the R&D intensity condition for the purposes of paragraph
21  in an accounting period to which that paragraph applies, but

20.b

are not applicable to any other accounting period beginning before the
appointed day.

###### Higher rate of payable credit for R&D-intensive SMEs from 1 April 2023

21

21.1

Sub-paragraph  (2)  applies if, in an accounting period beginning before the
appointed day but ending on or after 1 April 2023, a company—

21.1.a

has a Chapter 2 surrenderable loss, and

21.1.b

meets the R&D intensity condition.

21.2

The amount of R&D tax credit to which the company is entitled for the period
is to be determined as if the amendment made by section 4(3)(d) of FA 2023
(reduction in rate of credit from 14.5% to 10%) had not been made.

21.3

Subsections  (2)  to  (7)  of section  1045ZA  of CTA 2009, as inserted by
paragraph  6 (6) , determine whether a company meets the R&D intensity
condition in an accounting period for the purposes of sub-paragraph  (1) (b) .

21.4

But subsections  (2)  and  (3)  of that section are to be read for the
purposes of sub-paragraph  (3)  as if “40%” appeared instead of “30%”.

21.5

In this paragraph, “Chapter 2 surrenderable loss” and “R&D tax credit” have
the same meanings as in Chapter 2 of Part 13 of CTA 2009 (see sections 1054
and 1055 of that Act).

  Films, television programmes and video games

Section  3

##### New regime for films, television programmes and video games

1

After Part 14 of CTA 2009 insert—

######### Films, television programmes and video games

########## Introduction and interpretation

########### Introduction to Part

############ Overview of Part

1.1179A

1.1179A.1

This Part—

1.1179A.1.a

lays down special rules about the taxation of companies in relation to certain
production activities in creative sectors, and

1.1179A.1.b

provides an entitlement to a credit in respect of expenditure on those
activities.

1.1179A.2

In particular—

1.1179A.2.a

this Chapter makes general provision about the application of Chapters  2  and
3  and about the interpretation of this Part;

1.1179A.2.b

Chapter  2  lays down the special rules about taxation;

1.1179A.2.c

Chapter  3  provides the entitlement to credit;

1.1179A.2.d

Chapter  4  makes provision about the application of this Part to films and
television programmes;

1.1179A.2.e

Chapter  5  makes provision about the application of this Part to video games.

############ Qualifying companies and productions

1.1179AA

1.1179AA.1

Chapters  2  and  3  apply where there is a qualifying production and a
qualifying company for that production.

1.1179AA.2

The later Chapters supply the meanings of those terms.

1.1179AA.3

See in particular—

1.1179AA.3.a

section  1179D , in relation to films and television programmes;

1.1179AA.3.b

section  1179F , in relation to video games.

1.1179AA.4

Whether a company is the qualifying company for a qualifying production
(including whether the production is a qualifying production) is to be
assessed separately in relation to each accounting period of the company.

1.1179AA.5

The assessment is to be made by reference to the state of affairs at the end
of that period.

1.1179AA.6

So far as future events are relevant to the assessment, it is to be made by
reference to the reasonable expectations of the company at that time.

1.1179AA.7

Subsections  (5)  and  (6)  are subject to any provision of this Part that
provides for a production no longer to be regarded as a qualifying production
in an accounting period as a result of events after the end of that period.

1.1179AA.8

Once a qualifying company has made an election under section  1179B (1)  in
respect of a qualifying production, no other company can subsequently be the
qualifying company for that production.

1.1179AA.9

In this Part, “production”, except when contained in another defined term or
used to refer to the act of producing something, means—

1.1179AA.9.a

a film (see section  1179DA ),

1.1179AA.9.b

a television programme (see section  1179DD ), or

1.1179AA.9.c

a video game.

########### Definitions and miscellaneous provision

############ UK expenditure

1.1179AB

1.1179AB.1

In this Part, “ UK expenditure ” means expenditure on goods or services that
are used or consumed in the United Kingdom.

1.1179AB.2

Any apportionment of expenditure for the purposes of this Part between
expenditure that is and is not UK expenditure is to be made on a just and
reasonable basis.

############ Company tax returns

1.1179AC

1.1179AC.1

In this Part, “ company tax return ” has the same meaning as in Schedule 18 to
FA 1998 (see paragraph 3(1)).

1.1179AC.2

Any amendment to a company tax return that must be made by virtue of this
Part, and any assessment to give effect to such a requirement, can be made
despite any limitation on the time within which such an amendment or
assessment can normally be made.

############ Groups

1.1179AD

For the purposes of this Part, a company is in the same group as another
company if those companies are in the same group for the purposes of Part 5 of
CTA 2010.

############ Regulations

1.1179AE

1.1179AE.1

Regulations made by the Secretary of State under this Part are to be made by
statutory instrument.

1.1179AE.2

An instrument containing such regulations is subject to annulment in pursuance
of a resolution of either House of Parliament.

1.1179AE.3

A power to make regulations under this Part includes the power to make
incidental, supplemental, consequential and transitional provision and
savings.

########## Special rules about taxation

########### The separate production trade

############ Election to tax qualifying production as separate trade

1.1179B

1.1179B.1

The qualifying company for a qualifying production may elect in its company
tax return for an accounting period for the production to be taxed as a
separate trade.

1.1179B.2

The effect of such an election is that the activities of the company in
relation to the production are to be treated for corporation tax purposes as a
trade separate from any other activities of the company (including activities
in relation to other qualifying productions).

1.1179B.3

In this Part—

1.1179B.3.a

that trade is called “the separate production trade”;

1.1179B.3.b

the accounting period to which the return containing the election relates is
called “the opt-in period”.

############ Duration of separate trade

1.1179BA

1.1179BA.1

When the qualifying company is treated as beginning to carry on the separate
production trade is determined by—

1.1179BA.1.a

section  1179DW , in the case of a film or television programme;

1.1179BA.1.b

section  1179FO , in the case of a video game.

1.1179BA.2

If the result is that the separate production trade is treated as having been
carried on in an accounting period before the opt-in period, any relevant
company tax return must be amended so as to give effect to that treatment in
that earlier accounting period.

1.1179BA.3

Once a company has made an election under section  1179B (1) , the activities
of the company in relation to the production are to continue to be treated as
a separate trade in accordance with this Chapter even if—

1.1179BA.3.a

the production ceases to be a qualifying production, or

1.1179BA.3.b

the company ceases to be the qualifying company for it.

1.1179BA.4

That is the case even if the production ceases to be regarded as a qualifying
production in the opt-in period as a result of events after the end of that
period.

1.1179BA.5

In the following provisions of this Chapter, “qualifying production” and
“qualifying company” are accordingly capable of including productions or
companies that used to be so.

########### Accounting for the separate trade

############ Calculation of profits

1.1179BB

1.1179BB.1

The profits of the separate production trade are to be calculated in
accordance with this section.

1.1179BB.2

For the first period of account, the following are to be brought into account—

1.1179BB.2.a

as a debit, the costs of the qualifying production incurred by the qualifying
company to date, and

1.1179BB.2.b

as a credit, the proportion of the qualifying company’s estimated total income
from the qualifying production that is treated as earned at the end of that
period.

1.1179BB.3

For subsequent periods of account, the following are to be brought into
account—

1.1179BB.3.a

as a debit, the difference between—

1.1179BB.3.a.i

the amount of the costs of the qualifying production incurred by the
qualifying company to date, and

1.1179BB.3.a.ii

the corresponding amount for the previous period, and

1.1179BB.3.b

as a credit, the difference between—

1.1179BB.3.b.i

the proportion of the qualifying company’s estimated total income from the
qualifying production that is treated as earned at the end of that period, and

1.1179BB.3.b.ii

the corresponding amount for the previous period.

1.1179BB.4

The proportion of the qualifying company’s estimated total income that is
treated as earned at the end of a period of account is given by—

      C   /   T       ×   I         where—         C is the total of the costs
of the qualifying production incurred by the qualifying company to date,
T is the estimated total cost to the qualifying company of the qualifying
production, and           I is the qualifying company’s estimated total income
from the qualifying production.

1.1179BB.5

What counts as costs of, and income from, the qualifying production is
determined by—

1.1179BB.5.a

section  1179DX , in the case of a film or television programme;

1.1179BB.5.b

section  1179FP , in the case of a video game.

(See also section  1179CB .)

1.1179BB.6

But nothing in this Part, except section  1179BE , allows an amount to count
as costs of the qualifying production if it would not generally be allowed as
a deduction in calculating the profits of a trade for corporation tax
purposes.

1.1179BB.7

Estimates for the purposes of this section must be made—

1.1179BB.7.a

as at the balance sheet date for each period of account, and

1.1179BB.7.b

on a just and reasonable basis taking into consideration all relevant
circumstances.

1.1179BB.8

Subsection  (9)  applies if a period of account of the separate production
trade does not coincide with an accounting period of the qualifying company.

1.1179BB.9

The expenditure and receipts brought into account for the period under this
section, and the resulting profit or loss, are to be apportioned to accounting
periods of the company for the purposes of this Part by reference to the
number of days in the periods concerned.

############ When costs are to be taken as incurred

1.1179BC

1.1179BC.1

For the purposes of section  1179BB , costs are incurred when they are
represented in the state of completion of the work in progress.

1.1179BC.2

Accordingly—

1.1179BC.2.a

payments in advance for work to be done are to be ignored until the work has
been carried out, and

1.1179BC.2.b

deferred payments are to be recognised to the extent that the work is
represented in the state of completion.

1.1179BC.3

But an amount that has not been paid is not an incurred cost until there is an
unconditional obligation to pay it.

1.1179BC.4

If an obligation is linked to income being earned from the qualifying
production, no amount is to be brought into account in respect of the costs of
the obligation unless an appropriate amount of income is or has been brought
into account.

############ Preliminary expenditure

1.1179BD

1.1179BD.1

This section applies if, before the qualifying company began to carry on the
separate production trade, it incurred expenditure on the development of the
qualifying production.

1.1179BD.2

The expenditure may be treated as expenditure of the separate production trade
incurred immediately after the company began to carry on the trade.

1.1179BD.3

If expenditure so treated has previously been taken into account for other tax
purposes, any relevant company tax return must be amended accordingly.

############ Treatment of certain capital amounts as revenue

1.1179BE

1.1179BE.1

This section applies for corporation tax purposes in relation to the separate
production trade.

1.1179BE.2

Expenditure that—

1.1179BE.2.a

counts as costs of the qualifying production, and

1.1179BE.2.b

would (apart from this subsection) be regarded as of a capital nature by
reason only of being incurred on the creation of an asset in the form of the
qualifying production,

is to be treated as expenditure of a revenue nature.

(As to other capital expenditure, see section 53 and section  1179BB (6) .)

1.1179BE.3

Receipts that—

1.1179BE.3.a

count as income from the qualifying production, and

1.1179BE.3.b

would (apart from this subsection) be regarded as of a capital nature,

are to be treated as receipts of a revenue nature.

########### Losses in the separate trade

############ Carrying forward of production losses

1.1179BF

1.1179BF.1

This section applies if a company makes a loss in the separate production
trade in a pre-completion period (see sections  1179DY  and  1179FQ ).

1.1179BF.2

The loss is not available for loss relief, except as provided in subsections
(3)  and  (5) .

1.1179BF.3

The loss is not prevented from being carried forward under section 45B of CTA
2010 to be deducted from profits of the separate production trade in a
subsequent period.

1.1179BF.4

If the loss is so carried forward and deducted, the deduction is to be ignored
for the purposes of section 269ZB of CTA 2010.

1.1179BF.5

To the extent that the loss could be carried forward under section 45B of CTA
2010 to the completion period or a subsequent accounting period, it may
instead be treated for the purposes of section 37 and Part 5 of CTA 2010 as a
loss made in that period.

1.1179BF.6

Subsection  (5)  does not apply to the extent that the loss is carried forward
by virtue of section  1179BG .

1.1179BF.7

In this section, “ loss relief ” includes any means by which a loss might be
used to reduce the amount in respect of which the company, or any other
person, is chargeable to tax.

############ Transfer of terminal loss to other qualifying production

1.1179BG

1.1179BG.1

This section applies if—

1.1179BG.1.a

a company (“the principal company”) ceases to carry on the separate production
trade in respect of a production,

1.1179BG.1.b

the principal company could, but for the cessation of that trade, carry an
amount (“the terminal loss”) forward under section 45A or 45B of CTA 2010 to
an accounting period after that in which the cessation occurs,

1.1179BG.1.c

when the trade ceases, either the principal company or another company in the
same group carries on another separate production trade under this Chapter
(“the other trade”), and

1.1179BG.1.d

the ceased trade and the other trade both relate to productions that are or
were qualifying productions by virtue of the same Chapter of this Part.

1.1179BG.2

If the other trade is carried on by the principal company, the company may, by
making a claim, treat the terminal loss (or part of it) as a loss made in the
other trade that is carried forward under section 45B of CTA 2010.

1.1179BG.3

If the other trade is carried on by another company—

1.1179BG.3.a

the principal company may surrender the terminal loss (or part of it) to the
other company, and

1.1179BG.3.b

the other company may, by making a claim, elect for the surrendered amount to
be treated as a loss made in the other trade that is carried forward under
section 45B of CTA 2010.

1.1179BG.4

The carrying forward of a loss by virtue of subsection  (2)  or  (3)  is to
the first accounting period beginning after the cessation of the ceased trade.

1.1179BG.5

If—

1.1179BG.5.a

the other trade is no longer carried on that accounting period,

1.1179BG.5.b

the company carrying on the other trade is not entitled to an expenditure
credit under Chapter  3  for that accounting period in respect of the other
trade, or

1.1179BG.5.c

in a case within subsection  (3) , the other company does not make the
election in relation to that accounting period,

the claim under subsection  (2)  or the surrender under subsection  (3)  is to
be treated as not having been made.

1.1179BG.6

The Treasury may, in relation to surrenders or elections under subsection  (3)
, make provision by regulations corresponding, subject to such adaptations or
modifications as appear to them to be appropriate, to that made by Part 8 of
Schedule 18 to the FA 1998.

1.1179BG.7

A deduction made under section 45B of CTA 2010 by virtue of this section is to
be ignored for the purposes of section 269ZB of CTA 2010.

1.1179BG.8

The principal company is not entitled to relief under section 45F of CTA 2010
in respect of an amount surrendered under subsection  (3) .

########## Expenditure credit

########### The entitlement

############ Entitlement to expenditure credit

1.1179C

1.1179C.1

The qualifying company for a qualifying production is entitled to an
expenditure credit for—

1.1179C.1.a

the opt-in period, and

1.1179C.1.b

(subject to subsection  (2) ) any subsequent accounting period in which it
continues to carry on the separate production trade.

1.1179C.2

If in any of those subsequent periods the production is no longer a qualifying
production, or the company is no longer the qualifying company for it, the
company is not entitled to an expenditure credit for the period.

1.1179C.3

But that does not affect the entitlement of the company for any subsequent
period in which the production is once again a qualifying production or the
company is once again the qualifying company for it.

1.1179C.4

If a production ceases to be regarded as a qualifying production in an
accounting period as a result of events after the end of that period—

1.1179C.4.a

the qualifying company is no longer entitled to an expenditure credit for that
period, and

1.1179C.4.b

any company tax return drawn up in reliance on such an entitlement must be
amended so as to remove anything derived from that entitlement.

1.1179C.5

An expenditure credit to which a company is entitled may be claimed by the
company in accordance with Part 9D of Schedule 18 to FA 1998.

############ Amount of expenditure credit

1.1179CA

1.1179CA.1

The amount of the expenditure credit to which a qualifying company is entitled
for an accounting period is determined as follows.

      Step 1       Ascertain the total of the company’s relevant global
expenditure (see subsection  (2) ) for all accounting periods up to and
including the present one.           Step 2       Deduct from that total any
expenditure that is not UK expenditure (see section  1179AB ).           Step
3       If the amount remaining after step 2 exceeds 80% of the total
ascertained at step 1, deduct the amount of the excess.       The remaining
amount is the company’s “qualifying expenditure to date”.           Step 4
Deduct from the company’s qualifying expenditure to date the amount (if any)
that was the company’s qualifying expenditure to date in the accounting period
for which it was last entitled to, and claimed, an expenditure credit in
respect of the qualifying production.       The remaining amount is the
company’s “qualifying expenditure for the period”.           Step 5       The
amount of the credit to which the company is entitled is the relevant
percentage of the company’s qualifying expenditure for the period.       The
relevant percentage is determined by—         section  1179DV , in the case of
a film or television programme;           section  1179FN , in the case of a
video game.

1.1179CA.2

Expenditure is “relevant global expenditure” for an accounting period if—

1.1179CA.2.a

it is brought into account under section  1179BB  in calculating the profits
of the separate production trade for that period, and

1.1179CA.2.b

it counts as relevant production expenditure in relation to the qualifying
production under—

1.1179CA.2.b.i

section  1179DR , in the case of a film or television programme;

1.1179CA.2.b.ii

section  1179FJ , in the case of a video game.

########### Treatment of credit

############ Expenditure credit to count as taxable receipt

1.1179CB

1.1179CB.1

An expenditure credit under this Chapter is not to be treated as income for
the purposes of section  1179BB .

1.1179CB.2

But if a company is entitled to, and claims, an expenditure credit under this
Chapter for an accounting period, the profits of the separate production trade
for that period must (having first been calculated in accordance with section
1179BB ) be adjusted by bringing the amount of the expenditure credit into
account as a credit.

############ Redemption of value of expenditure credit

1.1179CC

If a company is entitled to, and claims, an expenditure credit under this
Chapter for an accounting period, the credit is to be dealt with as follows.

      Step 1       The amount of the credit is to be applied in discharging
any liability of the company to pay corporation tax for the accounting period.
Step 2       Any amount remaining after step 1 is to be reduced, if necessary,
to the amount given by—     A   -   B         where—         A is the initial
amount of the credit (before step 1), and           B is the amount of
corporation tax that would be chargeable on that amount if it were an amount
of profits for the accounting period on which corporation tax was chargeable
at the main rate.                   For provision about the treatment of an
amount deducted under this step, see section  1179CD .           Step 3
The amount remaining after step 2 is to be applied in discharging any
liability of the company to pay corporation tax for any other accounting
period.           Step 4       If the company is a member of a group, it may
surrender the whole or part of any amount remaining after step 3 to any other
member of the group (as to which see section  1179CE ).           Step 5
Any amount remaining after step 4 is to be applied in discharging any other
liability of the company to pay a sum to the Commissioners for His Majesty’s
Revenue and Customs—         under or by virtue of an enactment, or
under an agreement made in connection with any person’s liability to make a
payment to the Commissioners under or by virtue of an enactment.
Step 6       Any amount remaining after step 5 is (subject to sections  1179CG
and  1179CH ) to be paid to the company by an officer of Revenue and Customs.

############ Treatment of notional tax deduction

1.1179CD

1.1179CD.1

This section applies if an amount is deducted under step 2 in section  1179CC
from the amount of the qualifying company’s expenditure credit.

1.1179CD.2

If the qualifying company is a member of a group, it may, in respect of the
accounting period for which the expenditure credit arises, surrender the whole
or part of the deducted amount to any other member of the group (as to which
see section  1179CE ).

1.1179CD.3

To the extent that the deducted amount is not surrendered under subsection
(2) , it is to be carried forward to the next accounting period of the
qualifying company, and subsections  (4)  and  (5)  apply.

1.1179CD.4

The carried-forward amount is to be applied in discharging any liability of
the qualifying company to pay corporation tax for the accounting period.

1.1179CD.5

If—

1.1179CD.5.a

any of the carried-forward amount remains after the application of subsection
(4) , and

1.1179CD.5.b

the qualifying company is a member of a group,

the qualifying company may, in respect of the accounting period, surrender the
whole or part of the remaining amount to any other member of the group (as to
which see section  1179CE ).

1.1179CD.6

If any of the carried-forward amount remains after the application of
subsections  (4)  and  (5) , it is to be carried forward to the next
accounting period of the qualifying company, and those subsections apply again
in relation to that accounting period.

############ Amounts surrendered to other group companies

1.1179CE

1.1179CE.1

Subsection  (3)  applies if an amount of expenditure credit is surrendered by
the qualifying company to another member of its group under step 4 in section
1179CC  or under section  1179CD (2)  or  (5) .

1.1179CE.2

For the purposes of that subsection—

1.1179CE.2.a

the accounting period in respect of which the surrender is made is “the
surrender AP”;

1.1179CE.2.b

an accounting period of the other group member is an “overlapping AP” if it
overlaps to any extent with the surrender AP.

1.1179CE.3

The surrendered amount is to be dealt with as follows.

      Step 1       Select an overlapping AP.           Step 2       Calculate
the proportion of the overlapping AP that overlaps with the surrender AP, and
apply that proportion to the amount of corporation tax payable by the other
group member for that overlapping AP.           Step 3       Calculate the
proportion of the surrender AP that overlaps with the overlapping AP, and
apply that proportion to the surrendered amount.           Step 4       The
amount given by step 3 is to be applied in discharging the liability of the
other group member to pay the corporation tax mentioned in step 2, up to the
amount given by that step.           Step 5       Select another overlapping
AP, if there is one, and repeat steps 2 to 4.           Step 6       If any of
the surrendered amount remains after steps 2 to 4 have been taken in relation
to each overlapping AP, the remainder is to be treated for the purposes of
section  1179CC  or (as the case may be) section  1179CD  as if it had not
been surrendered as mentioned in subsection  (1) .

1.1179CE.4

A surrender to which subsection  (3)  applies is not to be—

1.1179CE.4.a

taken into account in determining, for corporation tax purposes, the profits
of the qualifying company or the other group member, or

1.1179CE.4.b

regarded for corporation tax purposes as the making of a distribution.

############ Priority of discharge

1.1179CF

1.1179CF.1

An amount within subsection  (2)  is to be applied as described in that
subsection before any amount within subsection  (3)  is applied as described
in that subsection.

1.1179CF.2

An amount is within this subsection if it is to be applied under—

1.1179CF.2.a

section  1179CD (4) , or

1.1179CF.2.b

section  1179CE (3)  as it applies in relation to an amount surrendered under
section  1179CD (2)  or  (5) ,

in discharging the liability of a company to pay corporation tax for an
accounting period.

1.1179CF.3

An amount is within this subsection if it is to be (or would but for
subsection  (1)  be) applied under—

1.1179CF.3.a

section  1179CC , or

1.1179CF.3.b

section  1179CE (3)  as it applies in relation to an amount surrendered under
section  1179CC ,

in discharging the same liability as an amount within subsection  (2) .

########### Restrictions on payment

############ No credit payable if company in administration or liquidation

1.1179CG

1.1179CG.1

No amount may be paid to a company at step 6 of section  1179CC  if, when the
company claims the expenditure credit from which the amount is derived, the
company is in administration or liquidation.

1.1179CG.2

For the purposes of this section, a company is in administration if—

1.1179CG.2.a

it is in administration under Part 2 of the Insolvency Act 1986 or Part 3 of
the Insolvency (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 ( S.I. 1989/2405 (N.I. 19)) , or

1.1179CG.2.b

a corresponding situation under the law of a country or territory outside the
United Kingdom exists in relation to the company.

1.1179CG.3

For the purposes of this section, a company is in liquidation if—

1.1179CG.3.a

it is in liquidation within the meaning of section 247 of that Act or Article
6 of that Order, or

1.1179CG.3.b

a corresponding situation under the law of a country or territory outside the
United Kingdom exists in relation to the company.

############ No credit payable if certain tax matters outstanding

1.1179CH

1.1179CH.1

Subsection  (2)  applies if—

1.1179CH.1.a

a company would (but for that subsection) be entitled to be paid an amount at
step 6 of section  1179CC , and

1.1179CH.1.b

the company’s tax return for the accounting period in question is enquired
into by an officer of Revenue and Customs.

1.1179CH.2

The amount does not have to be paid to the company; but an officer of Revenue
and Customs may make a payment on a provisional basis of such amount as the
officer thinks fit.

1.1179CH.3

Subsection  (4)  applies if—

1.1179CH.3.a

a company would (but for that subsection) be entitled to be paid an amount at
step 6 of section  1179CC , and

1.1179CH.3.b

the company has not paid to an officer of Revenue and Customs any amount that
it is required to pay—

1.1179CH.3.b.i

under PAYE regulations,

1.1179CH.3.b.ii

under section 966 of ITA 2007 (visiting performers), or

1.1179CH.3.b.iii

in respect of Class 1 national insurance contributions,

for payment periods ending in the accounting period in question.

1.1179CH.4

The amount does not have to be paid to the company; but an officer of Revenue
and Customs may make a payment of such amount as the officer thinks fit.

1.1179CH.5

For the purposes of subsection  (3) , a “payment period” is—

1.1179CH.5.a

in relation to PAYE regulations or Class 1 national insurance contributions, a
period—

1.1179CH.5.a.i

which ends on the fifth day of a month, and

1.1179CH.5.a.ii

for which the company is liable to account for income tax and national
insurance contributions to an officer of Revenue and Customs;

1.1179CH.5.b

in relation to section 966 of ITA 2007, a period for which the company is
required to make a return as described in section 969(1)(b) of that Act.

########### Artificial arrangements

############ Disqualifying arrangements and non-commercial transactions

1.1179CI

1.1179CI.1

Subsections  (2)  and  (3)  apply if, at any time, a company is party to
disqualifying arrangements in relation to anything that is, was or becomes a
qualifying production ( “the production” ).

1.1179CI.2

The company is not entitled to an expenditure credit under this Chapter in
respect of the production for any accounting period.

1.1179CI.3

Any relevant company tax return must be amended accordingly.

1.1179CI.4

Subsection  (5)  applies if a transaction—

1.1179CI.4.a

is attributable to arrangements (other than disqualifying arrangements)
entered into otherwise than for genuine commercial reasons, and

1.1179CI.4.b

would result in a company obtaining a relevant advantage.

1.1179CI.5

The relevant advantage is to be counteracted by the making of just and
reasonable adjustments to any amounts relevant to the calculation of the
company’s entitlement to an expenditure credit under this Chapter.

1.1179CI.6

Those adjustments may be made (for example) by way of amendment, assessment,
or modification of an assessment.

1.1179CI.7

For the purposes of this section, arrangements are disqualifying arrangements
if their main purpose, or one of their main purposes, is to enable the company
to obtain a relevant advantage.

1.1179CI.8

But such arrangements are not disqualifying arrangements if the obtaining of
that advantage as a result of the arrangements could reasonably be regarded as
consistent with—

1.1179CI.8.a

the principles (whether expressed or implied) on which the provisions of this
Part are based, and

1.1179CI.8.b

the policy objectives of those provisions.

1.1179CI.9

For the purposes of this section, a company would obtain a relevant advantage
if it would become entitled to an expenditure credit under this Chapter—

1.1179CI.9.a

to which it would not otherwise be entitled, or

1.1179CI.9.b

of a greater amount than that to which it would otherwise be entitled.

1.1179CI.10

In this section, “ arrangements ” includes any scheme, agreement or
understanding, whether or not legally enforceable.

########## Films and television programmes

########### General

############ Application of Chapters 

1.1179D

1.1179D.1

For the purposes of this Part—

1.1179D.1.a

a qualifying film (see section  1179DB ) or qualifying television programme
(see section  1179DE ) is a qualifying production, and

1.1179D.1.b

the production company for a qualifying film or a qualifying television
programme (see section  1179DP ) is the qualifying company for that film or
programme.

1.1179D.2

The following provisions of this Chapter apply for the purposes of this Part
in relation to films and television programmes.

1.1179D.3

Expenditure credit under Chapter  3  is called “audiovisual expenditure
credit” when the entitlement to it arises in respect of a film or television
programme.

########### Qualifying films

############ Meaning of “film”

1.1179DA

1.1179DA.1

“ Film ” includes any record, however made, of a sequence of visual images
that is capable of being used as a means of showing that sequence as a moving
picture.

1.1179DA.2

Each part of a series of films is treated as a separate film, unless—

1.1179DA.2.a

the films form a series with not more than 26 parts,

1.1179DA.2.b

the combined playing time is not more than 26 hours, and

1.1179DA.2.c

the series constitutes a self-contained work or is a series of documentaries
with a common theme,

in which case the films are treated as a single film.

1.1179DA.3

References to a film include the film soundtrack.

############ Qualifying films

1.1179DB

A film is a qualifying film if it meets—

1.1179DB.a

the theatrical release condition (see section  1179DC ),

1.1179DB.b

the British certification condition (see section  1179DJ ), and

1.1179DB.c

the UK expenditure condition (see section  1179DO ).

############ Theatrical release condition

1.1179DC

1.1179DC.1

A film meets the theatrical release condition if—

1.1179DC.1.a

the film is intended for exhibition to the paying public at the commercial
cinema, and

1.1179DC.1.b

a significant proportion of the earnings from the film is intended to be
obtained by such exhibition.

1.1179DC.2

If the film does not meet that condition in an accounting period after the
opt-in period, it cannot meet it in any subsequent accounting period (subject
to section  1179E ).

########### Qualifying television programmes

############ Meaning of “television programme”

1.1179DD

1.1179DD.1

“ Television programme ” means any programme (with or without sounds) which—

1.1179DD.1.a

is produced to be seen on television or on the internet, and

1.1179DD.1.b

consists of moving or still images or of legible text or of a combination of
those things.

1.1179DD.2

Two or more television programmes that are commissioned together under the
same agreement are to be treated as a single television programme.

############ Qualifying television programmes

1.1179DE

A television programme is a qualifying television programme if—

1.1179DE.a

it is of an eligible category (see section  1179DF ),

1.1179DE.b

it is not an excluded programme (see section  1179DG ),

1.1179DE.c

it meets the broadcast condition (see section  1179DH ),

1.1179DE.d

in the case of a programme that is not an animation or a children’s programme,
it meets the slot length and hourly cost conditions (see section  1179DI ),

1.1179DE.e

it meets the British certification condition (see section  1179DJ ), and

1.1179DE.f

it meets the UK expenditure condition (see section  1179DO ).

############ Categories of qualifying programme

1.1179DF

1.1179DF.1

The eligible categories of television programme are—

1.1179DF.1.a

dramas,

1.1179DF.1.b

documentaries,

1.1179DF.1.c

animations, and

1.1179DF.1.d

children’s programmes.

1.1179DF.2

A television programme is a drama if—

1.1179DF.2.a

it consists wholly or mainly of a depiction of events,

1.1179DF.2.b

the events are depicted wholly or mainly by one or more persons performing,
and

1.1179DF.2.c

the whole or a major proportion of what is done by the person or persons
performing, whether by way of speech, acting, singing or dancing, involves the
playing of a role.

(Accordingly, “ drama ” may include a comedy.)

1.1179DF.3

A television programme is a documentary if—

1.1179DF.3.a

it depicts real events, places or circumstances,

1.1179DF.3.b

it is not a drama, and

1.1179DF.3.c

it is primarily intended to record or inform.

1.1179DF.4

A programme is a children’s programme if, when production activities begin, it
is reasonable to expect that the persons who will make up the programme’s
primary audience will be under the age of 15.

1.1179DF.5

See section  1179EA (3)  for the meaning of “animation”.

############ Excluded programmes

1.1179DG

1.1179DG.1

A television programme is an excluded programme if—

1.1179DG.1.a

it is an advertisement or other promotional programme,

1.1179DG.1.b

it is a news or current affairs programme or discussion programme,

1.1179DG.1.c

it is a quiz show, game show, panel show, variety show, chat show or similar
entertainment,

1.1179DG.1.d

it consists of or includes a competition or contest, or the results of a
competition or contest,

1.1179DG.1.e

it is a broadcast of a live event or of a theatrical or artistic performance
given otherwise than for the purpose of being filmed, or

1.1179DG.1.f

it is produced for training purposes.

1.1179DG.2

But a children’s programme is not an excluded programme by virtue of being a
quiz show or game show, or falling within subsection  (1) (d) , if the prize
total does not exceed £1,000.

1.1179DG.3

For that purpose the “prize total” for a programme is the total of—

1.1179DG.3.a

the amount of each relevant prize that is a money prize, and

1.1179DG.3.b

the amount spent on each other relevant prize by, or on behalf of, its
provider;

and here “ relevant prize ” means a prize offered in connection with
participation in a quiz, game, competition or contest in, or promoted by, the
programme.

1.1179DG.4

The Treasury may by regulations amend subsection  (2)  for the purpose of
increasing the amount of the money limit for the time being specified in that
subsection.

############ Broadcast condition

1.1179DH

1.1179DH.1

A television programme meets the broadcast condition if—

1.1179DH.1.a

it is intended for broadcast to the general public, and

1.1179DH.1.b

it is not a film that meets the theatrical release condition (see section
1179DC ).

1.1179DH.2

If the television programme does not meet that condition in an accounting
period after the opt-in period, it cannot meet it in any subsequent accounting
period (subject to section  1179E ).

############ Slot length and hourly cost conditions

1.1179DI

1.1179DI.1

A television programme that consists of distinct episodes meets the slot
length condition if the slot length of each episode is greater than 20
minutes.

1.1179DI.2

A television programme that does not consist of distinct episodes meets the
slot length condition if the slot length of the programme is greater than 20
minutes.

1.1179DI.3

A television programme meets the hourly cost condition if the average core
expenditure per hour of slot length in relation to the programme is at least
£1 million.

1.1179DI.4

In this section, “ slot length ” means the period of time which the episode or
(as the case may be) programme is commissioned to fill.

########### British certification condition

############ British certification condition: provisional and final satisfaction

1.1179DJ

1.1179DJ.1

In this section, references to a certificate are to be read—

1.1179DJ.1.a

in relation to a film, as references to a certificate under Schedule 1 to the
Films Act 1985, and

1.1179DJ.1.b

in relation to a television programme, as references to a certificate under
section  1179DM .

1.1179DJ.2

A film or television programme meets the British certification condition in a
pre-completion period (see section  1179DY ) if—

1.1179DJ.2.a

an interim certificate has effect in relation to it at the end of that period,
and

1.1179DJ.2.b

the production company’s company tax return for that period is accompanied by
the certificate.

1.1179DJ.3

A film or television programme meets the British certification condition in
the completion period (see section  1179DY ) and any subsequent accounting
period if—

1.1179DJ.3.a

at the end of the completion period, either—

1.1179DJ.3.a.i

a final certificate has effect in relation to the film or programme, or

1.1179DJ.3.a.ii

the production company has abandoned production activities in relation to the
film or programme and an interim certificate has effect in relation to it, and

1.1179DJ.3.b

the production company’s company tax return for that period is accompanied by
the certificate.

1.1179DJ.4

Subsections  (2)  and  (3)  are subject to subsections  (5)  and  (6) .

1.1179DJ.5

If a film or television programme does not meet the British certification
condition in the completion period, it is no longer to be regarded as having
met the condition (nor, therefore, as being a qualifying film or qualifying
television programme) in any pre-completion period.

1.1179DJ.6

If, after the end of an accounting period, a certificate ceases to have effect
in respect of that period, the film or programme in question is no longer to
be regarded as having met the British certification condition (nor, therefore,
as being a qualifying film or qualifying television programme) in that period
in reliance on that certificate.

1.1179DJ.7

Subsection  (6)  does not apply where an interim certificate ceases to have
effect on being superseded by a final certificate.

1.1179DJ.8

For the purposes of subsection  (6) , a certificate that ceases to have effect
so ceases in respect of all accounting periods, except to the extent that a
direction under paragraph 3 of Schedule 1 to the Films Act 1985 or section
1179DM  provides otherwise.

############ Television programmes: test for certification

1.1179DK

1.1179DK.1

The Secretary of State, with the approval of the Treasury, may by regulations
specify conditions which must be met by a television programme before it may
be certified as a British programme.

1.1179DK.2

Such regulations may—

1.1179DK.2.a

specify different conditions in relation to different descriptions of
programme;

1.1179DK.2.b

provide that certain descriptions of programme may not be certified as a
British programme;

1.1179DK.2.c

enable the Secretary of State to direct that any provision made by virtue of
paragraph  (b)  does not apply to a programme that meets certain conditions.

############ Television programmes: applications for certification

1.1179DL

1.1179DL.1

The production company for a television programme may apply to the Secretary
of State for a certificate under section  1179DM  in relation to the
programme.

1.1179DL.2

An application may be for an interim certificate or a final certificate.

1.1179DL.3

An interim certificate is a certificate that—

1.1179DL.3.a

is granted before the programme is completed (see section  1179EB ), and

1.1179DL.3.b

states that the programme, if completed in accordance with the proposals set
out in the application, will be a British programme.

1.1179DL.4

A final certificate is a certificate that—

1.1179DL.4.a

is granted after the programme is completed, and

1.1179DL.4.b

states that the programme is a British programme.

1.1179DL.5

The Secretary of State may require an applicant to provide documents or
information to assist the Secretary of State in determining the application.

1.1179DL.6

The Secretary of State may require information provided for the purposes of an
application to be accompanied by a statutory declaration, made by the person
providing it, as to the truth of the information.

1.1179DL.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision supplementing this
section, including—

1.1179DL.7.a

provision about the form of applications,

1.1179DL.7.b

provision about the particulars and evidence necessary for satisfying the
Secretary of State that a programme meets any conditions that apply by virtue
of section  1179DK , and

1.1179DL.7.c

provision that any statutory declaration which is required by subsection  (6)
to be made by any person may be made on the person’s behalf by such person as
is specified in the regulations.

############ Television programmes: certification and revocation

1.1179DM

1.1179DM.1

If—

1.1179DM.1.a

an application is made in accordance with section  1179DL , and

1.1179DM.1.b

the Secretary of State is satisfied that the television programme concerned
meets any conditions that apply by virtue of section  1179DK ,

the Secretary of State must certify the programme accordingly.

1.1179DM.2

An interim certificate—

1.1179DM.2.a

may be given subject to conditions, and (unless the Secretary of State directs
otherwise) is of no effect if the conditions are not met, and

1.1179DM.2.b

may be expressed to expire after a specified period, and (unless the Secretary
of State directs otherwise) ceases to have effect at the end of that period.

1.1179DM.3

If it appears to the Secretary of State that a film or television programme
certified under this section ought not to have been certified, the Secretary
of State may revoke the certificate.

1.1179DM.4

Unless the Secretary of State directs otherwise, a certificate that is revoked
is treated as never having had effect.

############ Disclosure of information for certification purposes

1.1179DN

1.1179DN.1

Section 18(1) of the Commissioners for Revenue and Customs Act 2005
(restriction on disclosure by Revenue and Customs officials) does not prevent
disclosure to the Secretary of State for the purposes of the Secretary of
State’s functions under—

1.1179DN.1.a

Schedule 1 to the Films Act 1985, or

1.1179DN.1.b

sections  1179DK  to  1179DM .

1.1179DN.2

Information disclosed to the Secretary of State for those purposes may be
disclosed by the Secretary of State to the British Film Institute.

1.1179DN.3

The Treasury may by regulations amend subsection  (2) —

1.1179DN.3.a

so as to substitute for the person or body specified in that subsection a
different person or body, or

1.1179DN.3.b

in consequence of a change in the name of the person or body so specified.

1.1179DN.4

A person to whom information is disclosed under subsection  (1)  or  (2)  may
not otherwise disclose it except—

1.1179DN.4.a

for the purposes of the Secretary of State’s functions under the provisions
referred to in subsection  (1) ,

1.1179DN.4.b

if the disclosure is authorised by an enactment,

1.1179DN.4.c

in pursuance of an order of a court,

1.1179DN.4.d

for the purposes of a criminal investigation or legal proceedings (whether
criminal or civil) connected with the operation of this Part or Schedule 1 to
the Films Act 1985,

1.1179DN.4.e

with the consent of the Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs,
or

1.1179DN.4.f

with the consent of each person to whom the information relates.

1.1179DN.5

Section 19 of the Commissioners for Revenue and Customs Act 2005 (offence of
unlawful disclosure of revenue and customs information) applies in relation to
a contravention of subsection  (4)  as it applies in relation to a
contravention of the provisions referred to in subsection (1) of that section.

########### UK expenditure condition

############ UK expenditure condition: provisional and final satisfaction

1.1179DO

1.1179DO.1

A film or television programme meets the UK expenditure condition in a pre-
completion period (see section  1179DY ) if—

1.1179DO.1.a

the production company’s company tax return for the period states—

1.1179DO.1.a.i

the total amount of core expenditure that is expected to be incurred in
relation to the film or programme, and

1.1179DO.1.a.ii

the amount of that expenditure that is expected to be UK expenditure, and

1.1179DO.1.b

the second of those amounts is at least 10% of the first.

1.1179DO.2

A film or television programme meets the UK expenditure condition in the
completion period (see section  1179DY ) and any subsequent accounting period
if—

1.1179DO.2.a

the production company’s company tax return for the completion period states—

1.1179DO.2.a.i

the total amount of core expenditure that has been incurred in relation to the
film or programme, and

1.1179DO.2.a.ii

the amount of that expenditure that is UK expenditure, and

1.1179DO.2.b

the second of those amounts is at least 10% of the first.

1.1179DO.3

Subsection  (1)  is subject to subsections  (4)  and  (5) .

1.1179DO.4

If a film or television programme does not meet the UK expenditure condition
in a pre-completion period, it is no longer to be regarded as having done so
(nor, therefore, as being a qualifying film or qualifying television
programme) in any previous accounting period by virtue of subsection  (1)  as
it applies to that previous period.

1.1179DO.5
