If a film or television programme does not meet the UK expenditure condition
in the completion period, it is no longer to be regarded as having done so
(nor, therefore, as being a qualifying film or qualifying television
programme) in any pre-completion period.

1.1179DO.6

References in this section to core expenditure are to core expenditure
incurred—

1.1179DO.6.a

in the case of a film or programme other than a qualifying co-production, by
the production company, or

1.1179DO.6.b

in the case of a qualifying co-production, by the co-producers.

1.1179DO.7

The Treasury may by regulations amend the percentage specified in subsection
(1)  or  (2) .

########### Production companies

############ Meaning of “production company”

1.1179DP

1.1179DP.1

A company is the production company for a film or television programme that is
not a qualifying co-production if—

1.1179DP.1.a

it is responsible for—

1.1179DP.1.a.i

pre-production, principal photography and post-production of the film or
programme, and

1.1179DP.1.a.ii

delivery of the film or programme in completed form,

1.1179DP.1.b

it is actively engaged in production planning and decision-making during pre-
production, principal photography and post-production,

1.1179DP.1.c

it directly negotiates, contracts and pays for rights, goods and services in
relation to the film or programme, and

1.1179DP.1.d

it is more directly engaged in the matters described in paragraphs  (a)  to
(c) , taken as a whole, than any other company that satisfies those
paragraphs.

1.1179DP.2

A company is the production company for a film or television programme that is
a qualifying co-production if—

1.1179DP.2.a

the company is a co-producer of the co-production,

1.1179DP.2.b

the company makes an effective creative, technical and artistic contribution
to the film or programme, and

1.1179DP.2.c

its creative, technical, and artistic contribution is greater than that of any
other company that—

1.1179DP.2.c.i

is also a co-producer of the co-production, and

1.1179DP.2.c.ii

is chargeable to corporation tax on income it receives from the film or
programme (or would be if it received any).

1.1179DP.3

Activities carried on in partnership are to be ignored in determining whether
a company is the production company for a film or television programme.

############ Qualifying co-productions and co-producers

1.1179DQ

1.1179DQ.1

A film is a “qualifying co-production” if it falls to be treated as a national
film in the United Kingdom under an international agreement.

1.1179DQ.2

A television programme is a “qualifying co-production” if it is eligible to be
certified under section  1179DM  under an international agreement.

1.1179DQ.3

A company is a “co-producer” of a qualifying co-production if it is regarded
as such under the international agreement by virtue of which the film or
television programme in question is a qualifying co-production.

1.1179DQ.4

In this section, “ international agreement ” means an agreement between His
Majesty’s Government in the United Kingdom and any other government,
international organisation or authority.

########### Qualifying expenditure and rate of credit

############ Expenditure that qualifies for credit

1.1179DR

Expenditure incurred by the production company for a film or television
programme counts as “ relevant production expenditure ” for the purposes of
section  1179CA (2)  if—

1.1179DR.a

it is core expenditure in relation to that film or television programme (see
section  1179DS ), and

1.1179DR.b

it is not excluded expenditure (see sections  1179DT  and  1179DU ).

############ Meaning of “core expenditure”

1.1179DS

Expenditure is “ core expenditure ” in relation to a film or television
programme if it is expenditure on the pre-production, principal photography or
post-production of the film or programme.

############ Excluded expenditure: research and development

1.1179DT

Expenditure is excluded expenditure to the extent that the production company
would, in respect of the expenditure, be able to claim—

1.1179DT.a

an R&D expenditure credit under Chapter 6A of Part 3, or

1.1179DT.b

relief under Part 13 (relief for expenditure on research and development).

############ Excluded expenditure: non-arm’s-length dealings with connected parties

1.1179DU

1.1179DU.1

Expenditure is excluded expenditure to the extent that it represents connected
party profit, unless subsection  (3)  applies.

1.1179DU.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1) , expenditure represents connected party
profit—

1.1179DU.2.a

if it is a payment to a person (“ C ”) in exchange for something supplied by
that person,

1.1179DU.2.b

if the production company is connected with C, and

1.1179DU.2.c

if, and to the extent that, the amount of the payment exceeds the expenditure
incurred by C in supplying that thing.

1.1179DU.3

This subsection applies if the amount of the payment is no more than would
have been the case had the transaction been entered into at arm’s length.

1.1179DU.4

A transaction would have been entered into “at arm’s length” if it made “the
arm’s length provision” within the meaning of Part 4 of TIOPA 2010 (and for
this purpose any limitation on the application of that Part is to be
disregarded).

1.1179DU.5

Subsections  (6)  and  (7)  apply if—

1.1179DU.5.a

the supply by C to the production company is one of a sequence of transactions
in which the thing supplied has been supplied by one person to another, and

1.1179DU.5.b

either—

1.1179DU.5.b.i

each transacting party in the sequence is connected to at least one other
transacting party in the sequence, or

1.1179DU.5.b.ii

each transaction in the sequence is entered into in furtherance of a single
scheme or arrangement (of whatever kind, and whether or not legally
enforceable).

1.1179DU.6

The reference to C in subsection  (2) (c)  is to be read as a reference to the
supplier in the first transaction in the sequence.

1.1179DU.7

The reference to the transaction in subsection  (3)  is to be read as
including each transaction in the sequence.

1.1179DU.8

In this section, “ payment ” includes any transfer of value.

############ Percentage of qualifying expenditure translated into credit

1.1179DV

1.1179DV.1

This section determines the relevant percentage for the purposes of step 5 in
section  1179CA (1) .

1.1179DV.2

In the case of—

1.1179DV.2.a

a qualifying film that is not an animation, or

1.1179DV.2.b

a qualifying television programme that is not an animation or a children’s
programme,

the relevant percentage is 34%.

1.1179DV.3

In the case of—

1.1179DV.3.a

a qualifying film that is an animation, or

1.1179DV.3.b

a qualifying television programme that is an animation or a children’s
programme,

the relevant percentage is, subject to the following subsections, 39%.

1.1179DV.4

Subsection  (5)  applies if, for any accounting period, the production company
is entitled to, and claims, an audiovisual expenditure credit on the basis
that the film or programme falls within subsection  (2) .

1.1179DV.5

In relation to any subsequent accounting period, the relevant percentage is
34%.

1.1179DV.6

The Treasury may by regulations replace the percentage for the time being
specified in subsection  (2) ,  (3)  or  (5)  with a different percentage.

########### Accounting for the separate trade

############ When the separate trade begins

1.1179DW

For the purposes of section  1179B , the production company for a film or
television programme is treated as beginning the separate production trade in
respect of the film or programme—

1.1179DW.a

when pre-production of the film or programme begins,

1.1179DW.b

if earlier, when any income from the film or programme is received by the
company.

############ Costs and income of separate trade

1.1179DX

1.1179DX.1

This section applies for the purposes of section  1179BB  as that section
applies in relation to a film or television programme.

1.1179DX.2

Expenditure counts towards the costs of the film or programme if it is
expenditure on—

1.1179DX.2.a

production activities in connection with the film or programme, or

1.1179DX.2.b

activities with a view to exploiting the film or programme.

1.1179DX.3

But an amount that has not been paid within the period of 4 months beginning
with the first day after the final day of a period of account is not to count
towards the costs incurred in that period.

1.1179DX.4

Receipts count towards the income from the film or programme if they are
receipts in connection with the making or exploitation of the film or
programme, including—

1.1179DX.4.a

receipts from the sale of the film or programme or rights in it,

1.1179DX.4.b

royalties or other payments for use of the film or programme, or aspects of it
(for example, characters or music),

1.1179DX.4.c

payments for rights to produce games or other merchandise, and

1.1179DX.4.d

receipts by way of a profit share agreement.

############ Accounting periods

1.1179DY

1.1179DY.1

A reference to an accounting period, in relation to a film or television
programme, is a reference to an accounting period of the production company
for the film or programme.

1.1179DY.2

A reference to the “ completion period ”, in relation to a film or television
programme, is a reference to the accounting period in which—

1.1179DY.2.a

the film or programme is completed (see section  1179EB ), or

1.1179DY.2.b

the production company abandons production activities in relation to the film
or programme.

1.1179DY.3

The production company for a film or television programme must, in its company
tax return for the completion period, state whichever of those has occurred.

1.1179DY.4

A reference to a “ pre-completion period ”, in relation to a film or
television programme, is a reference to any accounting period before the
completion period in relation to that film or programme.

1.1179DY.5

In this section, “ production company ” includes a company that is no longer
the production company for the film or television programme but is still
carrying on the separate production trade in relation to it.

########### Miscellaneous

############ Effect of move out of higher-percentage category

1.1179DZ

1.1179DZ.1

Subsection  (2)  applies if, for an accounting period, a production company is
entitled to, and claims, an audiovisual expenditure credit—

1.1179DZ.1.a

in respect of a film on the basis that it is an animation, or

1.1179DZ.1.b

in respect of a television programme on the basis that it is an animation or a
children’s programme.

1.1179DZ.2

The production company may not, for any subsequent accounting period, claim an
audiovisual expenditure credit in respect of the film or programme on the
basis that it is—

1.1179DZ.2.a

a qualifying film other than an animation, or

1.1179DZ.2.b

a qualifying television programme other than an animation or a children’s
programme.

1.1179DZ.3

Subsection  (2)  ceases to apply if the company amends its company tax return
for the accounting period referred to in subsection  (1)  to withdraw the
claim for expenditure credit for that period.

1.1179DZ.4

An amendment may be made for that purpose despite any limitation on the time
within which the return could normally be amended.

############ Production qualifying consecutively as film and television programme

1.1179E

1.1179E.1

The same production may be a qualifying film in one accounting period and a
qualifying television programme in a subsequent accounting period, or vice
versa.

1.1179E.2

Such a change does not interrupt the application of this Part in relation to
the film or programme.

1.1179E.3

Section  1179DC (2)  does not apply to a failure to meet the theatrical
release condition in an accounting period if, in that period, the film was a
qualifying television programme.

1.1179E.4

Section  1179DH (2)  does not apply to a failure to meet the broadcast
condition in an accounting period if, in that period, the television programme
was a qualifying film.

1.1179E.5

A certificate under Schedule 1 to the Films Act 1985 has effect for the
purposes of this Part as it may apply to the certified film as a television
programme.

1.1179E.6

A certificate under section  1179DM  has effect for the purposes of this Part
as it may apply to the certified television programme as a film.

############ Meaning of “production activities”, “principal photography” and “animation”

1.1179EA

1.1179EA.1

“ Production activities ”, in relation to a film or television programme,
means the activities involved in development, pre-production, principal
photography and post-production of the film or programme.

1.1179EA.2

“ Principal photography ”, in relation to a film or television programme,
includes the generation of images by a computer for inclusion in the film or
programme.

1.1179EA.3

A film or television programme is an “animation” if (and only if)—

1.1179EA.3.a

the imagery of the completed film or programme includes animation, and

1.1179EA.3.b

the core expenditure on the completed animation constitutes at least 51% of
the total core expenditure on the completed film or programme.

############ When film or programme is completed

1.1179EB

1.1179EB.1

A film is “completed” when it is first in a form in which it can reasonably be
regarded as ready for copies of it to be made and distributed for presentation
to the general public.

1.1179EB.2

A television programme is “completed” when it is first in a form in which it
can reasonably be regarded as ready for broadcast to the general public.

########## Video games

########### General

############ Application of Chapters 

1.1179F

1.1179F.1

For the purposes of this Part—

1.1179F.1.a

a qualifying video game (see section  1179FA ) is a qualifying production, and

1.1179F.1.b

the development company for a qualifying video game (see section  1179FI ) is
the qualifying company for that video game.

1.1179F.2

The following provisions of this Chapter apply for the purposes of this Part
in relation to video games.

1.1179F.3

Expenditure credit under Chapter  3  is called “video game expenditure credit”
when the entitlement to it arises in respect of a video game.

########### Qualifying video games

############ Video games that are qualifying video games

1.1179FA

1.1179FA.1

A video game is a qualifying video game if—

1.1179FA.1.a

it is not an excluded game (see subsection  (2) ),

1.1179FA.1.b

it meets the intended supply condition (see section  1179FB ),

1.1179FA.1.c

it meets the British certification condition (see section  1179FC ), and

1.1179FA.1.d

it meets the UK expenditure condition (see section  1179FH ).

1.1179FA.2

A video game is an excluded game if it is produced for—

1.1179FA.2.a

advertising or promotional purposes, or

1.1179FA.2.b

the purposes of gambling, within the meaning of the Gambling Act 2005.

############ Intended supply condition

1.1179FB

1.1179FB.1

A video game meets the intended supply condition if it is intended for supply
to the general public.

1.1179FB.2

If the video game does not meet that condition in an accounting period after
the opt-in period, it cannot meet it in any subsequent accounting period.

########### British certification condition

############ British certification condition: provisional and final satisfaction

1.1179FC

1.1179FC.1

In this section, references to a certificate are to a certificate under
section  1179FF .

1.1179FC.2

A video game meets the British certification condition in a pre-completion
period (see section  1179FQ ) if—

1.1179FC.2.a

an interim certificate has effect in relation to it at the end of that period,
and

1.1179FC.2.b

the development company’s company tax return for that period is accompanied by
the certificate.

1.1179FC.3

A video game meets the British certification condition in the completion
period (see section  1179FQ ) and any subsequent accounting period if—

1.1179FC.3.a

at the end of the completion period, either—

1.1179FC.3.a.i

a final certificate has effect in relation to the video game, or

1.1179FC.3.a.ii

the development company has abandoned development activities in relation to
the video game and an interim certificate has effect in relation to it, and

1.1179FC.3.b

the development company’s company tax return for that period is accompanied by
the certificate.

1.1179FC.4

Subsections  (2)  and  (3)  are subject to subsections  (5)  and  (6) .

1.1179FC.5

If a video game does not meet the British certification condition in the
completion period, it is no longer to be regarded as having done so (nor,
therefore, as being a qualifying video game) in any pre-completion period.

1.1179FC.6

If, after the end of an accounting period, a certificate ceases to have effect
in respect of that period, the video game in question is no longer to be
regarded as having met the British certification condition (nor, therefore, as
being a qualifying video game) in that period in reliance on that certificate.

1.1179FC.7

Subsection  (6)  does not apply where an interim certificate ceases to have
effect on being superseded by a final certificate.

1.1179FC.8

For the purposes of subsection  (6) , a certificate that ceases to have effect
so ceases in respect of all accounting periods, except to the extent that a
direction under section  1179FF  provides otherwise.

############ Test for certification

1.1179FD

1.1179FD.1

The Secretary of State, with the approval of the Treasury, may by regulations
specify conditions which must be met by a video game before it may be
certified as a British video game.

1.1179FD.2

Such regulations may—

1.1179FD.2.a

specify different conditions in relation to different descriptions of video
game;

1.1179FD.2.b

provide that certain descriptions of video game may not be certified as a
British video game;

1.1179FD.2.c

enable the Secretary of State to direct that any provision made by virtue of
paragraph  (b)  does not apply to a video game that meets certain conditions.

############ Applications for certification

1.1179FE

1.1179FE.1

The development company for a video game may apply to the Secretary of State
for a certificate under section  1179FF  in relation to the programme.

1.1179FE.2

An application may be for an interim certificate or a final certificate.

1.1179FE.3

An interim certificate is a certificate that—

1.1179FE.3.a

is granted before the video game is completed (see section  1179FS ), and

1.1179FE.3.b

states that the video game, if completed in accordance with the proposals set
out in the application, will be a British video game.

1.1179FE.4

A final certificate is a certificate that—

1.1179FE.4.a

is granted after the video game is completed, and

1.1179FE.4.b

states that the video game is a British video game.

1.1179FE.5

The Secretary of State may require an applicant to provide documents or
information to assist the Secretary of State in determining the application.

1.1179FE.6

The Secretary of State may require information provided for the purposes of an
application to be accompanied by a statutory declaration, made by the person
providing it, as to the truth of the information.

1.1179FE.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision supplementing this
section, including—

1.1179FE.7.a

provision about the form of applications,

1.1179FE.7.b

provision about the particulars and evidence necessary for satisfying the
Secretary of State that a video game meets any conditions that apply by virtue
of section  1179FD , and

1.1179FE.7.c

provision that any statutory declaration which is required by subsection  (6)
to be made by any person may be made on the person’s behalf by such person as
is specified in the regulations.

############ Certification and revocation

1.1179FF

1.1179FF.1

If—

1.1179FF.1.a

an application is made in accordance with section  1179FE , and

1.1179FF.1.b

the Secretary of State is satisfied that the video game concerned meets any
conditions that apply by virtue of section  1179FD ,

the Secretary of State must certify the video game accordingly.

1.1179FF.2

An interim certificate—

1.1179FF.2.a

may be given subject to conditions, and (unless the Secretary of State directs
otherwise) is of no effect if the conditions are not met, and

1.1179FF.2.b

may be expressed to expire after a specified period, and (unless the Secretary
of State directs otherwise) ceases to have effect at the end of that period.

1.1179FF.3

If it appears to the Secretary of State that a video game certified under this
section ought not to have been certified, the Secretary of State may revoke
the certificate.

1.1179FF.4

Unless the Secretary of State directs otherwise, a certificate that is revoked
is treated as never having had effect.

############ Disclosure of information for certification purposes

1.1179FG

Section  1179DN  (disapplication of section 18, and application of section 19,
of the Commissioners for Revenue and Customs Act 2005) has effect in relation
to the Secretary of State’s functions under sections  1179FD  to  1179FF  as
it has effect in relation to the Secretary of State’s functions under sections
1179DK  to  1179DM .

########### UK expenditure condition

############ UK expenditure condition

1.1179FH

1.1179FH.1

A video game meets the UK expenditure condition in a pre-completion period
(see section  1179FQ ) if—

1.1179FH.1.a

the development company’s company tax return for the period states—

1.1179FH.1.a.i

the total amount of core expenditure that is expected to be incurred in
relation to the video game, and

1.1179FH.1.a.ii

the amount of that expenditure that is expected to be UK expenditure, and

1.1179FH.1.b

the second of those amounts is at least 10% of the first.

1.1179FH.2

A video game meets the UK expenditure condition in the completion period (see
section  1179FQ ) and any subsequent accounting period if—

1.1179FH.2.a

the development company’s company tax return for the completion period states—

1.1179FH.2.a.i

the total amount of core expenditure that has been incurred in relation to the
video game, and

1.1179FH.2.a.ii

the amount of that expenditure that is UK expenditure, and

1.1179FH.2.b

the second of those amounts is at least 10% of the first.

1.1179FH.3

Subsection  (1)  is subject to subsections  (4)  and  (5) .

1.1179FH.4

If a video game does not meet the UK expenditure condition in a pre-completion
period, it is no longer to be regarded as having done so (nor, therefore, as
being a qualifying video game) in any previous accounting period by virtue of
subsection  (1)  as it applies to that previous period.

1.1179FH.5

If a video game does not meet the UK expenditure condition in the completion
period, it is no longer to be regarded as having done so (nor, therefore, as
being a qualifying video game) in any pre-completion period.

1.1179FH.6

References in this section to core expenditure are to core expenditure
incurred by the development company.

1.1179FH.7

The Treasury may by regulations amend the percentage specified in subsection
(1)  or  (2) .

########### Development companies

############ Meaning of “development company”

1.1179FI

1.1179FI.1

A company is the development company for a video game if—

1.1179FI.1.a

it is responsible for designing, producing and testing the video game,

1.1179FI.1.b

it is actively engaged in planning and decision-making during the design,
production and testing of the video game,

1.1179FI.1.c

it directly negotiates, contracts and pays for rights, goods and services in
relation to the video game, and

1.1179FI.1.d

it is more directly engaged in the matters described in paragraphs  (a)  to
(c) , taken as a whole, than any other company that satisfies those
paragraphs.

1.1179FI.2

Activities carried on in partnership are to be ignored in determining whether
a company is the development company for a video game.

########### Qualifying expenditure and rate of credit

############ Expenditure that qualifies for credit

1.1179FJ

Expenditure incurred by the development company for a video game counts as “
relevant production expenditure ” for the purposes of section  1179CA (2)  if—

1.1179FJ.a

it is core expenditure in relation to that video game (see section  1179FK ),
and

1.1179FJ.b

it is not excluded expenditure (see sections  1179FL  and  1179FM ).

############ Meaning of “core expenditure”

1.1179FK

1.1179FK.1

Expenditure is “ core expenditure ” in relation to a video game if it is
expenditure on designing, producing or testing the video game.

1.1179FK.2

But core expenditure does not include expenditure on—

1.1179FK.2.a

designing the initial concept for a video game, or

1.1179FK.2.b

debugging, or carrying out maintenance in connection with, a completed video
game.

############ Excluded expenditure: research and development

1.1179FL

Expenditure is excluded expenditure to the extent that the development company
would, in respect of the expenditure, be able to claim—

1.1179FL.a

an R&D expenditure credit under Chapter 6A of Part 3, or

1.1179FL.b

relief under Part 13 (relief in respect of expenditure on research and
development).

############ Excluded expenditure: non-arm’s-length dealings with connected parties

1.1179FM

1.1179FM.1

Expenditure is excluded expenditure to the extent that it represents connected
party profit, unless subsection  (3)  applies.

1.1179FM.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1) , expenditure represents connected party
profit—

1.1179FM.2.a

if it is a payment to a person (“ C ”) in exchange for something supplied by
that person,

1.1179FM.2.b

if the development company is connected with C, and

1.1179FM.2.c

if, and to the extent that, the amount of the payment exceeds the expenditure
incurred by C in supplying that thing.

1.1179FM.3

This subsection applies if the amount of the payment is no more than would
have been the case had the transaction been entered into at arm’s length.

1.1179FM.4

A transaction would have been entered into “at arm’s length” if it made “the
arm’s length provision” within the meaning of Part 4 of TIOPA 2010 (and for
this purpose any limitation on the application of that Part is to be
disregarded).

1.1179FM.5

Subsections  (6)  and  (7)  apply if—

1.1179FM.5.a

the supply by C to the development company is one of a sequence of
transactions in which the thing supplied has been supplied by one person to
another, and

1.1179FM.5.b

either—

1.1179FM.5.b.i

each transacting party in the sequence is connected to at least one other
transacting party in the sequence, or

1.1179FM.5.b.ii

each transaction in the sequence is entered into in furtherance of a single
scheme or arrangement (of whatever kind, and whether or not legally
enforceable).

1.1179FM.6

The reference to C in subsection  (2) (c)  is to be read as a reference to the
supplier in the first transaction in the sequence.

1.1179FM.7

The reference to the transaction in subsection  (3)  is to be read as
including each transaction in the sequence.

1.1179FM.8

In this section, “ payment ” includes any transfer of value.

############ Percentage of qualifying expenditure translated into credit

1.1179FN

1.1179FN.1

In relation to a qualifying video game, the relevant percentage for the
purposes of step 5 in section  1179CA (1)  is 34%.

1.1179FN.2

The Treasury may by regulations replace the percentage for the time being
specified in subsection  (1)  with a different percentage.

########### Accounting for the separate trade

############ When the separate trade begins

1.1179FO

For the purposes of section  1179B , the development company for a video game
is treated as beginning the separate production trade in respect of the video
game—

1.1179FO.a

when the design of the video game begins,

1.1179FO.b

if earlier, when any income from the video game is received by the company.

############ Costs and income of separate trade

1.1179FP

1.1179FP.1

This section applies for the purposes of section  1179BB  as that section
applies in relation to a video game.

1.1179FP.2

Expenditure counts towards the costs of the video game if it is expenditure
on—

1.1179FP.2.a

development activities in connection with the video game, or

1.1179FP.2.b

activities with a view to exploiting the video game.

1.1179FP.3

But an amount that has not been paid within the period of 4 months beginning
with the first day after the final day of a period of account is not to count
towards the costs incurred in that period.

1.1179FP.4

Receipts count towards the income from the video game if they are receipts in
connection with the production or exploitation of the video game, including—

1.1179FP.4.a

receipts from the sale of the video game or rights in it,

1.1179FP.4.b

royalties or other payments for use of the video game, or aspects of it (for
example, characters or music),

1.1179FP.4.c

payments for rights to produce games or other merchandise, and

1.1179FP.4.d

receipts by way of a profit share agreement.

############ Accounting periods

1.1179FQ

1.1179FQ.1

A reference to an accounting period, in relation to a video game, is a
reference to an accounting period of the development company for the video
game.

1.1179FQ.2

A reference to the “ completion period ”, in relation to a video game, is a
reference to the accounting period in which—

1.1179FQ.2.a

the video game is completed (see section  1179FS ), or

1.1179FQ.2.b

the development company abandons development activities in relation to the
video game.

1.1179FQ.3

The development company for a video game must, in its company tax return for
the completion period, state whichever of those has occurred.

1.1179FQ.4

A reference to a “ pre-completion period ”, in relation to a video game, is a
reference to any accounting period before the completion period in relation to
that video game.

1.1179FQ.5

In this section, “ development company ” includes a company that is no longer
the development company for the video game but is still carrying on the
separate production trade in relation to it.

########### Miscellaneous

############ Meaning of “development activities”

1.1179FR

“ Development activities ”, in relation to a video game, means the activities
involved in designing, producing and testing the video game.

############ When video game is completed

1.1179FS

A video game is “completed” when it is first in a form in which it can
reasonably be regarded as ready for copies of it to be made and made available
to the general public.

6.4

In Part 8B (profits taxable at Northern Ireland rate), after Chapter 10
insert—

############ Films, television programmes and video games qualifying for expenditure credit

############# Introduction

############## Application and interpretation

6.4.357QE

6.4.357QE.1

This Chapter makes provision about the interaction between this Part and Part
14A  of CTA 2009 (films, television programmes and video games).

6.4.357QE.2

This Chapter applies if—

6.4.357QE.2.a

a company is a Northern Ireland company in an accounting period,

6.4.357QE.2.b

the company is treated under Part  14A  of CTA 2009 as carrying on a separate
trade in that period (see  1179B  of that Act), and

6.4.357QE.2.c

that trade is a qualifying trade.

6.4.357QE.3

References in this Chapter to “the Northern Ireland company”, “ the accounting
period ” and “ the separate trade ” are to be read accordingly.

############# Expenditure credit

############## Expenditure credit to count towards mainstream profits or losses

6.4.357QF

6.4.357QF.1

Subsection  (2)  applies if, under section  1179CB  of CTA 2009 (expenditure
credit under Part  14A  of CTA 2009 to be taxable receipt), the Northern
Ireland company brings an amount of audiovisual expenditure credit or video
game expenditure credit into account in calculating the profits of the
separate trade for the accounting period.

6.4.357QF.2

The amount is to form part of the mainstream profits or mainstream losses of
the trade for that period.

############# Losses of separate trade

############## Carrying forward of production losses

6.4.357QG

6.4.357QG.1

If the accounting period is a pre-completion period within the meaning of
section  1179BF  of CTA 2009 (carrying forward of production losses in
separate trade), that section applies in relation to the separate trade and
that accounting period subject to the following provisions.

6.4.357QG.2

In subsection  (1)  of that section, the reference to a loss is to be read as
a reference to—

6.4.357QG.2.a

any Northern Ireland losses, or

6.4.357QG.2.b

any mainstream losses;

and the rest of that section is to be read accordingly.

6.4.357QG.3

Subsection  (4)  applies if the Northern Ireland company has in the accounting
period—

6.4.357QG.3.a

both Northern Ireland losses of the separate trade and mainstream profits of
that trade, or

6.4.357QG.3.b

both mainstream losses of the separate trade and Northern Ireland profits of
that trade.

6.4.357QG.4

The company may, despite section  1179BF (2)  of CTA 2009, claim under section
37 (relief for trade losses against total profits) for—

6.4.357QG.4.a

relief for those Northern Ireland losses against those mainstream profits, or

6.4.357QG.4.b

relief for those mainstream losses against those Northern Ireland profits.

############## Transfer of terminal loss

6.4.357QH

6.4.357QH.1

Subsection  (2)  applies if—

6.4.357QH.1.a

the Northern Ireland company ceases to carry on the separate trade in the
accounting period,

6.4.357QH.1.b

as a result, section  1179BG  of CTA 2009 (transfer of terminal loss in
separate production trade to other production or group company) applies, and

6.4.357QH.1.c

the amount in respect of which it applies (see subsection  (1) (b)  of that
section) represents a Northern Ireland loss.

6.4.357QH.2

The references to a loss in subsections  (2)  and  (3) (b)  of that section
are to be read as references to a Northern Ireland loss.

##### Repeal of existing regimes for films, television programmes and video games

7

In CTA 2009, omit Parts 15 to 15B.

###### Films Act 1985

8.3

In Schedule 1 (certification of British films) (as amended by paragraph  2 )—

8.3.a

in the heading, omit “and film tax relief”;

8.3.b

in paragraph 1(1), in the definition of “film production company”, omit the
words from “or” to the end.

###### ICTA

9

9.1

Section 826 of ICTA (interest on tax overpaid) is amended as follows.

9.2

##### Commencement and transitional provision

###### General commencement

16

16.1

No election under section  1179B (1)  of CTA 2009 may be made in a company tax
return for an accounting period ending before 1 January 2024.

16.2

The amendments made by Parts  3  and  4  of this Schedule have effect in
relation to accounting periods beginning on or after 1 April 2027.

###### Closure of existing regimes to new productions

17

A company is not to be treated as carrying on a separate trade under Part 15,
15A or 15B of CTA 2009 if the trade would be treated under that Part as
beginning on or after 1 April 2025.

###### Opting into new regime during transitional period

18

18.1

If a company makes an election under section  1179B (1)  of CTA 2009 in its
company tax return for an accounting period beginning before 1 January 2024—

18.1.a

Part  14A  of CTA 2009 applies further to that election only in respect of the
portion of the accounting period that falls on or after that date, and

18.1.b

the relevant existing regime applies in respect of the portion of the
accounting period that falls before that date.

18.2

If a company makes an election under section  1179B (1)  of CTA 2009 in its
company tax return for an accounting period beginning on or after 1 January
2024, the relevant existing regime does not apply in relation to that
accounting period or any subsequent accounting period, subject to sub-
paragraphs  (3)  and  (4) .

18.3

If a company makes an election under section  1179B (1)  of CTA 2009 in its
company tax return for an accounting period beginning on or before but ending
after the relevant closure date, it may further elect in the return for sub-
paragraph  (4)  to apply.

18.4

If it does so—

18.4.a

Part  14A  of CTA 2009 applies further to the election under section  1179B
(1)  of CTA 2009 only in respect of the portion of the accounting period that
falls after the relevant closure date, and

18.4.b

the relevant existing regime applies in respect of the portion of the
accounting period that falls on or before that date.

18.5

Where, by virtue of this paragraph, different Parts of CTA 2009 apply in
respect of different portions of an accounting period, the portions are to be
treated as separate accounting periods for the purposes of—

18.5.a

those Parts, and

18.5.b

paragraphs  19  to  24  (but not for other corporation tax purposes).

18.6

For the purposes of this paragraph—

18.6.a

the “ relevant existing regime ” means—

18.6.a.i

Part 15 of CTA 2009, if the election under section  1179B (1)  of that Act
relates to a film;

18.6.a.ii

Part 15A of CTA 2009, if the election under section  1179B (1)  of that Act
relates to a television programme;

18.6.a.iii

Part 15B of CTA 2009, if the election under section  1179B (1)  of that Act
relates to a video game;

18.6.b

references to the application of the relevant existing regime are to its
application in relation to that film, television programme or video game;

18.6.c

the “relevant closure date” is—

18.6.c.i

31 March 2025, in the case of a film or television programme whose principal
photography has not begun, or a video game whose production has not begun, by
the end of that date;

18.6.c.ii

31 March 2027, in any other case.

18.7

Nothing in this paragraph expands the circumstances in which the relevant
existing regime can apply (except by making it apply in respect of a portion
of an accounting period).

###### Productions not moving into new regime

19

19.1

Sub-paragraphs  (2)  and  (3)  apply if, but for this paragraph, Part 15, 15A
or 15B of CTA 2009 would apply to a company in relation to a film, television
programme or video game in respect of an accounting period beginning on or
before but ending after the relevant closure date.

19.2

The company is to be treated for the purposes of the Part in question as if,
at the end of the relevant closure date, it—

19.2.a

ceased the separate trade that it is treated as carrying on under that Part,
and

19.2.b

abandoned its activities in relation to the film, television programme or
video game.

19.3

No election under section  1179B (1)  of CTA 2009 may be made in relation to
the film, television programme or video game.

19.4

The date that is the relevant closure date for the purposes of paragraph  18
is also the relevant closure date for the purposes of this paragraph.

###### Continuity between regimes: taxation as separate trade

20

20.1

Sub-paragraphs  (2)  to  (5)  apply if—

20.1.a

a company is treated as carrying on a separate trade under Part 15, 15A or 15B
of CTA 2009 in an accounting period (“AP1”),

20.1.b

in the next accounting period (“AP2”), the company is treated as carrying on a
separate trade under Part  14A  of CTA 2009, and

20.1.c

both trades relate to the same film, television programme or video game.

20.2

The separate trade that the company is treated as carrying on in AP2 is to be
treated as a continuation of the separate trade that the company was treated
as carrying on in AP1.

20.3

Accordingly, section  1179BA (2)  of CTA 2009 does not apply.

20.4

If a new period of account does not begin when AP2 begins, a new period of
account is to be treated as beginning at that time for the purposes of—

20.4.a

section 1189, 1216BA or 1217BA of CTA 2009 (as it applies in relation to AP1),
and

20.4.b

section  1179BB  of CTA 2009 (as it applies in relation to AP2).

20.5

For the purposes of section  1179BB (3)  of CTA 2009 as it applies in relation
to AP2, the references to the corresponding amounts for the previous period
are to be read as references to the corresponding amounts brought into account
under section 1189, 1216BA or 1217BA of that Act for AP1.

###### Continuity between regimes: calculation of expenditure credit

21

21.1

Sub-paragraphs  (3)  and  (4)  apply if—

21.1.a

a company is entitled to audiovisual expenditure credit or video game
expenditure credit under Chapter  3  of Part  14A  of CTA 2009 for an
accounting period, and

21.1.b

in respect of an earlier accounting period, the company was entitled to, and
claimed—

21.1.b.i

film tax relief under Chapter 3 of Part 15 of CTA 2009,

21.1.b.ii

television tax relief under Chapter 3 of Part 15A of that Act, or

21.1.b.iii

video games tax relief under Chapter 3 of Part 15 of that Act, and

21.1.c

both entitlements relate to the same film, television programme or video game.

21.2

In those sub-paragraphs, the earliest accounting period within sub-paragraph
(1) (a)  is “AP2” and the latest accounting period within sub-paragraph  (1)
(b)  is “AP1”.

21.3

For the purposes of step 1 in section  1179CA (1)  of CTA 2009 as it applies
in relation to AP2, the reference to relevant global expenditure includes the
amount that was “ qualifying expenditure incurred to date ” for the purposes
of section 1200(1) or (2), 1216CG(1) or (2) or 1217CG(1) or (2) of that Act in
relation to AP1.

21.4

For the purposes of step 4 in section  1179CA (1)  of CTA 2009 as it applies
in relation to AP2, the reference to the company’s qualifying expenditure to
date in the accounting period for which it was last entitled to, and claimed,
an expenditure credit is to be read as a reference to the amount taken as ‘E’
for the purposes of section 1200(1) or (2), 1216CG(1) or (2) or 1217CG(1) or
(2) of that Act in relation to AP1.

###### Continuity between regimes: British certification

22

22.1

Regulations made before the passing of this Act under a provision of CTA 2009
specified in the first column of the following table—

22.1.a

have effect for the purposes of  Part 14A  of CTA 2009 as if made under the
provision of that Part specified in the corresponding entry in the second
column of the table, and

22.1.b

are for those purposes to be read subject to any necessary modifications.

  TABLE       Existing provision in Part 15A or 15B of CTA 2009 New provision
in  Part 14A  of CTA 2009   Section 1216CB(2) Section  1179DK (1) Section
1216CC(7) Section  1179DL (7) Section 1217CB(2) Section  1179FD (1) Section
1217CC(7) Section  1179FE (7)

22.2

A certificate issued under section 1216CD or 1217CD of CTA 2009 continues to
have effect for the purposes of Part  14A  of that Act as if it were a
certificate issued under section  1179DM  or (as the case may be)  1179FF  in
that Part.

22.3

In relation to such a certificate, the references to revocation or ceasing to
be in force in sections 1216EA and 1217EA of CTA 2009 (as they continue to
apply in relation to accounting periods beginning before 1 April 2027) include
revocation or ceasing to be in force under section  1179DM  or (as the case
may be)  1179FF  of that Act.

22.4

The repeal of Parts 15, 15A and 15B of CTA 2009 does not affect the
requirement in section 1213(3), 1216EA(3) or 1217EA(3) of that Act so far as
it relates to entitlements in accounting periods beginning before 1 April 2027
(even if the “completion period” begins on or after that date).

22.5

In sections 1216EA(3) and (5) and 1217EA(3) and (5) of CTA 2009 (as they
continue to apply in relation to accounting periods beginning before 1 April
2027), the references to a final certificate include reference to a final
certificate issued under section  1179DM  or (as the case may be)  1179FF  of
that Act.

###### Continuity between regimes: UK expenditure (films and television programmes)

23

The repeal of Parts 15 and 15A of CTA 2009 does not affect the requirement in
section 1214(3) or 1216EB(3) of that Act, so far as it relates to entitlements
in accounting periods beginning before 1 April 2027 (even if the “completion
period” begins on or after that date).

###### Transition of video games from European expenditure condition to UK expenditure condition

24

24.1

Sub-paragraphs  (3)  and  (4)  apply if—

24.1.a

a company makes an election under section  1179B (1)  in relation to a video
game in its company tax return for an accounting period (“the opt-in period”),

24.1.b

no earlier accounting period was the completion period, and

24.1.c

in an earlier accounting period, the company was entitled to, and claimed,
special video games relief in respect of that video game.

24.2

In this paragraph, “special video games relief” and “completion period” have
the meanings given by section 1217E(1) of CTA 2009.

24.3

Subsections (3) and (4) of section 1217EB of CTA 2009 apply as if the video
game had been completed at the end of the accounting period preceding the opt-
in period (and, accordingly, as if that period were the completion period).

24.4

In section  1179FH  of CTA 2009 as it applies in relation to the video game,
the references to core expenditure are to be read as limited to core
expenditure incurred in or after the opt-in period.

###### Transfer of terminal losses between productions in existing and new regimes

25

25.1

In section  1179BG (1) (a)  of CTA 2009, the reference to the separate
production trade is to be read as including reference to a separate trade
carried on under Part 15, 15A or 15B of CTA 2009.

25.2

Section  1179BG (1) (d)  of CTA 2009 is to be taken as satisfied where—

25.2.a

the ceased trade was carried on under Part 15 or 15A of CTA 2009 and the other
trade relates to a film or television programme, or

25.2.b

the ceased trade was carried on under Part 15B of CTA 2009 and the other trade
relates to a video game.

25.3

Paragraphs (a) and (b) of section 1211(1) of CTA 2009 are to be taken as
satisfied where a company ceases to carry on a separate production trade under
Part  14A  of CTA 2009 in relation to a film (and that company and that trade
are respectively “company A” and “trade X” in the resulting application of
section 1211).

25.4

Paragraphs (a) and (b) of section 1216DC(1) of CTA 2009 are to be taken as
satisfied where a company ceases to carry on a separate production trade under
Part  14A  of CTA 2009 in relation to a television programme (and that company
and that trade are respectively “company A” and “trade X” in the resulting
application of section 1216DC).

25.5

Paragraphs (a) and (b) of section 1217DC(1) of CTA 2009 are to be taken as
satisfied where a company ceases to carry on a separate production trade under
Part  14A  of CTA 2009 in relation to a video game (and that company and that
trade are respectively “company A” and “trade X” in the resulting application
of section 1217DC).

###### Profit element of non-arm's-length payments to connected parties not to qualify for relief

7

7.1

Section 1217JA (expenditure on theatrical productions that qualifies for
relief) is amended as follows.

7.2

In subsection (1)(b), after “(2)” insert  “or  (3) ” .

7.3

After subsection (2) insert—

7.3.3

Expenditure is excluded to the extent that it represents connected party
profit, unless subsection  (5)  applies.

7.3.4

For the purposes of subsection  (3) , expenditure represents connected party
profit—

7.3.4.a

if it is a payment to a person (“ C ”) in exchange for something supplied by
that person,

7.3.4.b

if the company is connected with C, and

7.3.4.c

if, and to the extent that, the amount of the payment exceeds the expenditure
incurred by C in supplying that thing.

7.3.5

This subsection applies if the amount of the payment is no more than would
have been the case had the transaction been entered into at arm’s length.

7.3.6

A transaction would have been entered into “at arm’s length” if it made “the
arm’s length provision” within the meaning of Part 4 of TIOPA 2010 (and for
this purpose any limitation on the application of that Part is to be
disregarded).

7.3.7

Subsections  (8)  and  (9)  apply if—

7.3.7.a

the supply by C to the production company is one of a sequence of transactions
in which the thing supplied has been supplied by one person to another, and

7.3.7.b

either—

7.3.7.b.i

each transacting party in the sequence is connected to at least one other
transacting party in the sequence, or

7.3.7.b.ii

each transaction in the sequence is entered into in furtherance of a single
scheme or arrangement (of whatever kind, and whether or not legally
enforceable).

7.3.8

The reference to C in subsection  (4) (c)  is to be read as a reference to the
supplier in the first transaction in the sequence.

7.3.9

The reference to the transaction in subsection  (5)  is to be read as
including each transaction in the sequence.

7.3.10

In this section, “ payment ” includes any transfer of value.

7.4

Those amendments have effect in relation to expenditure incurred on or after 1
April 2024.

###### Amendment of R&D exclusion

8

8.1

8.1.a

8.1.b

###### Restriction where tax liabilities outstanding: meaning of “payment period”

9

In section 1217KB (payment in respect of theatre tax credit), after subsection

For the purposes of subsection (4), a “payment period” is—

9.4A.a

9.4A.a.i

9.4A.a.ii

insurance contributions to an officer of Revenue and Customs;

9.4A.b

in relation to section 966 of ITA 2007, a period for which the company is
required to make a return as described in section 969(1)(b) of that Act.

###### Relief not to be available for companies in insolvency

10

10.1

After section 1217KC insert—

############ Companies in insolvency

############# No claim if company in administration or liquidation

10.1.1217KD

10.1.1217KD.1

A company may not make a claim under section 1217H or section 1217K at a time
when it is in administration or liquidation.

10.1.1217KD.2

For the purposes of this section, a company is in administration if—

10.1.1217KD.2.a

it is in administration under Part 2 of the Insolvency Act 1986 or Part 3 of
the Insolvency (Northern Ireland) Order 1989 ( S.I. 1989/2405 (N.I. 19)) , or

10.1.1217KD.2.b

a corresponding situation under the law of a country or territory outside the
United Kingdom exists in relation to the company.

10.1.1217KD.3

For the purposes of this section, a company is in liquidation if—

10.1.1217KD.3.a

it is in liquidation within the meaning of section 247 of that Act or Article
6 of that Order, or

10.1.1217KD.3.b

a corresponding situation under the law of a country or territory outside the
United Kingdom exists in relation to the company.

10.2

That amendment has effect in relation to claims made on or after 1 April 2024.

##### Changes from European to UK expenditure: transitional provision

###### Transitional provision in relation to paragraph 

11

11.1

This paragraph makes transitional provision in connection with paragraph  5 .

11.2

The amendments made by that paragraph do not apply in relation to a theatrical
production if—

11.2.a

it has entered production before 1 April 2024, and

11.2.b

the separate theatrical trade in respect of it ceases before 1 April 2025.

11.3

Sub-paragraph  (4)  applies if—

11.3.a

a theatrical production has entered production before 1 April 2024,

11.3.b

the separate theatrical trade in respect of the production continues on or
after 1 April 2025,

11.3.c

the production company’s company tax return for the first accounting period
that ends on or after 1 April 2025 is accompanied by a statement of the amount
of the core expenditure on the theatrical production incurred before 1 April
2025 that is European expenditure, and

11.3.d

that statement shows that, in respect of core expenditure incurred before 1
April 2025, the European expenditure condition is met.

11.4

The company’s entitlement to—

11.4.a

an additional deduction under section 1217H of CTA 2009, or

11.4.b

a tax credit under section 1217K of that Act,

is unaffected by a failure to meet the UK expenditure condition so far as the
entitlement derives from expenditure incurred before 1 April 2025.

11.5

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (4) , an entitlement to a tax credit under
section 1217H of CTA 2009 derives from expenditure incurred before 1 April
2025 to the extent that it would arise if only costs incurred and income
received before that date were taken into account in calculating the
surrenderable loss of the company for the purposes of section 1217KA of that
Act.

11.6

Sub-paragraph  (7)  applies in relation to a theatrical production in respect
of which the separate theatrical trade continues on or after 1 April 2025.

11.7

The reference in section 1217NA(1) of CTA 2009, as amended by paragraph  5 ,
to a statement having been made under section 1217N(2) of that Act includes
reference to a statement having been made in relation to the European
expenditure condition under that provision before it was amended by paragraph
5 .

11.8

But the application of section 1217NA(1) of CTA 2009 as so amended is subject
to sub-paragraph  (4)  (where that sub-paragraph applies).

11.9

In this paragraph—

      “ theatrical production ”, “ separate theatrical trade ”, “ production
company ” and “ core expenditure ” have the same meanings as in Part 15C of
CTA 2009;           “ UK expenditure condition ” has the same meaning as in
that Part after the amendments made by paragraph  5 ;           “ European
expenditure ” and “European expenditure condition” have the same meanings as
in that Part before the amendments made by paragraph  5 .

11.10

For the purposes of this paragraph, a theatrical production “enters
production” when core expenditure is first incurred on it.

###### Transitional provision in relation to paragraph 

12

12.1

This paragraph makes transitional provision in relation to paragraph  6 .

12.2

The amendments made by that paragraph have effect in relation to accounting
periods ending on or after 1 April 2024.

12.3

Sub-paragraph  (4)  applies in a case where expenditure incurred before 1
April 2024 is to be taken into account as qualifying expenditure for the
purposes of section 1217J of CTA 2009 (amount of relief for theatrical
production).

12.4

The references in subsections (2) and (3) of that section (as amended by
paragraph  6 ) to so much of the qualifying expenditure incurred to date as is
UK expenditure are to be read as references to so much of the qualifying
expenditure incurred to date as—

12.4.a

has been incurred before 1 April 2024 and is European expenditure, or

12.4.b

has been incurred on or after that date and is UK expenditure.

12.5

But if the theatrical production in relation to which sub-paragraph  (4)
applies has entered production before 1 April 2024, the production company may
elect for that sub-paragraph to have effect in relation to that production as
if “2025” were substituted for  “2024” .

12.6

In this paragraph—

      “ theatrical production ”, “ production company ” and “ core expenditure
” have the same meanings as in Part 15C of CTA 2009;           “ UK
expenditure ” has the same meaning as in that Part after the amendments made
by paragraph  5 ;           “ European expenditure ” has the same meaning as
in that Part before the amendments made by paragraph  5 .

12.7

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (5) , a theatrical production “enters
production” when core expenditure is first incurred on it.

###### Profit element of non-arm's-length payments to connected parties not to qualify for relief

7

7.1

Section 1217RF (expenditure that qualifies for orchestra tax relief) is
amended as follows.

7.2

In subsection (1)—

7.2.a

omit the “and” after paragraph (a);

7.2.b

after paragraph (b) insert

, and

7.2.b.c

is not excluded by subsection  (3) .

7.3

After subsection (2) insert—

7.3.3

Expenditure is excluded to the extent that it represents connected party
profit, unless subsection  (5)  applies.

7.3.4

For the purposes of subsection  (3) , expenditure represents connected party
profit—

7.3.4.a

if it is a payment to a person (“ C ”) in exchange for something supplied,
transferred or done by that person,

7.3.4.b

if the company is connected with C, and

7.3.4.c

if, and to the extent that, the amount of the payment exceeds the expenditure
incurred by C in supplying, transferring or doing that thing.

7.3.5

This subsection applies if the amount of the payment is no more than would
have been the case had the transaction been entered into at arm’s length.

7.3.6

A transaction would have been entered into “at arm’s length” if it made “the
arm’s length provision” within the meaning of Part 4 of TIOPA 2010 (and for
this purpose any limitation on the application of that Part is to be
disregarded).

7.3.7

Subsections  (8)  and  (9)  apply if—

7.3.7.a

the supply by C to the company is one of a sequence of transactions in which
the thing supplied has been supplied by one person to another, and

7.3.7.b

either—

7.3.7.b.i

each transacting party in the sequence is connected to at least one other
transacting party in the sequence, or

7.3.7.b.ii

each transaction in the sequence is entered into in furtherance of a single
scheme or arrangement (of whatever kind, and whether or not legally
enforceable).

7.3.8

The reference to C in subsection  (4) (c)  is to be read as a reference to the
supplier in the first transaction in the sequence.

7.3.9

The reference to the transaction in subsection  (5)  is to be read as
including each transaction in the sequence.

7.3.10

In this section, “ payment ” includes any transfer of value.

7.4

Those amendments have effect in relation to expenditure incurred on or after 1
April 2024.

############ Companies in insolvency

############# No claim if company in administration or liquidation

For the purposes of this section, a company is in administration if—

10.1.1217RKA.2.a

it is in liquidation within the meaning of section 247 of that Act or Article
6 of that Order, or

10.1.1217RKA.3.b

a corresponding situation under the law of a country or territory outside the
United Kingdom exists in relation to the company.

11

11.1

This paragraph makes transitional provision in relation to paragraph  5 .

11.2

The amendments made by that paragraph have effect in relation to accounting
periods ending on or after 1 April 2024.

11.3

Sub-paragraph  (4)  applies in a case where expenditure incurred before 1
April 2024 is to be taken into account as qualifying expenditure for the
purposes of section 1218ZCF of CTA 2009 (amount of relief for museum or
gallery exhibition).

11.4

The references in subsections (2) and (3) of that section (as amended by
paragraph  5 ) to so much of the qualifying expenditure incurred to date as is
UK expenditure are to be read as references to so much of the qualifying
expenditure incurred to date as—

11.4.a

has been incurred before 1 April 2024 and is European expenditure, or

11.4.b

has been incurred on or after that date and is UK expenditure.

11.5

But if the exhibition in relation to which sub-paragraph  (4)  applies has
entered production before 1 April 2024, the production company may elect for
that sub-paragraph to have effect in relation to that exhibition as if “2025”
were substituted for  “2024” .

11.6

In this paragraph—

      “ exhibition ”, “ production company ” and “ core expenditure ” have the
same meanings as in Part 15E of CTA 2009;           “ UK expenditure ” has the
same meaning as in that Part after the amendments made by paragraph  4 ;
“ European expenditure ” has the same meanings as in that Part before the
amendments made by paragraph  4 .

11.7

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (5) , an exhibition “enters production”
when core expenditure is first incurred on it.

##### Time limit for claims

2

2.1

2.1.a

claim relates, in any other case.

after 1 April 2024.

##### Amendment of CTA 2010

1

##### CoACS to be institutional investors

2

In Section 528 (conditions for company), in subsection (4A), after paragraph
(b) insert—

2.ba

a person acting on behalf of an authorised contractual scheme (within the
meaning given by section 237(3) of FISMA 2000) which is a co-ownership scheme
(within the meaning given by section 235A of that Act) that meets the genuine
diversity of ownership condition or the non-close condition;

.

##### Non-close condition

3

3.1

Section 528 is amended as follows.

3.2

In subsection (4)—

3.2.a

in the words before paragraph (a), after “company” insert  “meets the non-
close condition.” , and

3.2.b

omit paragraphs (a) and (b).

3.3

After subsection (4B) insert—

3.3.4C

The non-close condition is met—

3.3.4C.a

in relation to a company, if—

3.3.4C.a.i

it is not a close company, or

3.3.4C.a.ii

it is a close company but only because it has an institutional investor as a
direct or indirect participator, and

3.3.4C.b

in relation to a person or scheme other than a company, if it would fall
within paragraph (a)(i) or (ii) if—

3.3.4C.b.i

the person’s business or the scheme were a company, and

3.3.4C.b.ii

the interests of persons in the business or scheme were shares in the company.

3.4

In subsection (5), for “subsection (4)(a)” substitute  “determining whether
the non-close condition is met” .

3.5

After subsection (5A) (as inserted by  paragraph 4 ) insert—

3.5.5B

For the purposes of subsection (4C)(a)(ii)—

3.5.5B.a

a person is a “direct participator” if the person is a participator for the
purposes of Part 10 of CTA 2010 (see section 454), and

3.5.5B.b

a person is an “indirect” participator in a company if the person has a share
or interest in the capital or income of the company through another body
corporate or other bodies corporate.

3.5.5C

In determining whether a person is an indirect participator—

3.5.5C.a

reference to having a share or interest in the capital or income of a company
through a body corporate is to be read in accordance with sub-paragraphs (9)
and (10) of paragraph 46 of Schedule 5AAA to TCGA 1992 (meaning of direct or
indirect participator), and

3.5.5C.b

a person is regarded for the purposes of those sub-paragraphs, and for the
purposes of subsection  (5B) (b)  of this section, as having a share or
interest in the capital or income of a company if the person would be a
participator in the company as a result of section 454(2) of CTA 2010.

3.6

Section 528 has effect, and is to be deemed always to have had effect, with
the amendments made by  this paragraph .

##### Paragraph 4: transitional provision

5

5.1

Sub-paragraph (2)  applies where—

5.1.a

immediately before the day on which this Act is passed, a company that is a
company UK REIT or the principal member of a group UK REIT, met the conditions
in section 528 of CTA 2010, and

5.1.b

the company ceases to meet one or more of those conditions on that day as a
result of one or more persons ceasing to be regarded as institutional
investors as a result of the amendments made by  paragraph 4 .

5.2

Part 12 of CTA 2010 has effect in relation to such a person for the purposes
of determining whether the company meets those conditions as if the amendments
made by  paragraph 4  had not been made for so long as the person’s interest
in the company as a proportion of all interests in the company—

5.2.a

does not increase as a result of the acquisition by the person of further
interests in the company, and

5.2.b

continuously remains relevant to the question of whether those conditions are
met.

5.3

Sub-paragraph (4)  applies where—

5.3.a

immediately before the day on which this Act is passed, a collective
investment vehicle, or a company that is not a collective investment vehicle,
(“the reliant entity”) relied on its having a qualifying investor as a direct
or indirect participator for the purpose of any provision of Schedule 5AAA to
TCGA 1992 (“a qualifying purpose”), and

5.3.b

the qualifying investor (“the former qualifying investor”) ceased to be a
qualifying investor a result of the amendments made by  paragraph 4 .

5.4

That Schedule has effect in relation to the former qualifying investor for a
qualifying purpose as if the amendments made by  paragraph 4  had not been
made for so long as—

5.4.a

the investor’s interest in the reliant entity as a proportion of all interests
in the entity does not increase as a result of the acquisition by the investor
of further interests in the reliant entity, and

5.4.b

the investor being a direct or indirect participator in the reliant entity
continuously remains relevant for at least one qualifying purpose.

5.5

Sub-paragraph (6)  applies when determining whether a collective investment
scheme constituted before the day on which this Act is passed meets the
genuine diversity of ownership condition for the purposes of any of paragraphs
(a) to (c) of section 528(4A).

5.6

Regulation 75(2) of the Offshore Funds (Tax) Regulations 2009 (including as it
applies for the purposes of regulation 75(5) of those Regulations) has effect,
for those purposes, as if it referred to a statement prepared by the manager
of the scheme (instead of the documents referred to in that paragraph) which—

5.6.a

is available to HMRC,

5.6.b

specifies the intended categories of investor when the scheme was marketed,

5.6.c

confirms that the interests in the scheme were made widely available, and

5.6.d

confirms that interests in the scheme were marketed and made available in
accordance with the requirements of regulation 75(4)(a) of those Regulations
(and that provision is to be read accordingly).

##### Qualifying companies to include companies managing qualifying ships

2

2.1

In paragraph 16 (qualifying companies and groups), in sub-paragraph (1)(b),
after “operates” insert  “or manages” .

2.2

After paragraph 18 insert—

########### Meaning of managing a qualifying ship

2.2.18A

A company is regarded for the purposes of this Schedule as managing a
qualifying ship if—

2.2.18A.a

the ship is a qualifying ship operated by a tonnage tax company (“ the
operator ”),

2.2.18A.b

the company carries on activities in relation to the ship that would be
tonnage tax activities of the operator if the operator carried them on, and

2.2.18A.c

those activities as carried on by the company represent a significant
contribution to the operation of the ship.

1,000 tons £0.60 £0.12 For each 100 tons between 1,000 and 10,000 tons £0.45
£0.09 For each 100 tons between 10,000 and 25,000 tons £0.30 £0.06 For each
100 tons above 25,000 tons £0.15 £0.03

.

########### Introduction

13.4.A1

13.4.A1.1

This Schedule applies for the purposes of sections 232 and 236.

13.4.A1.2.a

subsequent paragraphs give the meaning of expressions used in paragraph  A2 .

########### The benefit crystallisation events

13.4.A2

13.4.A2.1

Benefit crystallisation event 1 occurs in relation to an individual if sums or
assets held for the purposes of a money purchase arrangement under any of the
relevant pension schemes are designated as available for the payment of
drawdown pension to the individual.

13.4.A2.2

Benefit crystallisation event 2 occurs in relation to an individual if the
individual becomes entitled to a scheme pension under any of the relevant
pension schemes.

13.4.A2.3

Benefit crystallisation event 3 occurs in relation to an individual if the
individual, having become so entitled, becomes entitled to payment of the
scheme pension, otherwise than in excepted circumstances, at an increased
annual rate which—

13.4.A2.3.a

exceeds the threshold annual rate, and

13.4.A2.3.b

exceeds by more than the permitted margin the rate at which it was payable on
the day on which the individual became entitled to it.

13.4.A2.4

Benefit crystallisation event 4 occurs in relation to an individual if the
individual becomes entitled to a lifetime annuity purchased under a money
purchase arrangement under any of the relevant pension schemes.

13.4.A2.5

Benefit crystallisation event 6 occurs in relation to an individual if the
individual becomes entitled to a relevant lump sum under any of the relevant
pension schemes.

After section 278 (market value) insert—

########## Disqualifying pension credits

23.278A

23.278A.1

For the purposes of this Part, a pension credit is “disqualifying” if, when
the member becomes entitled to it, the person subject to the corresponding
pension debit has an actual (rather than a prospective) right to payment of a
pension under the relevant arrangement.

23.278A.2

The “relevant arrangement” is the arrangement to which the pension sharing
order, or provision by virtue of which the member becomes entitled to the
pension credit, relates.

########## Annuities and scheme pensions: meaning of “related to”

23.278B

23.278B.1

For the purposes of this Part, a dependants' annuity is “related to” a
lifetime annuity payable to a member of a registered pension scheme if—

23.278B.1.a

they are purchased either in the form of a joint life annuity or separately in
circumstances in which the day on which the one is purchased is no earlier
than seven days before, and no later than seven days after, the day on which
the other is purchased, and

23.278B.1.b

the dependants’ annuity will be payable to a dependant of the member.

23.278B.2

For the purposes of this Part, a nominees’ annuity is “related to” a lifetime
annuity payable to a member of a registered pension scheme if—

23.278B.2.a

they are purchased either in the form of a joint life annuity or separately in
circumstances in which the day on which the one is purchased is no earlier
than seven days before, and no later than seven days after, the day on which
the other is purchased, and

23.278B.2.b

the nominees’ annuity will be payable to a nominee of the member.

23.278B.3

For the purposes of this Part, a dependants’ scheme pension is “related to” a
scheme pension payable to a member of a registered pension scheme if—

23.278B.3.a

the day on which one is purchased or sums or assets are applied for its
provision is no earlier than seven days before, and no later than seven days
after, the day on which the other is purchased or sums or assets are applied
for its provision, and

23.278B.3.b

the dependants’ scheme pension will be payable to a dependant of the member.

26.5

For paragraph 3 (definition of “the applicable amount”) substitute—

26.5.2A

26.5.2A.1

This paragraph defines “ the applicable amount ” in relation to a relevant
pension in a case in which the relevant pension is income withdrawal.

26.5.2A.2

The applicable amount is one third of the scheme pension capital value.

26.5.2A.3

The scheme pension capital value is (subject to sub-paragraph  (4) ) the
aggregate of—

26.5.2A.3.a

the sums designated as available for the payment of drawdown pension on that
occasion, and

26.5.2A.3.b

the market value of the assets so designated.

26.5.2A.4

There is to be deducted from the amount determined under sub-paragraph  (3)
so much (if any) of the sums and assets designated as mentioned in sub-
paragraph  (3) (a)  or  (b)  as represent rights attributable to a
disqualifying pension credit.

26.5.2B

26.5.2B.1

This paragraph defines “ the applicable amount ” in relation to a relevant
pension in a case in which the relevant pension is a lifetime annuity.

26.5.2B.2

The applicable amount is one third of the annuity purchase price.

26.5.2B.3

The annuity purchase price is (subject to sub-paragraph  (4) ) the aggregate
of—

26.5.2B.3.a

such of the sums held for the purposes of the pension scheme, and

26.5.2B.3.b

the market value of such of the assets held for the purposes of the pension
scheme,

as are applied in (or in connection with) the purchase of the lifetime annuity
and any related dependants’ annuity and any related nominees’ annuity.

26.5.2B.4

There is to be deducted from the amount determined under sub-paragraph  (3) —

26.5.2B.4.a

if the sums or assets applied in (or in connection with) the purchase of the
annuity or any related dependants’ annuity or any related nominees’ annuity
consist of, or include, sums or assets representing the whole or part of the
member’s drawdown pension fund or of the member's flexi-access drawdown fund,
the aggregate of those sums and the market value of those assets, and

26.5.2B.4.b

in any case, so much (if any) of the sums or assets applied in (or in
connection with) the purchase of the annuity or any related dependants’
annuity or any related nominees’ annuity as represents rights which are
attributable to a disqualifying pension credit.

26.5.2C

26.5.2C.1

This paragraph defines “ the applicable amount ” in relation to a relevant
pension in a case in which the relevant pension is—

26.5.2C.1.a

a scheme pension under a defined benefits arrangement, or

26.5.2C.1.b

a collective money purchase arrangement.

26.5.2C.2

The applicable amount is (subject to sub-paragraph  (3) )—

      A   +   (   B   ×   C   )   -   D     4           where—         A is
the amount of the lump sum;           B is the relevant revaluation factor
(see section 276);           C is the amount of the pension which will be
payable to the member in the period of 12 months beginning with the day on
which the member becomes entitled to the pension (assuming that it remains
payable throughout that period at the rate at which it is payable on that
day);           D is so much (if any) of A or C as represents rights which are
attributable to a disqualifying pension credit.

26.5.2C.3

In determining C for the purposes of subsection  (2)  in a case in which the
pension is under a public service pension scheme, any abatement of the pension
is to be left out of account.

26.5.2D

26.5.2D.1

This paragraph defines “ the applicable amount ” in relation to a relevant
pension in a case in which the relevant pension is a scheme pension under a
money purchase arrangement that is not a collective money purchase
arrangement.

26.5.2D.2

The applicable amount is one third of the scheme pension purchase price.

26.5.2D.3

The scheme pension purchase price is (subject to sub-paragraph  (4) ) the
aggregate of—

26.5.2D.3.a

such of the sums held for the purposes of the pension scheme, and

26.5.2D.3.b

the market value of such of the assets held for the purposes of the pension
scheme,

as are applied in (or in connection with) the purchase or provision of the
scheme pension and any related dependants’ scheme pension.

26.5.2D.4

There is to be deducted from the amount determined under sub-paragraph  (3) —

26.5.2D.4.a

if the scheme pension is funded (in whole or in part) by the application of
sums or assets representing the whole or part of the member’s drawdown pension
fund or of the member’s flexi-access drawdown fund, the aggregate of those
sums and the market value of those assets, and

26.5.2D.4.b

in any case, so much (if any) of the sums and assets referred to in sub-
paragraph  (3) (a)  and  (b)  as represent rights which are attributable to a
disqualifying pension credit.

26.8.3B

26.8.3B.1

Sub-paragraph  (2)  applies if—

26.8.3B.1.a

26.8.3B.2.b

26.8.3B.3.b

26.8.3B.4

26.8.3B.4.b

############ Pension commencement excess lump sum

26.9.3C

26.9.3C.1

For the purposes of this Part a lump sum is a pension commencement excess lump
sum if—

26.9.3C.1.a

the member becomes entitled to it in connection with becoming entitled to a
relevant pension (or dies after becoming entitled to it but before becoming
entitled to the relevant pension in connection with which it was anticipated
that the member would become entitled to it);

26.9.3C.1.b

it is paid when none of the member’s lump sum allowance is available (see
paragraph  12A );

26.9.3C.1.c

it is paid within the period beginning six months before, and ending one year
after, the day on which the member becomes entitled to it;

26.9.3C.1.d

it does not reduce the rate of payment of any pension to which the member has
become (actually) entitled, or extinguish the member’s entitlement to payment
of any such pension;

26.9.3C.1.e

it is paid when the member has reached normal minimum pension age (or the ill-
health condition is met); and

26.9.3C.1.f

it is not an excluded lump sum (see  sub-paragraph (4) ).

26.9.3C.2

But if a lump sum falling within sub-paragraph (1) exceeds the permitted
maximum, the excess is not a pension commencement excess lump sum.

26.9.3C.3

In this paragraph “ the permitted maximum ”, in relation to a lump sum, means—

  (   A   ×   4   )   -   B         where—         “ A ” is the applicable
amount in relation to the relevant pension (see paragraphs  2A  to  2D );
“ B ” is the amount of the member’s lump sum and death benefit allowance that
is available on the payment of the lump sum (see paragraph  12A ).

26.9.3C.4

A lump sum is an “excluded lump sum” if—

26.9.3C.4.a

it would, apart from this paragraph, be permitted to be paid under the lump
sum rule in section 166, or

26.9.3C.4.b

the pension in connection with which the member becomes entitled to it is a
CMP-derived drawdown pension.

26.9.3C.5

In determining for the purposes of this paragraph—

26.9.3C.5.a

whether any of a member’s lump sum allowance is available on the payment of a
lump sum, or

26.9.3C.5.b

the amount of a member’s lump sum and death benefit allowance that is
available on the payment of a lump sum,

the member is treated as having already become entitled to any pension
commencement lump sum that is paid to the member in connection with becoming
entitled to the relevant pension.
