41

For Chapter 15A substitute—

########## Lump sums under registered pension schemes

########### Introduction

############ Introduction

41.637

41.637.1

This Chapter makes provision about the income tax treatment of authorised lump
sums and authorised lump sum death benefits.

41.637.2

In this Chapter—

41.637.2.a

“ authorised lump sum ” means a lump sum permitted by the lump sum rule in
section 166 of FA 2004 to be paid by a registered pension scheme to a member
of the scheme;

41.637.2.b

“ authorised lump sum death benefit ” means a lump sum death benefit permitted
by the lump sum death benefit rule in section 168 of that Act to be paid by a
registered pension scheme in respect of a member of the scheme.

41.637.3

Expressions used in this Chapter and Part 4 of FA 2004 (pensions etc) have the
same meaning in this Chapter as in that Part.

########### Tax treatment of authorised lump sums

############ Pension commencement lump sums

41.637A

No liability to income tax arises on a pension commencement lump sum paid
under a registered pension scheme.

############ Pension commencement excess lump sums

41.637B

A person to whom a pension commencement excess lump sum is paid under a
registered pension scheme is treated as having taxable pension income for the
tax year in which the payment is made equal to the amount of the lump sum.

############ Serious ill-health lump sums

41.637C

41.637C.1

Subject to subsections  (2)  and  (4) , no liability to income tax arises on a
serious ill-health lump sum paid under a registered pension scheme.

41.637C.2

If—

41.637C.2.a

a serious ill-health lump sum is paid under a registered pension scheme to a
member who (at the time of the payment) is under 75, and

41.637C.2.b

the lump sum exceeds the permitted maximum,

section 579A (pensions) applies to the excess as it applies to any pension
under a registered pension scheme.

41.637C.3

In subsection  (2)  “ the permitted maximum ”, in relation to a serious ill-
health lump sum paid to a member, means so much of the member’s lump sum and
death benefit allowance as is available immediately before the member becomes
entitled to the lump sum (see section  637S ).

41.637C.4

If a serious ill-health lump sum is paid under a registered pension scheme to
a member who (at the time of the payment) is 75 or over, section 579A
(pensions) applies to the lump sum as it applies to any pension under a
registered pension scheme.

############ Uncrystallised funds pension lump sums

41.637D

41.637D.1

Subject to subsection  (2) , where an uncrystallised funds pension lump sum is
paid under a registered pension scheme—

41.637D.1.a

no liability to income tax arises on 25% of the lump sum, and

41.637D.1.b

section 579A (pensions) applies in relation to the remainder of the lump sum
as it applies to any pension under a registered pension scheme.

41.637D.2

If—

41.637D.2.a

an uncrystallised funds pension lump sum is paid under a registered pension
scheme, and

41.637D.2.b

25% of the lump sum is an amount that exceeds the permitted maximum,

section 579A (pensions) applies to the excess as it applies to any pension
under a registered pension scheme.

41.637D.3

In subsection  (2)  “ the permitted maximum ”, in relation to an
uncrystallised funds pension lump sum paid to a member, means the lower of the
following amounts—

41.637D.3.a

so much of the member’s lump sum allowance as is available immediately before
the member becomes entitled to the lump sum (see section  637Q );

41.637D.3.b

so much of the member’s lump sum and death benefit allowance as is available
immediately before the member becomes entitled to the lump sum (see section
637S ).

############ Short service refund lump sum

41.637E

A short service refund lump paid under a registered pension scheme is subject
to income tax in accordance with section 205 of FA 2004 (charge to tax on
scheme administrator in respect of such a lump sum) but not otherwise.

############ Refund of excess contributions lump sums

41.637F

No liability to income tax arises on a refund of excess contributions lump sum
paid under a registered pension scheme.

############ Trivial commutation lump sums and winding-up lump sums

41.637G

41.637G.1

Subject to subsection (2), a member of a registered pension scheme to whom—

41.637G.1.a

a trivial commutation lump sum, or

41.637G.1.b

a winding-up lump sum,

is paid under the scheme is treated as having taxable pension income for the
tax year in which the payment is made equal to the amount of the lump sum.

41.637G.2

If, immediately before the lump sum is paid, the member has uncrystallised
rights under any one or more arrangements under the pension scheme, the amount
of the taxable pension income is reduced by the tax-free element (if any).

41.637G.3

In subsection  (2)  “ the tax-free element ” means 25% of the value of any
uncrystallised rights extinguished by the lump sum.

41.637G.4

In this section “ uncrystallised rights ” has the same meaning as in section
212 of FA 2004; and the value for the purposes of this section of any
uncrystallised rights is to be calculated in accordance with that section.

########### Tax treatment of authorised lump sum death benefits

############ Defined benefits lump sum death benefits

41.637H

41.637H.1

Subject to subsections  (2)  to  (6) , no liability to income tax arises on a
defined benefits lump sum death benefit paid under a registered pension
scheme.

41.637H.2

If—

41.637H.2.a

a defined benefits lump sum death benefit under a registered pension scheme is
paid in respect of a member who, on death, is under 75,

41.637H.2.b

the lump sum is paid before the end of the relevant two year period, and

41.637H.2.c

the lump sum exceeds the permitted maximum,

section 579A (pensions) applies to the excess as it applies to any pension
under a registered pension scheme.

41.637H.3

If—

41.637H.3.a

a defined benefits lump sum death benefit under a registered pension scheme is
paid in respect of a member who, on death, is under 75,

41.637H.3.b

the lump sum is not paid before the end of the relevant two year period, and

41.637H.3.c

the lump sum is paid to a qualifying person,

section 579A (pensions) applies to the lump sum as it applies to any pension
under a registered pension scheme.

41.637H.4

If—

41.637H.4.a

a defined benefits lump sum death benefit under a registered pension scheme is
paid in respect of a member who, on death, is under 75,

41.637H.4.b

the lump sum is not paid before the end of the relevant two year period, and

41.637H.4.c

the lump sum is paid to a non-qualifying person,

the lump sum is subject to income tax under section 206 of FA 2004 (special
lump sum death benefits charge on scheme administrator) but not otherwise.

41.637H.5

If a defined benefits lump sum death benefit under a registered pension scheme
is paid—

41.637H.5.a

in respect of a member who, on death, is 75 or over, and

41.637H.5.b

to a qualifying person,

section 579A (pensions) applies to the lump sum as it applies to any pension
under a registered pension scheme.

41.637H.6

If a defined benefits lump sum death benefit under a registered pension scheme
is paid—

41.637H.6.a

in respect of a member who, on death, is 75 or over, and

41.637H.6.b

to a non-qualifying person,

the lump sum is subject to income tax under section 206 of FA 2004 (special
lump sum death benefits charge on scheme administrator) but not otherwise.

41.637H.7

In this section—

      “ non-qualifying person ” has the same meaning as in section 206 of FA
2004;           “ the permitted maximum ”, in relation to a defined benefits
lump sum death benefit paid in respect of a member, means so much of the
member’s lump sum and death benefit allowance as is available immediately
before the lump sum is paid (see section  637S );           “ qualifying
person ” means a person who is not a non-qualifying person;           “ the
relevant two year period ” means the period of two years beginning with the
day on which the scheme administrator of the scheme first knew of the member’s
death or (if earlier) the day on which the scheme administrator could first
reasonably have been expected to have known of it.

############ Pension protection lump sum death benefits

41.637I

41.637I.1

      “ non-qualifying person ” has the same meaning as in section 206 of FA

lump sum death benefit paid in respect of a member, means so much of the

before the lump sum is paid (see section  637S );           “ qualifying
person ” means a person who is not a non-qualifying person.

############ Flexi-access drawdown lump sum death benefits

41.637M

41.637M.1

Subject to subsections  (2)  to  (6) , no liability to income tax arises on a
flexi-access drawdown lump sum death benefit paid under a registered pension
scheme.

41.637M.2

If—

the lump sum is paid to a qualifying person,

under a registered pension scheme.

41.637M.4

If—

41.637M.4.a

a flexi-access drawdown lump sum death benefit under a registered pension
scheme is paid in respect of a member who, on death, is under 75,

41.637M.4.b

to a non-qualifying person,

41.637M.7

41.637M.7.b

in relation to a flexi-access drawdown lump sum death benefit under paragraph

      “ non-qualifying person ” has the same meaning as in section 206 of FA

reasonably have been expected to have known of it.

############ Trivial commutation lump sum death benefits

41.637N

A person to whom a trivial commutation lump sum death benefit is paid under a
registered pension scheme is treated as having taxable pension income for the
tax year in which the payment is made equal to the amount of the lump sum.

########### Allowances

############ Individual’s lump sum allowance

41.637P

An individual’s “lump sum allowance” is £268,275.

############ Availability of individual’s lump sum allowance

41.637Q

41.637Q.1

This section is about the availability of an individual’s lump sum allowance
on the occurrence of a relevant benefit crystallisation event (“the current
event”).

41.637Q.2

In this section—

41.637Q.2.a

“ relevant benefit crystallisation event ”, in relation to an individual,
means the individual becoming entitled to a relevant lump sum;

41.637Q.2.b

“ relevant lump sum ” means—

41.637Q.2.b.i

a pension commencement lump sum, or

41.637Q.2.b.ii

an uncrystallised funds pension lump sum.

41.637Q.3

If no relevant benefit crystallisation event has occurred in relation to the
individual before the current event, the whole of the individual’s lump sum
allowance is available.

41.637Q.4

Otherwise, the amount of the individual’s lump sum allowance that is available
is—

41.637Q.4.a

so much of that allowance as is left after deducting the previously-used
amount, or

41.637Q.4.b

if none is left after deducting that amount, nil.

41.637Q.5

For this purpose “the previously-used amount” is the aggregate of the non-
taxable amounts in relation to each relevant benefit crystallisation event
that has occurred in relation to the individual before the current event.

41.637Q.6

In subsection  (5)  “ non-taxable amount ”, in relation to a relevant benefit
crystallisation event, means so much (if any) of the relevant lump sum to
which the event relates as is exempt from the charge to income tax by virtue
of any provision of this Chapter.

41.637Q.7

A reference in this section to a relevant benefit crystallisation event is to
a relevant benefit crystallisation event occurring on or after 6 April 2024.

41.637Q.8

For transitional provision under which the amount of an individual’s lump sum
allowance available on the occurrence of a relevant benefit crystallisation
event may be reduced as a result of events occurring before 6 April 2024, see
paragraph 125  of  Schedule 9  to FA 2024.

############ Individual’s lump sum and death benefit allowance

41.637R

An individual’s “lump sum and death benefit allowance” is £1,073,100.

############ Availability of individual’s lump sum and death benefit allowance

41.637S

41.637S.1

This section is about the availability of an individual’s lump sum and death
benefit allowance on the occurrence of a relevant benefit crystallisation
event (“the current event”).

41.637S.2

In this section—

41.637S.2.a

“ relevant benefit crystallisation event ”, in relation to an individual,
means—

41.637S.2.a.i

the individual becoming entitled to a relevant lump sum, or

41.637S.2.a.ii

a person being paid a relevant lump sum death benefit in respect of the
individual;

41.637S.2.b

“ relevant lump sum ” means—

41.637S.2.b.i

a pension commencement lump sum,

41.637S.2.b.ii

a serious ill-health lump sum, or

41.637S.2.b.iii

an uncrystallised funds pension lump sum;

41.637S.2.c

“ relevant lump sum death benefit ” means any authorised lump sum death
benefit other than—

41.637S.2.c.i

a charity lump sum death benefit, or

41.637S.2.c.ii

a trivial commutation lump sum death benefit.

41.637S.3

If no relevant benefit crystallisation event has occurred in relation to the
individual before the current event, the whole of the individual’s lump sum
and death benefit allowance is available.

41.637S.4

Otherwise, the amount of the individual’s lump sum and death benefit allowance
that is available is—

41.637S.4.a

so much of that allowance as is left after deducting the previously-used
amount, or

41.637S.4.b

if none is left after deducting that amount, nil.

41.637S.5

For this purpose “the previously-used amount” is the aggregate of the non-
taxable amounts in relation to each relevant benefit crystallisation event
that has occurred in relation to the individual before the current event.

41.637S.6

In subsection  (5)  “ non-taxable amount ”, in relation to a relevant benefit
crystallisation event, means so much (if any) of the relevant lump sum, or
relevant lump sum death benefit, to which the event relates as is exempt from
the charge to income tax by virtue of any provision of this Chapter.

41.637S.7

Where more than one relevant benefit crystallisation event within  subsection
(2) (a) (i)  occurs in relation to an individual on the same day, it is for
the individual to decide the order in which they are to be treated as
occurring for the purposes of this section.

41.637S.8

Where more than one relevant benefit crystallisation event within  subsection
(2) (a) (ii)  occurs in relation to an individual, they are to be treated for
the purposes of this section as occurring—

41.637S.8.a

immediately before the individual’s death,

41.637S.8.b

immediately after any pension commencement lump sum to which the individual
becomes entitled immediately before death by virtue of section 166(2) of FA
2004 (lump sum rule), and

41.637S.8.c

in such order as may be decided by the individual’s personal representatives.

41.637S.9

A reference in this section to a relevant benefit crystallisation event is to
a relevant benefit crystallisation event occurring on or after 6 April 2024.

41.637S.10

For transitional provision under which the amount of an individual’s lump sum
and death benefit allowance available on the occurrence of a relevant benefit
crystallisation event may be reduced as a result of events occurring before 6
April 2024, see  paragraph 126  of  Schedule 9  to FA 2024.

41.637S.11

For further transitional provision that may affect the operation of this
section, see paragraph 20 of Schedule 36 to FA 2004 (pensions in payment
before commencement of Part 4 of FA 2004).

(5) and (6).

the member has not previously become entitled to any pension or lump sum under
the pension scheme;

.

##### Non-UK schemes

###### Amendments of Part 4 of FA 2004

43

Part 4 of FA 2004 (pension schemes etc) is amended as follows.

44

In section 244 (non-UK schemes: application of certain charges), after “under
this Part” insert  “, and under Part 9 of ITEPA 2003 (pension income),” .

45

For section 244A (overseas transfer charge) substitute—

########## Overseas transfer charge: introduction

45.244AA

A charge to income tax, to be known as the overseas transfer charge, arises
under the following sections—

45.244AA.a

section 244AC  (overseas transfer charge: transfers where no exclusion
applies);

45.244AA.b

section 244IA  (overseas transfer charge: transfers exceeding available
allowance).

########## Overseas transfer charge: interpretation

45.244AB

45.244AB.1

In this section and in  sections 244AC  to 244N—

      “ former QROPS ” means a scheme that has at any time been a QROPS;
“ onward transfer ” means (subject to  subsection (3) ) a transfer of sums or
assets held for the purposes of, or representing accrued rights under, an
arrangement under a QROPS or a former QROPS in relation to a member so as to
become held for the purposes of, or to represent rights under, an arrangement
under another QROPS in relation to that person as a member of that other
QROPS;           “ original transfer ”, in relation to an onward transfer,
means (subject to  subsection (3) )—         the recognised transfer or
relieved relevant non-UK scheme transfer in respect of which the following
conditions are met—         it is from a registered pension scheme or a
relieved relevant non-UK scheme to a QROPS,           the sums and assets
transferred by the onward transfer directly or indirectly derive from those
transferred by it, and           it is more recent than any other recognised
transfer or relieved relevant non-UK scheme transfer in respect of which the
conditions in sub-paragraphs (i) and (ii) are met, or                 where
there is no such recognised transfer or relieved relevant non-UK scheme
transfer, the relevant transfer (see paragraph 1(6) of Schedule 34) in respect
of which the following conditions are met—         it is from a relevant non-
UK scheme (see paragraph 1(5) of Schedule 34),           it is a transfer of
the whole or part of the UK tax-relieved fund (see paragraph 3 of Schedule 34)
of a member of the scheme,           it is to a QROPS, and           the sums
and assets transferred by the onward transfer directly or indirectly derive
from those transferred by it;                       “ QROPS ” means a
qualifying recognised overseas pension scheme;           “ recognised transfer
” has the meaning given by section 169;           “ the relevant period ”
means—         in the case of a recognised transfer or a relieved relevant
non-UK scheme transfer made on 6 April in any year, the five years beginning
with the date of that transfer,           in the case of any other recognised
transfer or relieved relevant non-UK scheme transfer, the period consisting of
the combination of—         the period beginning with the date of the transfer
and ending immediately before the next 6 April, and           the five years
beginning at the end of that initial period,                 in the case of an
onward transfer, the period—         beginning with the date of the transfer,
and           ending at the end of the relevant period for the original
transfer (see paragraphs (a) and (b) or, as the case may be, paragraphs (d)
and (e)),                 in the case of a relevant transfer that—         is
made on 6 April in any year, and           is the original transfer for an
onward transfer,         the five years beginning with the date of the
relevant transfer, and           in the case of a relevant transfer that—
is made otherwise than on 6 April in any year, and           is the original
transfer for an onward transfer,         the period consisting of the
combination of: the period beginning with the date of the relevant transfer
and ending immediately before the next 6 April; and the five years beginning
at the end of that initial period;                 “ relieved relevant non-UK
scheme ” means a pension scheme that is a relevant non-UK scheme within the
meaning of sub-paragraph (5) of paragraph 1 of Schedule 34 in respect of which
at least one of paragraphs (a) to (c) of that sub-paragraph applies;
“ relieved relevant non-UK scheme transfer ” means a transfer, other than a
block transfer, of sums or assets held for the purposes of, or representing
accrued rights under, an arrangement under a relieved relevant non-UK scheme
in relation to a relieved member of the scheme so as to become held for the
purposes of, or to represent rights under, an arrangement under a QROPS in
relation to that person as a member of that QROPS;           “ ring-fenced
transfer fund ”, in relation to a QROPS or former QROPS, has the meaning given
by paragraph 1 of Schedule 34.

45.244AB.2

For the purposes of the definition of “relieved relevant non-UK scheme
transfer”—

45.244AB.2.a

a transfer is “ a block transfer ” in relation to a member of a pension scheme
if it involves the transfer, in a single transaction, of all the sums and
assets held for the purposes of, or representing accrued rights under, the
arrangements under the scheme which relate to the member and at least one
other member of the scheme;

45.244AB.2.b

an individual is “a relieved member” of a relieved relevant non-UK scheme if—

45.244AB.2.b.i

any of the contributions in respect of which relief has been given as
mentioned in paragraph (a) or (b) of the definition of “relevant non-UK
scheme” in paragraph 1(5) of Schedule 34 were contributions paid by or on
behalf of, or in respect of, the individual, or

45.244AB.2.b.ii

the individual is the member, or one of the members, who has been exempt from
liability to tax as mentioned in paragraph (c) of that definition.

45.244AB.3

Where, apart from this subsection, there would be different original transfers
for different parts of an onward transfer, each such part of the onward
transfer is to be treated as a separate onward transfer for the purposes of
this section and  sections 244AC  to 244N.

########## Overseas transfer charge: transfers where no exclusion applies

45.244AC

45.244AC.1

The overseas transfer charge arises where—

45.244AC.1.a

a transfer within  subsection (2)  is made to a QROPS, and

45.244AC.1.b

the transfer is not excluded from the charge by or under any of sections 244B
to 244H.

45.244AC.2

A transfer to a QROPS is within this subsection if it is—

45.244AC.2.a

a recognised transfer,

45.244AC.2.b

a relieved relevant non-UK scheme transfer, or

45.244AC.2.c

an onward transfer that is made during the relevant period for the original
transfer.

45.244AC.3

Sections 244B to 244H are subject to section 244I (circumstances in which
exclusions do not apply).

After section 244I insert—

########## Overseas transfer charge: transfers exceeding available allowance

54.244IA

54.244IA.1

The overseas transfer charge arises where—

54.244IA.1.a

a transfer to a QROPS is made that is—

54.244IA.1.a.i

within  section 244AC (2) (a)  or  (b) , or

54.244IA.1.a.ii

an onward transfer within  section 244AC (2) (c)  in relation to which the
original transfer is a transfer within paragraph (b) of the definition of “
original transfer ” (see  section 244AB (1) ),

54.244IA.1.b

the transfer is excluded from the charge under  section 244AC  by or under any
of sections 244B to 244H, and

54.244IA.1.c

the transferred value (determined in accordance with section 244K) exceeds the
amount of the member’s overseas transfer allowance that is available on the
making of the transfer.

54.244IA.2

The overseas transfer charge also arises where—

54.244IA.2.a

a transfer of the kind mentioned in  subsection (1) (a)  is made to a QROPS,

54.244IA.2.b

a charge under  section 244AC  (“ the original charge ”) arises in relation to
the transfer,

54.244IA.2.c

a person liable to the original charge becomes entitled under section 244M to
a repayment in respect of the original charge, and

54.244IA.2.d

the transferred value (determined in accordance with section 244K) exceeds the
amount of the member’s overseas transfer allowance that is available on the
making of the transfer.

########## Member’s overseas transfer allowance

54.244IB

A member’s “overseas transfer allowance” is an amount equal to the member’s
lump sum and death benefit allowance.

########## Availability of member’s overseas transfer allowance

54.244IC

54.244IC.1

This section is about the availability of a member’s overseas transfer
allowance on the making of a transfer of the kind mentioned in  section 244IA
(1) (a)  (“the current overseas transfer”).

54.244IC.2

If no transfer of the kind mentioned in  section 244IA (1) (a)  has been made
in relation to the member before the current overseas transfer, the whole of
the member’s overseas transfer allowance is available.

54.244IC.3

Otherwise, the amount of the member’s overseas transfer allowance that is
available is—

54.244IC.3.a

so much of that allowance as is left after deducting the previously-used
amount, or

54.244IC.3.b

if none is left after deducting that amount, nil.

54.244IC.4

For this purpose “the previously-used amount” is the aggregate of the
transferred value (determined in accordance with section 244K) of each
transfer (if any) of the kind mentioned in  section 244IA (1) (a)  that has
been made in relation to the member before the current overseas transfer.

54.244IC.5

A reference in this section to a transfer of the kind mentioned in  section
244IA (1) (a)  is to a transfer made on or after 6 April 2024.

########## Amount of charge

56.244JA

56.244JA.1

Where the overseas transfer charge arises under  section 244AC  in relation to
a transfer, the charge is—

56.244JA.1.a

in a case where the transfer is an onward transfer and the overseas transfer
charge under  section 244IA (1)  arose in relation to the original transfer,
25% of so much of the transferred value of the original transfer as did not
exceed the amount of the member’s overseas transfer allowance that was
available on the making of the original transfer;

56.244JA.1.b

in any other case, 25% of the transferred value.

56.244JA.2

Where the overseas transfer charge arises under  section 244IA  in relation to
a transfer, the charge is 25% of so much of the transferred value as exceeds
the amount of the member’s overseas transfer allowance that is available on
the making of the transfer.

############ Enhancement of allowances

64.3.12A

64.3.12A.1

The provisions of Schedule 36 relating to the enhancement of an individual’s

of allowances provisions ”) apply in relation to an individual who is a
relieved member of a relieved non-UK pension scheme as if the relieved non-UK

member relief),

a member of the pension scheme has been, or members of the pension scheme have

(exemption for provision made by employer for retirement or death benefit) in
respect of provision made under the pension scheme at any time after 5th April
2006 when the pension scheme was an overseas pension scheme.

any of the contributions in respect of which relief has been given as
mentioned in  sub-paragraph (2) (a)  or  (b)  were contributions paid by or on
behalf of, or in respect of, the individual, or

64.3.12A.3.b

the individual is the member, or one of the members, who has been exempt from
liability to tax as mentioned in  sub-paragraph (2) (c) .

becoming entitled to a pension commencement lump sum or an uncrystallised
funds pension lump sum, where one or more lump sum and death benefit allowance
enhancement factors operate in relation to the relevant benefit
crystallisation event.

registered pension schemes) has effect in relation to the individual as if the

death benefit allowance) were an amount equal to—

  A   +       A   ×   B             where—         A is—         in the case
of an individual in relation to whom a relevant protection provision applies
(see  sub-paragraph (3) ), the individual’s protected lump sum and death
benefit allowance (see  sub-paragraph (4) );           in any other case,
£1,073,100;                 B is the aggregate of the lump sum and death
benefit allowance enhancement factors that operate in relation to the relevant
benefit crystallisation event.

########## Pension credits from previously crystallised rights

78.20A

78.20A.1

This paragraph applies in relation to a relevant benefit crystallisation event
occurring in relation to an individual where—

corresponding pension debit consisted of, or included, rights to a post-
commencement pension in payment, and

78.20A.1.d

notice of intention to rely on this paragraph is given to His Majesty’s
Revenue and Customs in accordance with regulations made by the Commissioners
for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs.

became entitled on or after 6th April 2006.

    A     £   1   ,   000   ,   000             where A is the post-
commencement pension in payment portion of the amount which is the appropriate
amount for the purposes of section 29(1) of WRPA 1999 or Article 26(1) of

referred to in the definition of A—

78.20A.6.a

in a case where the appropriate amount is arrived at under section 29(2) or
(3)(b) of WRPA 1999 or Article 26(2) or (3)(b) of WRP(NI)O 1999, is so much of
that amount as is attributable to rights to a post-commencement pension in
payment;

78.20A.6.b

in a case where the appropriate amount is arrived at under section 29(3)(a) of
WRPA 1999 or Article 26(3)(a) of WRP(NI)O 1999, is so much of that amount as
is just and reasonable.

2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum and death benefit allowance).

78.20B.4

Paragraph 20D  provides the lump sum and death benefit allowance enhancement
factor in the case of any other arrangement.

78.20B.5

For the purposes of this Part an individual is a relevant overseas individual
at any time if, at that time, the individual either is not a relevant UK
individual or—

78.20B.5.a

is a relevant UK individual by virtue only of paragraph (c) of section 189(1)
(individuals resident in UK at some time in previous five tax years), and

78.20B.5.b

is not employed by a person resident in the United Kingdom.

78.20B.6

In this paragraph and in  paragraphs 20C  and  20D  “ the active membership
period ”, in relation to an arrangement relating to the individual, is the
period—

78.20B.6.a

beginning with the date on which the benefits first began to accrue to or in
respect of the individual under the arrangement or, if later, 6th April 2006,
and

78.20B.6.b

ending on 5th April 2024.

78.20B.7

But if benefits ceased to accrue to or in respect of the individual under the
arrangement at a time before 5th April 2024, the active membership period is
to be treated as having ended at that time.

78.20B.8

Where this paragraph applies, for the purposes of this Part a lump sum is not
an uncrystallised funds pension lump sum (see paragraph 4A of Schedule 29) if,
immediately before the lump sum is paid, the amount given by the formula in
sub-paragraph (9)  is less than 25% of the lump sum.

78.20B.9

The formula is—

      A   -   B     4           where—         A is—         in the case of an
individual in relation to whom a relevant protection provision applies, the
individual’s protected lump sum and death benefit allowance (see  paragraph 6A
(4) );           in any other case, £1,073,100;                 B is the
amount that would be the previously-used amount within the meaning of  section
637S  of ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum and death benefit
allowance) if a relevant benefit crystallisation event within the meaning of
that section had occurred immediately before the lump sum is paid.

########## Non-residence: money purchase arrangements

78.20C

78.20C.1

This paragraph applies in the case of an arrangement that is a money purchase
arrangement.

78.20C.2

The lump sum and death benefit allowance enhancement factor is—

78.20C.2.a

if the arrangement is a cash balance arrangement, the cash balance arrangement
non-residence factor (see  sub-paragraphs (3)  to  (5) ), and

78.20C.2.b

in any other case, the other money purchase arrangement non-residence factor
(see  sub-paragraphs (6)  and  (7) ).

78.20C.3

The cash balance arrangement non-residence factor is—

78.20C.3.a

the factor arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (4)  in relation to
the part of the active membership period during which the individual was a
relevant overseas individual, or

78.20C.3.b

if there have been two or more parts of that period during which the
individual was a relevant overseas individual, the aggregate of the factors
arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (4)  in relation to each of
those parts of that period.

78.20C.4

The factor arrived at by the application of this subsection in relation to any
part of the active membership period is—

      A   -   B       £   1   ,   000   ,   000             where—         A
is the closing value of the individual’s rights under the arrangement;
B is the opening value of the individual’s rights under the arrangement.

78.20C.5

For the purposes of  sub-paragraph (4) —

78.20C.5.a

the closing value of the individual's rights under the arrangement is the
amount which would, on the valuation assumptions (see section 277), be
available for the provision of benefits to or in respect of the individual
under the arrangement if the individual became entitled to the benefits at the
end of that part of that period, and

78.20C.5.b

the opening value of the individual's rights under the arrangement is the
amount which would, on the valuation assumptions, be available for the
provision of benefits to or in respect of the individual under the arrangement
if the individual became entitled to the benefits at the beginning of that
part of that period.

78.20C.6

The other money purchase arrangement non-residence factor is—

78.20C.6.a

the factor arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (7)  in relation to
the part of the active membership period during which the individual was a
relevant overseas individual, or

78.20C.6.b

if there have been two or more parts of that period during which the
individual was a relevant overseas individual, the aggregate of the factors
arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (7)  in relation to each of
those parts of that period.

78.20C.7

The factor arrived at by the application of this sub-paragraph in relation to
any part of the active membership period is—

    C     £   1   ,   000   ,   000             where C is the amount of the
contributions made under the arrangement by or in respect of the individual in
any part of the active membership period during which the individual is a
relevant overseas individual.

########## Non-residence: other arrangements

78.20D

78.20D.1

This paragraph applies in the case of an arrangement that is not a money
purchase arrangement.

78.20D.2

The lump sum and death benefit allowance enhancement factor is—

78.20D.2.a

if the arrangement is a defined benefits arrangement, the defined benefits
arrangement non-residence factor (see  sub-paragraphs (3)  and  (4) ), and

78.20D.2.b

if the arrangement is a hybrid arrangement, the hybrid arrangement non-
residence factor (see  sub-paragraphs (5)  to  (7) ).

78.20D.3

The defined benefits arrangement non-residence factor is—

78.20D.3.a

the factor arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (4)  in relation to
the part of the active membership period during which the individual was a
relevant overseas individual, or

78.20D.3.b

if there have been two or more parts of that period during which the
individual was a relevant overseas individual, the aggregate of the factors
arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (4)  in relation to each of
those parts of that period.

78.20D.4

The factor arrived at by the application of this sub-paragraph in relation to
any part of the active membership period is—

          A   ×   B   +   C       -       A   ×   D   +   E           £   1
,   000   ,   000             where—         A is the relevant valuation
factor (see section 276);           B is the amount of the annual rate of the
pension which would, on the valuation assumptions (see section 277), be
payable to the individual under the arrangement if the individual became
entitled to payment of it at the end of that part of that period;           C
is the amount of the lump sum to which the individual would, on the valuation
assumptions, be entitled under the arrangement t (otherwise than by
commutation of pension) if the individual became entitled to payment of it at
the end of that part of that period;           D is the amount of the annual
rate of the pension which would, on the valuation assumptions, be payable to
the individual under the arrangement if the individual became entitled to
payment of it at the beginning of that part of that period;           E is the
amount of the lump sum to which the individual would, on the valuation
assumptions, be entitled under the arrangement (otherwise than by commutation
of pension) if the individual became entitled to payment of it at the
beginning of that part of that period.

78.20D.5

The hybrid arrangement non-residence factor is the greater or greatest of such
of—

78.20D.5.a

what would be the cash balance arrangement non-residence factor (under section
222) if the arrangement were a cash balance arrangement,

78.20D.5.b

what would be the other money purchase arrangement non-residence factor (under
that section) if the arrangement were a collective money purchase arrangement,

78.20D.5.c

what would be the other money purchase arrangement non-residence factor (under
that section) if the arrangement were a money purchase arrangement other than
a cash balance arrangement or a collective money purchase arrangement, and

78.20D.5.d

what would be the defined benefits arrangement non-residence factor (under
sub-paragraphs (3)  and  (4) ) if the arrangement were a defined benefits
arrangement,

as are relevant factors in relation to the arrangement.

78.20D.6

A factor is a relevant factor in relation to a hybrid arrangement if, in any
circumstances, the benefits that may be provided to or in respect of the
individual under the arrangement may be benefits linked to that factor.

78.20D.7

For the purposes of  sub-paragraph (6) —

78.20D.7.a

cash balance benefits are linked to the cash balance arrangement non-residence
factor;

78.20D.7.b

other money purchase benefits are linked to the other money purchase
arrangement non-residence factor;

78.20D.7.c

defined benefits are linked to the defined benefits arrangement non-residence
factor.

########## Transfers from recognised overseas pension scheme: general

78.20E

78.20E.1

This paragraph applies in relation to a relevant benefit crystallisation event
occurring in relation to an individual where—

78.20E.1.a

at any time after 5th April 2006 but before 6th April 2024, there has been a
recognised overseas scheme transfer, and

78.20E.1.b

notice of intention to rely on it is given to His Majesty’s Revenue and
Customs in accordance with regulations made by the Commissioners for His
Majesty’s Revenue and Customs.

78.20E.2

There is a “recognised overseas scheme transfer” if any sums or assets—

78.20E.2.a

held for the purposes of an arrangement under a recognised overseas pension
scheme, or

78.20E.2.b

representing accrued rights under such an arrangement,

are transferred so as to become held for the purposes of, or to represent
rights under, an arrangement under a registered pension scheme relating to the
individual.

78.20E.3

The arrangement specified in  sub-paragraph (2) (a)  or  (b)  is referred to
in this paragraph and in  paragraphs 20F  and  20G  as the “recognised
overseas scheme arrangement”.

78.20E.4

A lump sum and death benefit allowance enhancement factor operates in relation
to the relevant benefit crystallisation event mentioned in  paragraph 6A (1) .

78.20E.5

The lump sum and death benefit allowance enhancement factor is the recognised
overseas scheme transfer factor.

78.20E.6

The recognised overseas scheme transfer factor is—

      A   -   B       £   1   ,   000   ,   000             where—         A
is the aggregate of the amount of any sums transferred, and the market value
of any assets transferred, on the recognised overseas scheme transfer;
B is the relevant relievable amount (see  paragraphs 20F  and  20G ).

78.20E.7

In this paragraph and in  paragraphs 20F  and  20G  “the overseas arrangement
active membership period” is the period—

78.20E.7.a

beginning with the date on which the benefits first began to accrue to or in
respect of the individual under the recognised overseas scheme arrangement or,
if later, 6th April 2006, and

78.20E.7.b

ending on 5th April 2024.

78.20E.8

But if benefits ceased to accrue to or in respect of the individual under the
recognised overseas scheme arrangement at a time before 5th April 2024, the
overseas arrangement active membership period is to be treated as having ended
at that time.

78.20E.9

Where this paragraph applies, for the purposes of this Part a lump sum is not
an uncrystallised funds pension lump sum (see paragraph 4A of Schedule 29) if,
immediately before the lump sum is paid, the amount given by the formula in
sub-paragraph (10)  is less than 25% of the lump sum.

78.20E.10

The formula is—

      A   -   B     4           where—         A is—         in the case of an
individual in relation to whom a relevant protection provision applies, the
individual’s protected lump sum and death benefit allowance (see  paragraph 6A
(4) );           in any other case, £1,073,100;                 B is the
amount that would be the previously-used amount within the meaning of  section
637S  of ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum and death benefit
allowance) if a relevant benefit crystallisation event within the meaning of
that section had occurred immediately before the lump sum is paid.

########## Overseas scheme transfers: money purchase arrangements

78.20F

78.20F.1

This paragraph applies in the case of a recognised overseas scheme arrangement
that was a money purchase arrangement.

78.20F.2

The relevant relievable amount is—

78.20F.2.a

if the recognised overseas scheme arrangement was a cash balance arrangement,
the cash balance relevant relievable amount (see  sub-paragraphs (3)  to  (5)
), and

78.20F.2.b

if the recognised overseas scheme arrangement was any other sort of money
purchase arrangement, the other money purchase relevant relievable amount (see
sub-paragraphs (6)  and  (7) ).

78.20F.3

The cash balance relevant relievable amount is—

78.20F.3.a

the amount arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (4)  in relation to
the part of the overseas arrangement active membership period during which the
individual was not a relevant overseas individual, or

78.20F.3.b

if there have been two or more parts of that period during which the
individual was not a relevant overseas individual, the aggregate of the
amounts arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (4)  in relation to
each of those parts of that period.

78.20F.4

The amount arrived at by the application of this subsection in relation to any
part of the overseas arrangement active membership period is—

  A   -   B         where—         A is the closing value of the individual’s
rights under the arrangement, and           B is the opening value of the
individual’s rights under the arrangement.

78.20F.5

For the purposes of  sub-paragraph (4) —

78.20F.5.a

the closing value of the individual's rights under the recognised overseas
scheme arrangement is the amount which would, on the valuation assumptions
(see section 277), be available for the provision of benefits to or in respect
of the individual under the arrangement if the individual became entitled to
the benefits at the end of that part of that period, and

78.20F.5.b

the opening value of the individual's rights under the arrangement is the
amount which would, on the valuation assumptions, be available for the
provision of benefits to or in respect of the individual under the arrangement
if the individual became entitled to the benefits at the beginning of that
part of that period.

78.20F.6

The other money purchase relevant relievable amount is—

78.20F.6.a

the amount arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (7)  in relation to
the part of the overseas arrangement active membership period during which the
individual was not a relevant overseas individual, or

78.20F.6.b

if there have been two or more parts of that period during which the
individual was not a relevant overseas individual, the aggregate of the
amounts arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (7)  in relation to
each of those parts of that period.

78.20F.7

The amount arrived at by the application of this sub-paragraph in relation to
any part of the overseas arrangement active membership period is the amount of
the contributions made under the arrangement by or in respect of the
individual in any part of the overseas arrangement active membership period
during which the individual was not a relevant overseas individual.

########## Overseas scheme transfers: other arrangements

78.20G

78.20G.1

This section applies in the case of a recognised overseas scheme arrangement
that was not a money purchase arrangement.

78.20G.2

The relevant relievable amount is—

78.20G.2.a

if the recognised overseas scheme arrangement was a defined benefits
arrangement, the defined benefits relevant relievable amount (see  sub-
paragraphs (3)  and  (4) ), and

78.20G.2.b

if the recognised overseas scheme arrangement was a hybrid arrangement, the
hybrid relevant relievable amount (see  sub-paragraph (5)  to  (7) ).

78.20G.3

The defined benefits relevant relievable amount is—

78.20G.3.a

the amount arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (4)  in relation to
the part of the overseas arrangement active membership period during which the
individual was not a relevant overseas individual, or

78.20G.3.b

if there have been two or more parts of that period during which the
individual was not a relevant overseas individual, the aggregate of the
amounts arrived at by the application of  sub-paragraph (4)  in relation to
each of those parts of that period.

78.20G.4

The amount arrived at by the application of this subsection in relation to any
part of the overseas arrangement active membership period is—

      A   ×   B   +   C       -       A   ×   D   +   E             where—
A is the relevant valuation factor (see section 276);           B is the
annual rate of the pension which would, on the valuation assumptions (see
section 277), be payable to the individual under the recognised overseas
scheme arrangement if the individual became entitled to payment of it at the
end of that part of that period;           C is the amount of the lump sum to
which the individual would, on the valuation assumptions, be entitled under
the arrangement (otherwise than by commutation of pension) if the individual
became entitled to payment of it at the end of that part of that period;
D is the annual rate of the pension which would, on the valuation assumptions,
be payable to the individual under the arrangement if the individual became
entitled to payment of it at the beginning of that part of that period;
E is the amount of the lump sum to which the individual would, on the
valuation assumptions, be entitled under the arrangement (otherwise than by
commutation of pension) if the individual became entitled to payment of it at
the beginning of that part of that period.

78.20G.5

The hybrid relevant relievable amount is the greater or greatest of such of—

78.20G.5.a

what would be the cash balance relevant relievable amount (under section 225)
if the recognised overseas scheme arrangement had been a cash balance
arrangement,

78.20G.5.b

what would be the other money purchase relevant relievable amount (under that
section) if that arrangement had been a collective money purchase arrangement,

78.20G.5.c

what would be the other money purchase relevant relievable amount (under that
section) if that arrangement had been a money purchase arrangement other than
a cash balance arrangement or a collective money purchase arrangement, and

78.20G.5.d

what would be the defined benefits relevant relievable amount (under  sub-
paragraph (3)  and  (4) ) if that arrangement had been a defined benefits
arrangement,

as are relevant to that arrangement.

78.20G.6

An amount is relevant to a hybrid arrangement if, in any circumstances, the
benefits that may be provided to or in respect of the individual under the
arrangement may be benefits linked to that amount.

78.20G.7

For the purposes of  sub-paragraph (6) —

78.20G.7.a

cash balance benefits are linked to the cash balance relevant relievable
amount;

78.20G.7.b

other money purchase benefits are linked to the other money purchase relevant
relievable amount;

78.20G.7.c

defined benefits are linked to the defined benefits relevant relievable
amount.

###### Amendments of the Taxation of Pension Schemes (Transitional Provisions) Order 2006

95

95.1

The Taxation of Pension Schemes (Transitional Provisions) Order 2006 ( S.I.
2006/572 ) is amended as follows.

95.2

In article 25A (conditions to be met by stand-alone lump sums), in paragraph
(3), for “benefit crystallisation event” substitute  “relevant benefit
crystallisation event” .

95.3

In article 25B (circumstances in which stand-alone lump sums are paid), in
paragraph (2), for “paragraph 2 of Schedule 29” substitute  “Chapter 15A of
Part 9 of ITEPA 2003” .

95.4

In article 25C (payment of stand-alone lump sums: tax consequences), for
paragraphs (2) and (3A) substitute—

95.4.1A

Articles 25CA to 25CC apply for the purposes of determining the tax treatment
of a stand-alone lump sum.

95.5

After article 25C insert—

############ Circumstance A: tax treatment of stand-alone lump sums

95.5.25CA

95.5.25CA.1

Chapter 15A  of Part 9 of ITEPA 2003 (pension income: lump sums under
registered pension schemes) has effect with the following modifications for
the purposes of determining the income tax treatment of a stand-alone lump sum
paid to a member of a pension scheme in circumstances where article 25B(2)
(circumstance A) applies.

95.5.25CA.2

That Chapter has effect as if, after  section 637G  (trivial commutation lump
sums and winding-up lump sums) there were inserted—

################## Stand-alone lump sums

95.5.25CA.2.637GA

95.5.25CA.2.637GA.1

Subject to  subsection (2) , no liability to income tax arises on a stand-
alone lump sum paid under a registered pension scheme.

95.5.25CA.2.637GA.2

If the amount of the stand-alone lump sum exceeds the permitted maximum,
section 579A (pensions) applies to the excess as it applies to any pension
under a registered pension scheme.

95.5.25CA.2.637GA.3

In  subsection (2)  “ the permitted maximum ”, in relation to a stand-alone
lump sum, means the lower of—

95.5.25CA.2.637GA.3.a

the maximum amount of a stand-alone lump sum that could have been paid to the
individual with no liability to income tax on 5 April 2023, and

95.5.25CA.2.637GA.3.b

so much of the individual’s lump sum and death benefit allowance as is
available immediately before the individual becomes entitled to the lump sum
(see  section 637S ).

95.5.25CA.3

Section 637Q  of ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum allowance)
has effect as if, in the definition of “relevant lump sum” in  subsection (2)
(b)  of that section, there were included a reference to a stand-alone lump
sum.

95.5.25CA.4

Section 637S  of ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum and death
benefit allowance) has effect as if, in the definition of “relevant lump sum”
in  subsection (2) (b)  of that section, there were included a reference to a
stand-alone lump sum.

############ Circumstance B: tax treatment of stand-alone lump sums

95.5.25CB

95.5.25CB.1

Chapter 15A  of Part 9 of ITEPA 2003 (pension income: lump sums under
registered pension schemes) has effect with the following modifications for
the purposes of determining the income tax treatment of a stand-alone lump sum
paid to a member of a pension scheme in circumstances where article 25B(3)
(circumstance B) applies.

95.5.25CB.2

That Chapter has effect as if, after  section 637G  (trivial commutation lump
sums and winding-up lump sums) there were inserted—

################## Stand-alone lump sums

95.5.25CB.2.637GA

95.5.25CB.2.637GA.1

Subject to  subsection (2) , no liability to income tax arises on a stand-
alone lump sum paid under a registered pension scheme.

95.5.25CB.2.637GA.2

If the amount of the stand-alone lump sum exceeds the permitted maximum,
section 579A (pensions) applies to the excess as it applies to any pension
under a registered pension scheme.

95.5.25CB.2.637GA.3

In  subsection (2)  “ the permitted maximum ”, in relation to a stand-alone
lump sum, means—

95.5.25CB.2.637GA.3.a

the amount of a stand-alone lump sum that could have been paid to the
individual with no liability to income tax on 5 April 2023 under the
arrangement pursuant to which the entitlement to the stand-alone lump sum
arises in respect of the individual, less

95.5.25CB.2.637GA.3.b

the aggregate of the amounts of any stand-alone lump sums and pension
commencement lump sums previously paid to the individual under that
arrangement after that date.

95.5.25CB.3

Section 637Q  of ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum allowance)
has effect as if, in the definition of “relevant lump sum” in  subsection (2)
(b)  of that section, there were included a reference to a stand-alone lump
sum.

95.5.25CB.4

Section 637S  of ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum and death
benefit allowance) has effect as if, in the definition of “relevant lump sum”
in  subsection (2) (b)  of that section, there were included a reference to a
stand-alone lump sum.

############ Circumstance C: tax treatment of stand-alone lump sums

95.5.25CC

95.5.25CC.1

Chapter 15A  of Part 9 of ITEPA 2003 (pension income: lump sums under
registered pension schemes) has effect with the following modifications for
the purposes of determining the income tax treatment of a stand-alone lump sum
paid to a member of a pension scheme in circumstances where article 25B(4)
(circumstance C) applies.

95.5.25CC.2

That Chapter has effect as if, after  section 637G  (trivial commutation lump
sums and winding-up lump sums) there were inserted—

################## Stand-alone lump sums

95.5.25CC.2.637GA

95.5.25CC.2.637GA.1

Subject to  subsection (2) , no liability to income tax arises on a stand-
alone lump sum paid under a registered pension scheme.

95.5.25CC.2.637GA.2

If the amount of the stand-alone lump sum exceeds the permitted maximum,
section 579A (pensions) applies to the excess as it applies to any pension
under a registered pension scheme.

95.5.25CC.2.637GA.3

In  subsection (2)  “ the permitted maximum ”, in relation to a stand-alone
lump sum, means the lower of—

95.5.25CC.2.637GA.3.a

the maximum amount of a stand-alone lump sum that could have been paid to the
individual with no liability to income tax on 5 April 2023, and

95.5.25CC.2.637GA.3.b

so much of the individual’s lump sum and death benefit allowance as is
available immediately before the individual becomes entitled to the lump sum
(see  section 637S ).

95.5.25CC.3

Section 637Q  of ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum allowance),
has effect as if, in the definition of “relevant lump sum” in  subsection (2)
(b)  of that section, there were included a reference to a stand-alone lump
sum.

95.5.25CC.4

For the purposes of that section, the “non-taxable amount” of a stand-alone
lump sum is to be treated as being an amount equal to 25% of the lump sum.

95.5.25CC.5

Section 637S of ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum and death
benefit allowance), in the definition of “relevant lump sum” in  subsection
(2) (b)  of that section, there were included a reference to a stand-alone
lump sum.

95.6

In article 25D (stand-alone lump sums: further provisions)—

95.6.a

in paragraph (2)—

95.6.a.i

for “VULSR — APCLS” substitute  “A — B” ;

95.6.a.ii

omit the words from “, in the modified sub-paragraph (6)” to the end;

95.6.b

in paragraph (3), for “in the modified sub-paragraph (6) of paragraph 2 of
Schedule 29, the term “APCLS”” substitute  “the term “B”” .

of Schedule 36 to FA 2004);           the Registered Pension Schemes (Enhanced
Allowances Transitional Protection) Regulations 2011 ( S.I. 2011/1752 ) (where

Allowances Transitional Protection) (Notification) Regulations 2013 ( S.I.
2013/1741 ) (where the member relies on fixed protection 2014 under Schedule
22 to FA 2013);           the Registered Pension Schemes and Relieved Non-UK
Pension Schemes (Enhanced Allowances Transitional Protection) (Individual
Protection 2014 Notification) Regulations 2014 ( S.I. 2014/1842 ) (where the
member relies on individual protection 2014 under Schedule 6 to FA 2014);
paragraph 14 of Schedule 4 to the Finance Act 2016 (where the member relies on
fixed or individual protection 2016 under that Schedule);

105.b
