##### Commencement and transitional provision etc

###### Commencement

124

The amendments made by section  14  and this Schedule have effect for the tax
year 2024-25 and subsequent tax years.

###### Availability of individual’s lump sum allowance

125

125.1

This paragraph applies where—

125.1.a

one or more benefit crystallisation events within the meaning of Part 4 of FA
2004 occurred in relation to an individual before 6 April 2024,  ...

125.1.b

a relevant benefit crystallisation event within the meaning of  section 637Q
of ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum allowance) occurs in
relation to the individual on or after that date , and

125.1.c

at the time the relevant benefit crystallisation occurs, the individual—

125.1.c.i

is not an individual to whom paragraph 12 of Schedule 36 to FA 2004 applies
(enhanced protection), or

125.1.c.ii

is such an individual and is not within paragraph 24(1) of Schedule 36 to FA
2004 (persons with lump sum protection).

125.2

. . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .

125.3

  The   amount of the individual’s lump sum allowance that is available on the
occurrence of the relevant benefit crystallisation event is—

125.3.a

the amount of that allowance that is available in accordance with  section
637Q  of ITEPA 2003 on the occurrence of that event, less

125.3.b

an amount equal to 25% of the individual’s lifetime allowance previously-used
amount;

or, if that produces a negative result, nil.

125.3A

Where—

125.3A.a

the individual is an individual to whom paragraph 7 of Schedule 36 to FA 2004
applies (primary protection),

125.3A.b

the individual is not within paragraph 24(1) of Schedule 36 to FA 2004
(persons with lump sum protection), and

125.3A.c

25% of the individual’s lifetime allowance previously-used amount is greater
than £375,000,

sub-paragraph (3) has effect as if the amount determined under paragraph (b)
of that sub-paragraph were £375,000.

125.4

But   sub-paragraph (3) does   not apply if, on the occurrence of the relevant
benefit crystallisation event, a transitional tax-free amount certificate is
in force in relation to the individual.

125.5

In such a case, the amount of the individual’s lump sum allowance that is
available on the occurrence of the relevant benefit crystallisation event is—

125.5.a

the amount of that allowance that is available in accordance with  section
637Q  of ITEPA 2003 on the occurrence of that event, less

125.5.b

the individual’s lump sum transitional tax-free amount;

or, if that produces a negative result, nil.

125.6

For provision about the meaning of expressions used in this paragraph, see
paragraph 129 .

###### Availability of individual’s lump sum and death benefit allowance

126

126.1

This paragraph applies where—

126.1.a

one or more benefit crystallisation events within the meaning of Part 4 of FA
2004 occurred in relation to an individual before 6 April 2024,  ...

126.1.b

a relevant benefit crystallisation event within the meaning of  section 637S
of ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum and death benefit
allowance) occurs in relation to the individual on or after that date.  , and

126.1.c

at the time the relevant benefit crystallisation occurs, the individual is not
an individual to whom paragraph 12 of Schedule 36 to FA 2004 applies (enhanced
protection).

126.2

Where the individual’s lifetime allowance previously-used amount is equal to
or greater than the individual’s lifetime allowance, none of the individual’s
lump sum and death benefit allowance is available on the occurrence of the
relevant benefit crystallisation event.

126.3

Otherwise, the amount of the individual’s lump sum and death benefit allowance
that is available on the occurrence of the relevant benefit crystallisation
event is—

126.3.a

the amount of that allowance that is available in accordance with  section
637S  of ITEPA 2003 on the occurrence of that event, less

126.3.b

an amount equal to the appropriate percentage of the individual’s lifetime
allowance previously-used amount;

or, if that produces a negative result, nil.

126.3A

Where—

126.3A.a

the individual is an individual to whom paragraph 7 of Schedule 36 to FA 2004
applies (primary protection),

126.3A.b

the individual is not within paragraph 24(1) of Schedule 36 to FA 2004
(persons with lump sum protection),

126.3A.c

the appropriate percentage is 25%, and

126.3A.d

25% of the individual’s lifetime allowance previously-used amount is greater
than £375,000,

sub-paragraph (3) has effect as if the amount determined under paragraph (b)
of that sub-paragraph were £375,000.

126.4

In   sub-paragraphs (3) and (3A)   “ the appropriate percentage ” means—

126.4.a

100% in a case in which—

126.4.a.i

the individual becomes entitled to a serious ill-health lump sum before 6
April 2024 and is under the age of 75 at the time of the payment, or

126.4.a.ii

the individual dies before 6 April 2024 under the age of 75 and before that
date a person is paid a lump sum death benefit in respect of the individual;

126.4.b

25% in any other case.

126.5

But sub-paragraphs  (2)  to  (4)  do not apply if, on the occurrence of the
relevant benefit crystallisation event, a transitional tax-free amount
certificate is in force in relation to the individual.

126.6

In such a case, the amount of the individual’s lump sum and death benefit
allowance that is available on the occurrence of the relevant benefit
crystallisation event is—

126.6.a

the amount of that allowance that is available in accordance with  section
637S  of ITEPA 2003 on the occurrence of that event, less

126.6.b

the individual’s lump sum and death benefit transitional tax-free amount;

or, if that produces a negative result, nil.

126.7

For provision about the meaning of expressions used in this paragraph, see
paragraph 129 .

###### Transitional tax-free amount certificates

127

127.1

A “transitional tax-free amount certificate” is a certificate relating to an
individual that—

127.1.a

is issued by a registered pension scheme on an application made in accordance
with this paragraph, and

127.1.b

certifies that the scheme administrator of the scheme is satisfied as to—

127.1.b.i

the amount of the individual’s lump sum transitional tax-free amount, and

127.1.b.ii

the amount of the individual’s lump sum and death benefit transitional tax-
free amount.

127.2

An application for a certificate in relation to an individual—

127.2.a

may be made by the individual or, if the individual is deceased, the
individual’s personal representatives;

127.2.b

may be made to any registered pension scheme of which the individual is a
member or, if the individual is deceased, of which the individual was a member
immediately before death;

127.2.c

must be accompanied by complete evidence as to the amount of the individual’s
lump sum and death benefit transitional tax-free amount;

127.2.d

may not be made after the occurrence, in relation to the individual, of a
relevant benefit crystallisation event within the meaning of  section 637S  of
ITEPA 2003 (availability of individual’s lump sum and death benefit
allowance).

127.3

The scheme administrator of a registered pension scheme to which an
application is made must, before the end of the period of three months
beginning with the date on which the scheme receives the application,
determine the application by—

127.3.a

issuing the applicant with a certificate, or

127.3.b

notifying the applicant that the application is refused.

127.4

A certificate must (in addition to certifying the matter mentioned in  sub-
paragraph (1) (b) ) contain the following information—

127.4.a

the individual’s name, address and national insurance number,

127.4.b

the individual’s lifetime allowance previously-used amount expressed as a
percentage of the standard lifetime allowance,

127.4.c

the amount that the scheme administrator is satisfied is the individual’s lump
sum transitional tax-free amount, and

127.4.d

the amount that the scheme administrator is satisfied is the individual’s lump
sum and death benefit transitional tax-free amount.

127.5

A certificate may be in such form as the scheme administrator may determine
and may, in particular, be incorporated into any other document that is given
to the applicant by the scheme.

127.6

If at any time it appears to the scheme administrator of a registered pension
scheme that the amount specified on a certificate under  sub-paragraph (4) (c)
or  (d)  does not accurately reflect the individual’s lump sum transitional
tax-free amount or (as the case may be) lump sum and death benefit
transitional tax-free amount, they must cancel the certificate by giving
notice of the cancellation to the applicant or, if the applicant is deceased,
the applicant’s personal representatives.

127.7

A certificate—

127.7.a

comes into force when it is issued, and

127.7.b

ceases to be in force on the giving of a notice under sub-paragraph  (6) .

127.8

The Commissioners for His Majesty’s Revenue and Customs may by regulations—

127.8.a

amend sub-paragraph  (3)  by substituting a different period for that for the
time being specified there, or

127.8.b

make further provision about transitional tax-free certificates.

127.9

For provision about the meaning of expressions used in this paragraph, see
paragraph 129 .

127.10

In the second column of the Table in section 98 of TMA 1970 (penalty for
failure to give certificates etc), at the appropriate place insert—

Paragraph  127  of  Schedule 9  to the Finance Act 2024

.

###### Availability of member’s overseas transfer allowance

127A

127A.1

This paragraph applies where—

127A.1.a

one or more benefit crystallisation events within the meaning of Part 4 of FA
2004 occurred in relation to an individual before 6 April 2024, and

127A.1.b

a transfer of the kind mentioned in section 244IA(1)(a) of FA 2004 is made in
relation to the individual on or after that date.

127A.2

Where the individual’s lifetime allowance previously-used amount is equal to
or greater than the individual’s lifetime allowance, none of the individual’s
overseas transfer allowance is available on the making of the transfer.

127A.3

Otherwise, the amount of the individual’s overseas transfer allowance that is
available on the making of the transfer is—

127A.3.a

the amount of that allowance that is available in accordance with section
244IC of FA 2004 on the making of the transfer, less

127A.3.b

the individual’s lifetime allowance previously-used amount,

or, if that produces a negative result, nil.

###### Provision of information by scheme administrators to members

128

128.1

A reference in the Provision of Information Regulations to a relevant benefit
crystallisation event is, in relation to times before 6 April 2024, a
reference to a benefit crystallisation event within the meaning of Part 4 of
FA 2004.

128.2

Sub-paragraph  (3)  applies where—

128.2.a

one or more benefit crystallisation events within the meaning of Part 4 of FA
2004 occurred in relation to a member of a registered pension scheme before 6
April 2024, and

128.2.b

it is necessary to determine, for the purposes of any provision of the
Provision of Information Regulations as that provision has effect for the tax
year 2024-25 or a subsequent tax year, the amount of the member’s lump sum
allowance that has been expended by the events mentioned in paragraph  (a) .

128.3

For those purposes, the amount of the member’s lump sum allowance that has
been expended by the events mentioned in  sub-paragraph (2) (a)  is—

128.3.a

if a transitional tax-free amount certificate is in force in relation to the
member, so much of the member’s lump sum transitional tax-free amount as is
referable to those events;

128.3.b

otherwise, an amount equal to 25% of so much of the member’s lifetime
allowance previously-used amount as is referable to those events.

128.4

Sub-paragraph  (5)  applies where—

128.4.a

one or more benefit crystallisation events within the meaning of Part 4 of FA
2004 occurred in relation to a member of a registered pension scheme before 6
April 2024, and

128.4.b

it is necessary to determine, for the purposes of any provision of the
Provision of Information Regulations as it has effect for the tax year 2024-25
or a later tax year, the amount of the member’s lump sum and death benefit
allowance that has been expended by the events mentioned in paragraph  (a) .

128.5

For those purposes, the amount of the member’s lump sum and death benefit
allowance that has been expended by the events mentioned in  sub-paragraph (4)
(a)  is—

128.5.a

if a transitional tax-free amount certificate is in force in relation to the
member, so much of the member’s lump sum and death benefit transitional tax-
free amount as is referable to those events;

128.5.b

otherwise, an amount equal to the appropriate percentage of so much of the
member’s lifetime allowance previously-used amount as is referable to those
events.

128.6

In  sub-paragraph (5) (b)  “ the appropriate percentage ” means—

128.6.a

100% in a case in which—

128.6.a.zi

the amount of the member’s lifetime allowance previously-used amount is equal
to or greater than the member’s lifetime allowance,

128.6.a.i

the member becomes entitled to a serious ill-health lump sum under the scheme
before 6 April 2024 and is under the age of 75 at the time of the payment, or

128.6.a.ii

the member dies before 6 April 2024 under the age of 75 and before that date a
person is paid a lump sum death benefit under the scheme in respect of the
individual;

128.6.b

25% in any other case.

128.7

In this paragraph “ the Provision of Information Regulations ” means the
Registered Pension Schemes (Provision of Information) Regulations ( S.I.
2006/567 ).

128.8

For further provision about the meaning of expressions used in this paragraph,
see  paragraph 129 .

###### Paragraphs 

129

129.1

“ Lump sum transitional tax-free amount ”, in relation to an individual, means
the total of—

129.1.a

each pension commencement lump sum (if any) to which the individual has,
before 6 April 2024, become entitled under a registered pension scheme,  ...

129.1.b

each uncrystallised funds pension lump sum (if any) to which the individual
has, before 6 April 2024, become entitled under a registered pension scheme,
so far as no charge to income tax under Part 9 of ITEPA 2003 or Part 4 of FA
2004 arises in respect of it.

129.1.c

each stand-alone lump sum (if any) to which the individual has, before 6 April
2024, become entitled under a registered pension scheme, so far as no charge
to income tax under Part 9 of ITEPA 2003 or Part 4 of FA 2004 arises in
respect of it, and

129.1.d

where a benefit crystallisation event within sub-paragraph (2)(a) of paragraph
20 of Schedule 36 to FA 2004 (pre-commencement pensions) was treated as having
occurred before 6 April 2024 in relation to the individual, an amount equal to
25% of the amount treated as crystallised by that event under sub-paragraph
(2)(b) of that paragraph.

129.2

“ Lump sum and death benefit transitional tax-free amount ”, in relation to an
individual, means the total of—

129.2.a

each relevant lump sum (if any) to which the individual has, before 6 April
2024, become entitled under a registered pension scheme, so far as no charge
to income tax under Part 9 of ITEPA 2003 or Part 4 of FA 2004 arises in
respect of it,  ...

129.2.b

each relevant lump sum death benefit (if any) paid before 6 April 2024 by a
registered pension scheme in respect of the individual so far as no charge to
income tax under Part 9 of ITEPA 2003 or Part 4 of FA 2004 arises in respect
of it , and

129.2.c

where a benefit crystallisation event within sub-paragraph (2)(a) of paragraph
20 of Schedule 36 to FA 2004 (pre-commencement pensions) was treated as having
occurred before 6 April 2024 in relation to the individual, an amount equal to
25% of the amount treated as crystallised by that event under sub-paragraph
(2)(b) of that paragraph.

129.3

For the purposes of  sub-paragraph (2) —

129.3.a

a lump sum is “relevant” if the individual becoming entitled to it constituted
a benefit crystallisation event within the meaning of Part 4 of FA 2004;

129.3.b

a lump sum death benefit is “relevant” if its payment constituted a benefit
crystallisation event within the meaning of Part 4 of FA 2004.

129.4

“ Complete evidence ”, in relation to an individual’s lump sum and death
benefit transitional tax-free amount, means evidence of—

129.4.a

each lump sum (if any) to which the individual has become entitled, and

129.4.b

each lump sum death benefit (if any) that has been paid in respect of the
individual,

that is comprised, or any part of which is comprised, in the individual’s lump
sum and death benefit transitional tax-free amount.

129.5

In paragraphs  125  to  128  and this paragraph—

“ complete evidence ” has the meaning given by  sub-paragraph (4) ; “ lifetime
allowance ” has the same meaning as in Part 4 of FA 2004; “ lifetime allowance
previously-used amount ” means the amount that would have been the previously-
used amount for the purposes of section 219 of FA 2004 (availability of
individual’s lifetime allowance) if a benefit crystallisation event (within
the meaning of that section) had occurred immediately before 6 April 2024; “
lump sum and death benefit transitional tax-free amount ” has the meaning
given by  sub-paragraphs (2)  and  (3) ; “ lump sum death benefit ” has the
same meaning as in Part 4 of FA 2004; “ lump sum transitional tax-free amount
” has the meaning given by  sub-paragraph (1) ; “ pension commencement lump
sum ” has the same meaning as in Part 4 of FA 2004; “ the Provision of
Information Regulations ” means the Registered Pension Schemes (Provision of
Information) Regulations ( S.I. 2006/567 ); “ scheme administrator ” has the
same meaning as in Part 4 of FA 2004; “ serious ill-health lump sum ” has the
same meaning as in Part 4 of FA 2004;   “ stand-alone lump sum ” has the
meaning given by article 25 of the Taxation of Pension Schemes (Transitional
Provisions) Order 2006 ( S.I. 2006/572 );   “ standard lifetime allowance ”,
in relation to an individual, has the same meaning as in Part 4 of FA 2004 as
that Part has effect in relation to the individual; “ transitional tax-free
amount certificate ” means a certificate under  paragraph 127 ; “
uncrystallised funds pension lump  sum ” has the same meaning as in Part 4 of
FA 2004.

129.6

A reference in any of paragraphs  125  to  128  or this paragraph to a
provision of FA 2004 is to that provision as it had effect immediately before
6 April 2024.

###### Statements for certain members who would not otherwise receive one in the tax year 2024-25

130

130.1

The scheme administrator of a registered pension scheme must provide a
statement to each relevant person before the end of the tax year 2024-25.

130.2

In  sub-paragraph (1)  “ relevant person ” means—

130.2.a

any member of the scheme—

130.2.a.i

in relation to whom one or more benefit crystallisation events occurred before
6 April 2024, and

130.2.a.ii

who on that date does not have an actual (as opposed to prospective)
entitlement to be paid a pension, or

130.2.b

the personal representatives of a member within  paragraph (a)  who has died.

130.3

The statement must contain the information in regulation 14(3) of the
Provision of Information Regulations (percentage of standard lifetime
allowance expended by benefit crystallisation events) in respect of benefit
crystallisation events occurring before 6 April 2024.

130.4

In this paragraph—

“ benefit crystallisation event ” means a benefit crystallisation event within
the meaning of Part 4 of FA 2004, as that Part had effect immediately before 6
April 2024; “ the Provision of Information Regulations ” means the Registered
Pension Schemes (Provision of Information) Regulations ( S.I. 2006/567 )  , as
those regulations had effect immediately before 6 April 2024 ; “ scheme
administrator ” has the same meaning as in Part 4 of FA 2004.

###### Lump sums paid on or after 6 April 2024 where entitlement arose before that date

130A

130A.1

This paragraph applies in relation to a lump sum to which a member of a
registered pension scheme becomes entitled before 6 April 2024 and which is
paid on or after that date.

130A.2

The amendments made by Schedule 9 to FA 2024 and these regulations are to be
disregarded for the purposes of determining—

130A.2.a

the extent (if any) to which the lump sum is a lump sum within subsection (1)
of section 166 of FA 2004 (lump sum rule), and

130A.2.b

the tax treatment of the lump sum.

###### Lump sum death benefits paid on or after 6 April 2024 that crystallised before that date

131

In  section 637S  (availability of individual’s lump sum and death benefit
allowance) “ relevant lump sum death benefit ” does not include a lump sum
death benefit if and to the extent that it is paid in respect of rights that,
before 6 April 2024, crystallised under section 216 of FA 2004.

###### Modifications of scheme rules

132

132.1

A rule of a registered pension scheme relating to a member’s entitlement to  ,
or to the payment of,   a lifetime allowance excess lump sum has effect, in
relation to entitlements arising on or after 6 April 2024, and so far as
possible, as a rule relating to the member’s entitlement to  , or to the
payment of,   a pension commencement excess lump sum.

132.2

The amendments of Part 4 of FA 2004 made by or under this Schedule do not
affect the interpretation of any relevant rule of a registered pension scheme.

132.3

For the purposes of  sub-paragraph (2) , a rule of a registered pension scheme
is “relevant” if the rule imposes a limit on the amount of a benefit payable
under the scheme to, or in respect of, a member by reference to the member’s
lifetime allowance, the standard lifetime allowance or the lifetime allowance
charge.

132.4

In this paragraph “ lifetime allowance ”, “ standard lifetime allowance ” and
“ lifetime allowance charge ” have the same meaning as in Part 4 of FA 2004 as
that Part had effect immediately before 6 April 2024.

132.5

This paragraph ceases to have effect at the end of the tax year 2028-29.

###### Continuity of the law

132A

132A.1

This paragraph applies where any provision of or made under this Schedule re-
enacts (with or without modification) a provision of the pensions tax code
that is repealed by or under this Schedule.

132A.2

The repeal and re-enactment does not affect the continuity of the law.

132A.3

Anything done (including any subordinate legislation made) or having effect as
if done, under or for the purposes of the repealed provision that could have
been done under or for the purposes of the corresponding provision of the
pensions tax code, if in force or effective immediately before the
commencement of that corresponding provision, has effect thereafter as if done
under or for the purposes of that corresponding provision.

132A.4

Any reference (express or implied) in any enactment, instrument or document to
a provision of the pensions tax code shall be construed (so far as the context
permits) as including, as respects times, circumstances or purposes in
relation to which the corresponding repealed provision had effect, a reference
to that corresponding provision.

132A.5

Any reference (express or implied) in any enactment, instrument or document to
a repealed provision shall be construed (so far as the context permits) as
respects times, circumstances or purposes in relation to which the
corresponding provision of the pensions tax code has effect, as being or
(according to the context) including a reference to that corresponding
provision.

132A.6

This paragraph has effect subject to any specific transitional provision or
saving contained in or made under this Schedule.

132A.7

In this paragraph a reference to an enactment being repealed includes its
being substituted or revoked.

132A.8

In this paragraph “ pensions tax code ” means—

132A.8.a

Part 4 of FA 2004 (pension schemes) and subordinate legislation made under it,
and

132A.8.b

Part 9 of ITEPA 2003 (pension income) and subordinate legislation made under
it.

###### Power to make further transitional provision

133

133.1

The Treasury may make transitional, transitory or saving provision (in
addition to that contained in paragraphs  126  to  132 ) in connection with
the coming into force of any amendment made by section  14  or this Schedule.

133.2

Regulations under this paragraph may—

133.2.a

insert provision into this Part of this Schedule;

133.2.b

amend any provision of paragraphs  126  to  132 ;

133.2.c

make different provision for different purposes.

###### Power to make further provision in connection with the abolition of lifetime allowance charge

134

134.1

The Treasury may by regulations make further provision (in addition to that
contained in Parts  1  to  5  of this Schedule) in consequence of, or
otherwise in connection with, the provision made by sections 18, 19 and 23 of
F(No.2)A 2023.

134.2

Regulations under this paragraph may—

134.2.a

amend any provision of the Income Tax Acts (including any provision of, or
amendment made by, this Schedule);

134.2.b

if made after 5 April 2024, be made so as to have effect for the tax year in
which they are made;

134.2.c

make different provision for different purposes;

134.2.d

include transitional, transitory or saving provision.

134.3

Regulations under this paragraph that increase any person’s liability to tax
may not be made unless a draft of the statutory instrument containing them has
been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, the House of Commons.

134.4

No regulations under this paragraph may be made after 5 April 2026.

134.5

In  sub-paragraph (2)  “ amend ” includes repeal or revoke.

  Calculation of trade profits etc

Section 16

##### Main provisions

###### Introduction of cash basis default

1

Chapter 3 of Part 2 of ITTOIA 2005 (trade profits: basic rules) is amended as
follows.

2

After section 24 insert—

########## Basis of accounting

########### Cash basis to apply by default

2.24A

2.24A.1

The profits of a trade for a tax year must be calculated on the cash basis,
unless—

2.24A.1.a

the trade is an excluded trade in relation to the tax year (see  section 25B
), or

2.24A.1.b

an election under  section 25C (1)  has effect in relation to the trade for
the tax year.

2.24A.2

In this Part—

2.24A.2.a

references to calculating the profits of a trade on the cash basis are
references to doing so in accordance with this section, and

2.24A.2.b

references to a trade in relation to which the cash basis applies are to a
trade the profits of which are required by virtue of  subsection (1)  to be
calculated on the cash basis.

2.24A.3

Chapter 3A contains provision about the calculation of profits on the cash
basis and the application of the rest of this Part in relation to the cash
basis.

2.24A.4

Where the cash basis applies in relation to a trade, sections 27, 28 and 30 do
not apply in relation to the calculation of the profits of the trade.

2.24A.5

This section does not affect provisions of the Income Tax Acts relating to the
calculation of the profits of Lloyd's underwriters.

3

In section 25 (generally accepted accounting practice)—

3.a

in subsection (1), after “trade” insert  “to which the cash basis does not
apply” ;

3.b

omit subsection (3).

4

Omit section 25A (cash basis for small businesses).

5

Before section 26 insert—

########## Election for profits to be calculated in accordance with GAAP

5.25C

5.25C.1

A person who is or has been carrying on a trade, other than an excluded trade,
may elect for the profits of the trade to be calculated in accordance with
generally accepted accounting practice (instead of on the cash basis).

5.25C.2

An election made in relation to a trade under  subsection (1)  has effect—

5.25C.2.a

for the tax year for which it is made, and

5.25C.2.b

for every subsequent tax year (subject to  subsection (3) ).

5.25C.3

An election made in relation to a trade under  subsection (1)  ceases to have
effect if—

5.25C.3.a

the trade is an excluded trade in relation to a tax year, or

5.25C.3.b

the person who is or has been carrying on the trade, other than an excluded
trade, elects to calculate its profits for a subsequent tax year on the cash
basis.

5.25C.4

Subsection (3)  does not prevent an election being made under  subsection (1)
for any subsequent tax year.

5.25C.5

For the meaning of “excluded trade”, see  section 25B .

8.b.ii

##### Minor and consequential amendments

###### Amendments of ITTOIA 2005

####### Other amendments of Chapter 3 of Part 2

9

Chapter 3 of Part 2 of ITTOIA 2005 (trade profits: basic rules) is amended as
follows.

10

Before section 24 insert the following italic heading—

  Professions and vocations

.

11

Before section 25C (inserted by  paragraph 5  of this Schedule) insert —

########### Excluded trades

11.25B

11.25B.1

A trade is an excluded trade in relation to a tax year if the trade meets any
of conditions A to G.

11.25B.2

Condition A is that—

11.25B.2.a

the person who is or has been carrying on the trade is a firm, and

11.25B.2.b

one or more of the persons who have been partners in the firm at any time
during the tax year was not an individual at that time.

11.25B.3

Condition B is that the person who is or has been carrying on the trade was a
limited liability partnership at any time during the tax year.

11.25B.4

Condition C is that an election under Chapter 8 (trade profits: herd basis
rules) has effect in relation to the trade for the tax year.

11.25B.5

Condition D is that a claim under Chapter 16 (claim for averaging of
fluctuating profits) has been made in relation to the trade for the tax year.

11.25B.6

Condition E is that, at any time within the period of 7 years ending
immediately before the tax year, the person who is or has been carrying on the
trade obtained an allowance under Part 3A of CAA 2001 (business premises
renovation allowances) in relation to the trade.

11.25B.7

Condition F is that the trade is or was at any time during the tax year a
mineral extraction trade within the meaning of Part 5 of CAA 2001 (see section
394(2) of that Act).

11.25B.8

Condition G is that—

11.25B.8.a

at any time before the beginning of the tax year the person who is or has been
carrying on the trade obtained an allowance under Part 6 of CAA 2001 (research
and development allowances) in respect of qualifying expenditure incurred by
the person in relation to the trade, and

11.25B.8.b

the person owns an asset representing the expenditure.

In this subsection “ qualifying expenditure ” has the same meaning as in Part
6 of CAA 2001.

11.25B.9

The Treasury may by regulations amend this section.

11.25B.10

A statutory instrument containing regulations under  subsection (9)  that
restricts the circumstances in which an election may be made under  section
25C  may not be made unless a draft of the instrument containing the
regulations has been laid before, and approved by a resolution of, the House
of Commons.

Before section 27 insert the following italic heading—

  Rules relating to calculation of profits

.

13

Before section 30 insert the following italic heading—

  Animals kept for trade purposes

.

14

Before section 31 insert the following italic heading—

  Rules relating to deductions

.

##### Commencement and transitional provision

###### Commencement

47

The amendments made by this Schedule have effect for the tax year 2024-25 and
subsequent tax years.

###### Transitional provision

48

48.1

This paragraph has effect for the purposes of construing references in the
Income Tax Acts to the cash basis in relation to the calculation of the
profits of a trade (but not a property business) for a tax year before
2024-25.

48.2

Any reference to calculating the profits of a trade on the cash basis is to be
read as a reference to doing so in accordance with section 25A of ITTOIA 2005.

48.3

Any reference to the cash basis applying (or not applying) in relation to a
trade for the tax year is to be read as a reference to an election under
section 25A of ITTOIA 2005 having effect (or not having effect) in relation to
the trade for the tax year.

49

49.1

This paragraph has effect for the purposes of construing references in the
Income Tax Acts to a change in the basis of calculation of the profits of a
trade (but not a property business) for the tax year 2024-25.

49.2

A person carrying on a trade “ enters the cash basis ” in relation to the
trade in the tax year 2024-25 if—

49.2.a

the cash basis applies in relation to the trade for the tax year 2024-25, and

49.2.b

no election under section 25A of ITTOIA 2005 had effect in relation to the
trade for the tax year 2023-24,

and related expressions are to be construed accordingly.

49.3

A person carrying on a trade “ leaves the cash basis ” in relation to the
trade in the tax year 2024-25 if—

49.3.a

an election under section 25A of ITTOIA 2005 had effect in relation to the
trade for the tax year 2023-24, and

49.3.b

the cash basis does not apply in relation to the trade for the tax year
2024-25,

and related expressions are to be construed accordingly.

49.4

For the purposes of this paragraph, the cash basis applies to a trade in
relation to a tax year if the profits of the trade for the tax year are
required by virtue of  section 24A (1)  of ITTOIA 2005 to be calculated in
accordance with that section.

50

Paragraphs  48  and  49  apply to professions and vocations as they apply to
trades.

5

After section 72 (clearance services: supplementary) insert—

########## Meaning of “exempt capital-raising instrument” and “exempt listing instrument”

########### Meaning of “exempt capital-raising instrument”

5.72ZA

5.72ZA.1

For the purposes of sections 67 and 70, an instrument is an “exempt capital-
raising instrument” if the instrument transfers relevant securities in the
course of capital-raising arrangements.

5.72ZA.2

In this section, “ capital-raising arrangements ” means arrangements pursuant
to which relevant securities are issued by a company for the purpose of
raising new capital.

5.72ZA.3

An instrument is not prevented from being an exempt capital-raising instrument
by reason only of a delay in transferring relevant securities where—

5.72ZA.3.a

a person (“ the transferor ”) acquires the relevant securities—

5.72ZA.3.a.i

before capital-raising arrangements are entered into, or

5.72ZA.3.a.ii

in the course of capital-raising arrangements,

5.72ZA.3.b

the transferor is subject to a restriction that has the effect of preventing
the transfer of the relevant securities in the course of the capital-raising
arrangements, and

5.72ZA.3.c

the instrument transfers the relevant securities as soon as reasonably
practicable after the time at which the restriction ceases to have effect.

########### Meaning of “exempt listing instrument”

5.72ZB

5.72ZB.1

For the purposes of sections 67 and 70, an instrument is an “exempt listing
instrument” if—

5.72ZB.1.a

the instrument transfers relevant securities of a company in the course of
qualifying listing arrangements, and

5.72ZB.1.b

those arrangements do not affect the beneficial ownership of the relevant
securities.

5.72ZB.2

In this section, “ listing arrangements ” means arrangements pursuant to which
relevant securities, or depositary receipts for relevant securities, are
listed on a recognised stock exchange.

5.72ZB.3

For the purposes of this section, listing arrangements are “qualifying” if,
immediately before the first transfer of relevant securities in the course of
the listing arrangements, no relevant securities in the company or depositary
receipts for relevant securities in the company are listed on the recognised
stock exchange to which the listing arrangements relate.

5.72ZB.4

An instrument is not prevented from being an exempt listing instrument by
reason only of a delay in transferring relevant securities where—

5.72ZB.4.a

a person (“ the transferor ”) acquires the relevant securities before
qualifying listing arrangements are entered into,

5.72ZB.4.b

the transferor is subject to a restriction that has the effect of preventing
the transfer of the relevant securities in the course of the qualifying
listing arrangements, and

5.72ZB.4.c

the instrument transfers the relevant securities as soon as reasonably
practicable after the time at which the restriction ceases to have effect.

5.72ZB.5

Section 1005 of the Income Tax Act 2007 (meaning of “ recognised stock
exchange ”, “ listed ” etc) applies in relation to this section as it applies
in relation to the Income Tax Acts.

15

After section 97A insert—

########## Depositary receipts and clearance services: further exceptions

########### Exempt capital-raising transfers

15.97AB

15.97AB.1

There is to be no charge to tax under section 93 or 96 in respect of an exempt
capital-raising transfer.

15.97AB.2

For the purposes of  subsection (1) , a transfer of chargeable securities is
an “exempt capital-raising transfer” if the transfer is in the course of
capital-raising arrangements.

15.97AB.3

In this section, “ capital-raising arrangements ” means arrangements pursuant
to which chargeable securities are issued by a company for the purpose of
raising new capital.

15.97AB.4

A transfer of chargeable securities is not prevented from being an exempt
capital-raising transfer by reason only of a delay in transferring the
chargeable securities where—

15.97AB.4.a

a person (“ the transferor ”) acquires the chargeable securities—

15.97AB.4.a.i

before capital-raising arrangements are entered into, or

15.97AB.4.a.ii

in the course of capital-raising arrangements,

15.97AB.4.b

the transferor is subject to a restriction that has the effect of preventing
the transfer of the chargeable securities in the course of the capital-raising
arrangements, and

15.97AB.4.c

the transfer is made as soon as reasonably practicable after the time at which
the restriction ceases to have effect.

########### Exempt listing transfers

15.97AC

15.97AC.1

There is to be no charge to tax under section 93 or 96 in respect of an exempt
listing transfer.

15.97AC.2

For the purposes of  subsection (1) , a transfer of chargeable securities
issued by a company is an “exempt listing transfer” if—

15.97AC.2.a

it is a transfer in the course of qualifying listing arrangements, and

15.97AC.2.b

those arrangements do not affect the beneficial ownership of the chargeable
securities.

15.97AC.3

In this section, “ listing arrangements ” means arrangements pursuant to which
chargeable securities, or depositary receipts for chargeable securities, are
listed on a recognised stock exchange.

15.97AC.4

For the purposes of this section, listing arrangements are “qualifying” if,
immediately before the first transfer of chargeable securities in the course
of the listing arrangements, no chargeable securities in the company or
depositary receipts for chargeable securities in the company are listed on the
recognised stock exchange to which the listing arrangements relate.

15.97AC.5

A transfer of chargeable securities is not prevented from being an exempt
listing transfer by reason only of a delay in transferring the chargeable
securities where—

15.97AC.5.a

a person (“ the transferor ”) acquires the chargeable securities before
qualifying listing arrangements are entered into,

15.97AC.5.b

the transferor is subject to a restriction that has the effect of preventing
the transfer of the chargeable securities in the course of the qualifying
listing arrangements, and

15.97AC.5.c

the transfer is made as soon as reasonably practicable after the time at which
the restriction ceases to have effect.

15.97AC.6

Section 1005 of the Income Tax Act 2007 (meaning of “ recognised stock
exchange ”, “ listed ” etc) applies in relation to this section as it applies
in relation to the Income Tax Acts.

########### Exception for transfers of shares held by issuing company

15.97AD

There is to be no charge to tax under section 93 or 96 in respect of a
transfer of shares in a company which are held by the company (whether in
accordance with section 724 of the Companies Act 2006 (treasury shares) or
otherwise).

  Pillar Two

##### Introduction

.

1.2

The amendments made by those Parts have effect for accounting periods
beginning on or after 31 December 2023.

##### Multinational top-up tax

###### Partnerships

2

2.1

In section 122 (chargeable persons)—

2.1.a

in subsection (1)(a)(ii), omit “that is not a body corporate”,

2.1.b

in subsection (2)(c)(ii), omit “that is not a body corporate”, and

2.1.c

omit subsections (4) to (6).

2.2

After section 232, insert—

############ Partnerships

2.2.232A

2.2.232A.1

A partnership is to be regarded for the purposes of this Part as continuing to
be the same partnership regardless of a change in membership, provided that a
person who was a member before the change remains a member after the change.

2.2.232A.2

Where—

2.2.232A.2.a

ownership interests in a partnership are transferred to more than one
individual or entity, and

2.2.232A.2.b

the result is a partnership of which none of the original partners are
members,

that new partnership is to be treated as if it were the same partnership as
the old partnership.

2.2.232A.3

Where a partnership is otherwise dissolved in an accounting period—

2.2.232A.3.a

the partnership is to be treated as a continuing entity for the purpose of
dealing with its rights and obligations under this Part in respect of that
accounting period and previous accounting periods, and

2.2.232A.3.b

for the purposes of Schedule 14 (administration) each person who was a partner
in that accounting period (before the partnership’s dissolution) is to be
treated as a partner of the continuing entity.

2.2.232A.4

The reference in  subsection (2)  to a transfer of ownership interests
includes any series of transactions having the effect of a transfer (including
by way of the cancellation of interests and the issue of corresponding
interests).

2.3

In section 259 (other definitions), in subsection (1) at the appropriate place
insert—

      “ partnership ” does not include anything that is a body corporate;

2.4

After section 268 insert—

############ Partnerships

2.4.268A

Section 232A (partnerships) applies for the purposes of this Part as it
applies for the purposes of Part 3.

2.5

In section 269 (chargeable persons for domestic top-up tax)—

2.5.a

in subsection (1)—

2.5.a.i

in paragraph (a), omit “that is not a body corporate”, and

2.5.a.ii

in paragraph (b), omit “that is not a body corporate” in the second place it
occurs, and

2.5.b

omit subsections (4) to (6).

2.6

In Schedule 14 (administration of multinational top-up tax)—

2.6.a

in paragraph 3—

2.6.a.i

partnership”,

2.6.a.ii

in that sub-paragraph, omit paragraph (c), and

2.6.a.iii

for sub-paragraph (3) substitute—

2.6.a.iii.3

In this Schedule—

2.6.a.iii.3.a

“ limited partnership ” includes an entity established under the law of a
territory outside the United Kingdom that is equivalent to a limited
partnership, and

2.6.a.iii.3.b

“ general partner ” includes a partner of such an entity that corresponds to a
general partner.

2.6.a.iii.4

See also section 232A, which contains provision about the continuity of
partnerships which is relevant to this paragraph.

2.6.a.iii.5

Where an obligation of a partnership may be met by one of its partners and the
partnership does not comply with that obligation—

2.6.a.iii.5.a

an officer of Revenue and Customs may by notice require any such partner to
meet the obligation, and

2.6.a.iii.5.b

that partner is to be treated for that purpose as the filing member (and
accordingly may be subject to any penalty for a failure to comply).

,

2.6.b

after paragraph 37 insert—

############## Partnership payment notices

2.6.b.37A

2.6.b.37A.1

An officer of Revenue and Customs may issue a partnership payment notice if an
amount of multinational top-up tax payable by a member of a multinational
group that is a partnership (including any interest on that amount) is not
paid by the end of the period of three months beginning with the relevant date
(see paragraph 34(7) to (9)).

2.6.b.37A.2

A partnership payment notice may be issued to any person (wherever in the
world they are located) who—

2.6.b.37A.2.a

is a partner, or

2.6.b.37A.2.b

was a partner at any time in the accounting period to which the amount payable
relates.

2.6.b.37A.3

A partnership payment notice is a notice requiring the recipient to pay an
outstanding amount of multinational top-up tax payable by a member of the
group that is a partnership by a date specified in the notice.

2.6.b.37A.4

Sub-paragraphs (4) to (9) of paragraph 34 and paragraph 36 apply to a
partnership payment notice as they apply to a group payment notice.

2.6.b.37A.5

In this paragraph and in  paragraph 37B , reference to a partner, in the case
of a limited partnership, is to a general partner.

############## Recovery of partnership payment and effect for tax purposes etc

2.6.b.37B

2.6.b.37B.1

This paragraph applies where a partner of a member of a multinational group
that is a partnership (the “payer”) makes a payment in respect of the
liability to pay multinational top-up tax of the partnership (whether or not
in consequence of a partnership payment notice).

2.6.b.37B.2

The payer may recover the amount from the other partners.

2.6.b.37B.3

In calculating the payer's income, profits or losses for tax purposes—

2.6.b.37B.3.a

the payment is not allowed as a deduction, and

2.6.b.37B.3.b

the reimbursement of any such payment is not to be regarded as a receipt.

2.6.b.37B.4

The payment or its reimbursement—

2.6.b.37B.4.a

is not (otherwise) to be taken into account in calculating the profits or
losses of for corporation tax or income tax purposes of either the payer or
the other partners, and

2.6.b.37B.4.b

is not to be regarded as a distribution for income tax or corporation tax
purposes.

2.6.b.37B.5

The amount paid by the payer is to be taken into account in calculating—

2.6.b.37B.5.a

the amount of multinational top-up tax unpaid by the partnership, and

2.6.b.37B.5.b

the amount due by virtue of a partnership payment notice relating to the
amount unpaid.

2.6.b.37B.6

Similarly, any payment by the partnership or by any of the other partners of
any of the amount unpaid is to be taken into account in calculating the amount
due by virtue of a partnership payment notice (or by virtue of any other
partnership payment notice relating to the amount unpaid).

2.6.b.37B.7

In this paragraph, “ for tax purposes ” means for the purposes of income tax,
corporation tax, multinational top-up tax or domestic top-up tax.

, and

2.6.c

in paragraph 39—

2.6.c.i

omit the “or” after paragraph (a) in sub-paragraph (1),

2.6.c.ii

after that paragraph insert—

2.6.c.ii.aa

a partner of a partnership makes a payment on behalf of the partnership or
another partner, or

, and

2.6.c.iii

in sub-paragraph (2), after paragraph (a) insert—

2.6.c.iii.aa

deeming a payment made by a partner of a partnership to have been made by the
partnership or another partner;

.

;

###### Pension expense

7

For section 147 (accrued pension expense) substitute—

########## Accrued pension expense

7.147

7.147.1

This section applies in an accounting period where a member of a multinational
group—

7.147.1.a

has made contributions to a pension fund in the period,

7.147.1.b

has received amounts from the pension fund in the period, or

7.147.1.c

otherwise has amounts of income or expense relating to the pension fund
reflected in its underlying profits.

7.147.2

Take the amount of income or expense (expressed as a negative number where
expense) that has arisen directly in respect of the fund as reflected in the
member’s underlying profits and—

7.147.2.a

add the sum of contributions made to the fund by the member in the period, and

7.147.2.b

subtract any amount received by the member from the fund in the period.

7.147.3

If the result of subsection (2)—

7.147.3.a

is more than nil, reduce the underlying profits by that result, or

7.147.3.b

is less than nil, increase the underlying profits by that result (as expressed
a positive number).

###### Tax credits

8

8.1

After section 147 insert—

############ Treatment of tax credits

8.1.147A

8.1.147A.1

The underlying profits of a member of a multinational group, and the covered
tax balance of that member (see Chapter 5), are to be adjusted (if necessary)
to secure that—

8.1.147A.1.a

qualifying refundable tax credits are accounted for as income rather than as
tax expense,

8.1.147A.1.b

tax credits that are marketable transferable tax credits in relation to the
member are accounted for as income rather than as tax expense, and

8.1.147A.1.c

other tax credits are accounted for as tax expense rather than as income.

8.1.147A.2

Section 148 sets out when tax credits are qualifying refundable tax credits.

8.1.147A.3

Section  148A  sets out the meaning of “transferable tax credit” and
“marketable transferable tax credit”.

8.1.147A.4

Sections  148B  and  148C  set out rules about the value of marketable
transferable tax credits.

8.1.147A.5

Sections  176A  to  176C  (in Chapter 5) set out rules about the value of tax
credits that are not marketable transferable tax credits but which are
transferable or were transferred (and which as a result of  subsection (1) (c)
are generally to be accounted for as tax expense).

8.1.147A.6

See also sections  176D  to  176F  which contain special rules for tax credits
received in under a tax equity partnership arrangement.

8.2

In section 148 (treatment of qualifying refundable tax credits)—

8.2.a

in the heading, for “Treatment” substitute  “Meaning” ,

8.2.b

omit subsection (1), and

8.2.c

in subsection (4)(b), omit “tax”.

8.3

After that section insert—

############ Transferable tax credits

8.3.148A

8.3.148A.1

A tax credit is a transferable tax credit in relation to a member of a
multinational group if—

8.3.148A.1.a

the member is—

8.3.148A.1.a.i

the person to whom the credit was originally granted (“the originator”), or

8.3.148A.1.a.ii

a person (“a purchaser”) who has acquired the credit (whether from the
originator or anyone else), and

8.3.148A.1.b

the transferability condition is met in relation to the member.

8.3.148A.2

A transferable tax credit is a marketable transferable tax credit in relation
to a member of a multinational group if—

8.3.148A.2.a

it is a transferable tax credit, and

8.3.148A.2.b

the marketable condition is met in relation to the member.

8.3.148A.3

Those conditions are met differently depending on whether the member is the
originator or a purchaser.

8.3.148A.4

The transferability condition is met—

8.3.148A.4.a

in relation to the originator if, under the law of the territory in which the
credit was granted, credits of that type may be transferred to a person or
entity that is not connected with originator before the end of 15 months after
the end of the accounting period in which the credit is granted, and

8.3.148A.4.b

in relation to a purchaser if, under the law of that territory, credits of
that type may be transferred to a person or entity that is not connected with
the purchaser—

8.3.148A.4.b.i

under the same or similar conditions as would apply to the originator, and

8.3.148A.4.b.ii

before the end of the accounting period in which it was transferred to the
purchaser.

8.3.148A.5

The marketable condition is met—

8.3.148A.5.a

in relation to the originator, if—

8.3.148A.5.a.i

the credit is transferred to a person or entity that is not connected with the
originator before the end of 15 months of the accounting period in which the
credit was granted at a price equal to or in excess of 80% of its net present
value, or

8.3.148A.5.a.ii

similar credits are traded between persons or entities that are not connected
to each other before the end of 15 months of the accounting period in which
they are granted, and are typically traded at a price equal to or in excess of
80% of their net present value, and

8.3.148A.5.b

in relation to a purchaser, if the purchaser acquired the credit from a person
or entity that is not connected to the purchaser at a price equal to or in
excess of 80% of its net present value.

8.3.148A.6

Subsections  (7)  and  (8)  apply for the purposes of determining the net
present value of a tax credit.

8.3.148A.7

In making that determination, assume that the entity that holds it will be
able to use it in the accounting periods in which it may be used.

8.3.148A.8

The discount rate to be used in making that determination is to be determined
by reference to the return on debt instruments that are issued by the
government of the territory in which the credit was granted—

8.3.148A.8.a

that have—

8.3.148A.8.a.i

the same, or a similar, maturity to the period over which the credit is to be
used, or

8.3.148A.8.a.ii

in a case in which the credit is to be used over a period exceeding 5 years, a
maturity of 5 years, and

8.3.148A.8.b

that are issued—

8.3.148A.8.b.i

in relation to a credit that has been transferred, in the accounting period in
which the credit was transferred, or

8.3.148A.8.b.ii

in relation to a credit held that has not been transferred, in the accounting
period in which it was granted.

8.3.148A.9

References in  subsections (6)  and  (8)  to an accounting period are—

8.3.148A.9.a

in relation to determining net present value in connection with determining
whether the marketable condition is met by the originator, an accounting
period of the originator, and

8.3.148A.9.b

in relation to determining net present value in connection with determining
whether the marketable condition is met by a purchaser, an accounting period
of the purchaser.

8.3.148A.10

Where a transferable tax credit is also a qualifying refundable tax credit, it
is to be treated as not being a transferable tax credit for the purposes of
this Part.

############ Value of marketable transferable tax credits: originator

8.3.148B

8.3.148B.1

The underlying profits of a member of a multinational group that is the
originator in relation to a marketable transferable tax credit are to be
adjusted to secure that the value of marketable transferable tax credits it
holds, and has held, as originator are reflected as follows.

8.3.148B.2

Where the credit is not transferred before the end of 15 months after the end
of the accounting period in which it was granted, the full value of the credit
is to be recognised as income.

8.3.148B.3

Where the credit is subsequently transferred for consideration which is less
than the value of the credit, the difference between the value of the credit
and the consideration received for its transfer is to be recognised as a loss
in the accounting period in which it is transferred.

8.3.148B.4

Where the credit is transferred before the end of 15 months after the end of
the accounting period in which the credit is granted, the consideration for
the transfer (rather than the value of the credit) is to be recognised as
income.

8.3.148B.5

Where the credit has not been transferred, and was not fully used, before its
expiry, the value of so much of the credit as has not been used is to be
reflected as a loss in the accounting period in which the credit expired.

############ Value of marketable transferable tax credits: purchaser

8.3.148C

8.3.148C.1

The underlying profits of a member of a multinational group that is the
purchaser in relation to a marketable transferable tax credit are to be
adjusted to secure that the value of marketable transferable tax credits it
holds, and has held, as purchaser are reflected as follows.

8.3.148C.2

On using an amount of the credit in an accounting period, the amount given by
subsection (3) is to be recognised as income.

8.3.148C.3

That amount is the amount given by multiplying—

8.3.148C.3.a

the amount used divided by the full value of the credit, by

8.3.148C.3.b

the amount given by subtracting the purchase price of the credit from the full
value of the credit.

8.3.148C.4

On transferring the credit, the amount in subsection (5) is to be reflected in
the underlying profits for the accounting period in which the transfer
occurred—

8.3.148C.4.a

if positive, as a gain, or

8.3.148C.4.b

if negative, as a loss.

8.3.148C.5

That amount is the amount given by subtracting—

8.3.148C.5.a

the sum of—

8.3.148C.5.a.i

the purchase price of the credit, and

8.3.148C.5.a.ii

any amounts recognised as income in accordance with subsection (2) (whether in
that accounting period or a previous accounting period), from

8.3.148C.5.b

the sum of—

8.3.148C.5.b.i

the amount of the credit that has been used, and

8.3.148C.5.b.ii

the consideration for the transfer.

8.3.148C.6

Where the credit has not been transferred, and was not fully used, before its
expiry, the amount in subsection (7) is to be reflected as a loss in the
accounting period in which the credit expired.

8.3.148C.7

That amount is the amount given by subtracting—

8.3.148C.7.a

the amount of the credit that was used, from

8.3.148C.7.b

the sum of the purchase price of the credit and any amounts recognised in
accordance with subsection (2).

8.4

In section 175 (amounts excluded from covered tax balance), in subsection (2),
in paragraph (c), after “credit”, in the second place it occurs, insert  “, or
in respect of a marketable transferable tax credit,” .

8.5

In section 176 (amounts to be reflected in covered tax balance), in subsection
(2)—

8.5.a

in paragraph (d), in sub-paragraph (i), after “credit” insert  “or a
marketable transferable tax credit” , and

8.5.b

in paragraph (e), after “credit” insert  “or a marketable transferable tax
credit” .

8.6

After section 176 insert—

############ Transferable tax credits

############# Meaning of “non-marketable transferable tax credits”

8.6.176A

8.6.176A.1

Sections  176B  and  176C  make provision about “non-marketable transferable
tax credits”.

8.6.176A.2

A tax credit held by a member of a multinational group that is the originator
of the credit is a non-marketable transferable tax credit if—

8.6.176A.2.a

it may be transferred to another person or entity, and

8.6.176A.2.b

it is neither a marketable transferable tax credit nor a qualifying refundable
tax credit.

8.6.176A.3

A tax credit held by a member of a multinational group as a purchaser of the
credit is a non-marketable transferable tax credit if it is neither a
marketable transferable tax credit nor a qualifying refundable tax credit.

8.6.176A.4

In this section and in sections  176B  and  176C  “originator” and “purchaser”
are to be construed in accordance with  section 148A (1) (a) .

############# Value of non-marketable transferable tax credits: originator

8.6.176B

8.6.176B.1

The covered tax balance of a member of a multinational group that holds a non-
marketable transferable tax credit as originator is to be adjusted to secure
that the value of the credit is reflected as follows.

8.6.176B.2

The value of the tax credit is to be reflected as it is used.

8.6.176B.3

If the credit is transferred (after the end of the period of 15 months after
the accounting period in which the credit is granted), the consideration for
the transfer is to be reflected as a credit in the accounting period in which
the transfer occurred.

############# Value of non-marketable transferable tax credits: purchaser

8.6.176C

8.6.176C.1

The covered tax balance of a member of a multinational group that holds a non-
marketable transferable tax credit as purchaser is to be adjusted to secure
that the value the credit is reflected as follows.

8.6.176C.2

On using an amount of the credit, the amount given by subsection (3) is to be
reflected as a credit in the covered tax balance for the accounting period in
which it is used.

8.6.176C.3

That amount is the amount given by multiplying—

8.6.176C.3.a

the amount used divided by the full value of the credit, by

8.6.176C.3.b

the amount given by subtracting the purchase price of the credit from the full
value of the credit.

8.6.176C.4

On transferring the credit, the amount in subsection (5) is—

8.6.176C.4.a

if positive, to be reflected as a credit in the covered tax balance for the
accounting period in which the transfer occurred, or

8.6.176C.4.b

if negative, to be reflected as a loss in the underlying profits of the member
for that period.

8.6.176C.5

That amount is the amount given by subtracting—

8.6.176C.5.a

the sum of—

8.6.176C.5.a.i

the purchase price of the credit, and

8.6.176C.5.a.ii

any amounts recognised reflected in the covered tax balance in accordance with
subsection (2) (whether in that accounting period or a previous accounting
period), from

8.6.176C.5.b

the sum of—

8.6.176C.5.b.i

the amount of the credit that has been used, and

8.6.176C.5.b.ii

the consideration for the transfer.

8.6.176C.6

Where the credit has not been transferred, and was not fully used, before its
expiry, the amount in subsection (7) is to be reflected as a loss in the
underlying profits of the member for the accounting period in which the credit
expired.

8.6.176C.7

That amount is the amount given by subtracting—

8.6.176C.7.a

the amount of the credit that was used, from

8.6.176C.7.b

the sum of the purchase price of the credit and any amounts recognised in
accordance with subsection (2).

###### Exclusion of certain insurance reserve movement expense

###### Tax equity partnerships

16

16.1

After section  176C  (as inserted by  paragraph 8 ), insert—

############ Tax equity partnerships

############# Tax credits etc allocated under tax equity partnerships

16.1.176D

16.1.176D.1

Where—

16.1.176D.1.a

a member of a multinational group is an investor in a tax equity partnership
arrangement, and

16.1.176D.1.b

an election under section 165 (excluded equity gains and losses included)
applies in relation to the member for an accounting period,

qualifying flow-through tax benefits provided to the member under that
arrangement in that period are to be excluded from the covered tax balance of
that member for that period.

16.1.176D.2

“ Flow-through tax benefits ” means tax credits, other than qualifying
refundable tax credits, and the value of amounts of tax deductible losses made
available to be used by an investor in a tax equity partnership arrangement
under that arrangement (whether or not those credits or losses are used by the
investor).

16.1.176D.3

Section  176E  (proportional amortisation method) applies for the purposes of
determining the extent to which flow-through tax benefits are “qualifying”
where—

16.1.176D.3.a

in determining the underlying profits of the investor, the proportional
amortisation method is used to account for the arrangement, or

16.1.176D.3.b

the filing member of the multinational group of which the investor is a member
has elected that section 176D should apply for those purposes in relation to
the member.

16.1.176D.4

Otherwise, section  176F  (subtraction method) applies for those purposes.

16.1.176D.5

For the purposes of this Part, a member of a multinational group is an
investor in a tax equity partnership arrangement if—

16.1.176D.5.a

the member has made an investment in an entity that is tax transparent in the
territory in which the member is located,

16.1.176D.5.b

the investment is treated as an equity interest for tax purposes in the
territory in which the member is located,

16.1.176D.5.c

the investment would, under an authorised accounting standard of the territory
in which the entity operates, be treated as an equity interest,

16.1.176D.5.d

the entity is not a member of the multinational group, and

16.1.176D.5.e

it is reasonable to expect, at the time of making the investment, that the
return on the investment would be negative in the absence of the provision of
flow-through tax benefits.

16.1.176D.6

But a member of a multinational group is not to be regarded as an investor in
a tax equity partnership arrangement if—

16.1.176D.6.a

the investment in the entity does not represent a genuine economic interest in
that entity such that the member is exposed to the possibility of a loss on
the investment, or

16.1.176D.6.b

the territory in which the member is located limits the use of tax equity
partnership arrangements to arrangements that involve a multinational group
subject to multinational top-up tax or its equivalent under the law of a
territory outside the United Kingdom.

16.1.176D.7

Flow-through tax benefits provided to a member of a multinational group in an
accounting period that are not qualifying are to be reflected as a credit in
the covered tax balance for that period.

16.1.176D.8

Flow-through tax benefits (whether qualifying or not) provided to a member of
a multinational group are not to be reflected in the underlying profits of
that member, even if that would be the effect of the election under section
165.

16.1.176D.9

For the purposes of  subsection (3) (a) , the “ proportional amortisation
method ” means a method of accounting under which—

16.1.176D.9.a

the initial capital investment in the arrangement is amortised over the term
of the investment with the amortisation expense for an accounting period based
on the proportion of the flow-through tax benefits expected to be provided
over the term of the arrangement that are expected to be provided in that
period, and

16.1.176D.9.b

the difference between the flow-through tax benefits received in an accounting
period and that amortisation expense for that period is reflected as tax
expense.

16.1.176D.10

For the purposes of this section and sections  176E  and  176F , the value of
an amount of tax deductible losses made available to be used by an investor is
given by multiplying the amount multiplied by the tax rate that applies to the
investor.

16.1.176D.11

Paragraph 2 of Schedule 15 (annual elections) applies to an election under
subsection (3) (b) .

############# Flow-through tax benefits: proportional amortisation method

16.1.176E

16.1.176E.1

Where this section applies, to determine the extent to which flow-through tax
benefits provided to an investor in an accounting period under a tax equity
partnership arrangement are qualifying, take the following steps—

      Step 1       Determine the amount of capital investment provided by the
investor to the arrangement at its commencement.           Step 2       Divide
the flow-through through tax benefits provided under the arrangement in the
accounting period by the total flow-through tax benefits expected to be
provided over the whole term of the arrangement.           Step 3
Multiply the result of Step 1 by the result of Step 2.           Step 4
Add the following together—         the amounts, if any, of tax credits made
available to be used by the investor under the arrangement in the accounting
period;           the value of the amounts, if any, of tax deductible losses
made available to be used by the investor under the arrangement in the
accounting period;           the amounts, if any, of distributions made to the
investor in the accounting period;           the amounts, if any, received by
the investor for the sale of any part of its investment in the arrangement in
the accounting period.                 Step 5       If the result of Step 3 is
equal to or greater than the result of Step 4, all of the flow-through tax
benefits provided under the arrangement in the accounting period are
qualifying.       Otherwise proceed to Step 6.           Step 6       Subtract
the result of Step 3 from the result of Step 4.           Step 7       The
amount of the flow-through benefits provided under the arrangement in the
accounting period that is qualifying is the amount given by reducing the
amount of those benefits (but not below nil) by the result of Step 6.

16.1.176E.2

Accordingly, the amount by which those benefits are reduced in accordance with
Step 7 represents non-qualifying flow-through tax benefits which are to be
reflected as a credit in the investor’s covered tax balance.

############# Flow-through tax benefits: subtraction method

16.1.176F

Where this section applies, to determine the extent to which flow-through tax
benefits provided to an investor in an accounting period under a tax equity
partnership arrangement are qualifying, take the following steps—

      Step 1       Determine the amount of capital investment provided by the
investor to the arrangement at its commencement.           Step 2
Subtract the following from that amount—         the amounts, if any, of tax
credits made available to be used by the investor under the arrangement since
the commencement of the arrangement, other than tax credits that are not
qualifying refundable tax credits that were made available in the accounting
period;           the value of the amounts, if any, of tax deductible losses
made available to be used by the investor under the arrangement since its
commencement, other than losses made available in the accounting period;
the amounts, if any, of distributions made to the investor since the
arrangement’s commencement;           the amounts, if any, received by the
investor for the sale of any part of its investment in the arrangement.
Step 3       If the result of Step 2 is nil or less, no flow-through tax
benefits provided under arrangement in the accounting period are qualifying.
If the result of that step is more than nil, proceed to Step 4.           Step
4       Subtract the flow-through tax benefits provided to the investor in the
accounting period under the arrangement from the result of Step 2.
Step 5       If the result of Step 4 is nil or greater, all of the flow-
through tax benefits provided under the arrangement in the accounting period
are qualifying.       Otherwise, the amount of those benefits that is
qualifying is the amount of those benefits that when subtracted from the
result of Step 2 would give a result of nil.

16.2

In Schedule 15 (elections), in paragraph 2(1), before paragraph (a) insert—

16.2.za

section 176D (3) (b) ;

.

17.4.1A

17.4.1A.a

expense,

17.4.1A.b

profits, and

17.4.1A.c

that qualifying current tax expense is to be allocated to O (and is to be

17.4.1B

included in adjusted profits) applies to an amount of qualifying current tax
expense allocated in accordance with subsection (1) as if—

17.4.1B.a

17.4.1B.b

amount not allocated remains with C.

17.7.b.3B

But if an amount would, ignoring this subsection, remain with C and that
amount relates to income or gains that are not included in the adjusted
profits of F, that amount is to be excluded from the covered tax balance of
both C and F.

20.5

After section 183 insert—

############ Alternative to section 183 where carry forward of credits not permitted

20.5.183A

20.5.183A.1

A special foreign tax asset of a member of a multinational group is to be used
to increase its covered tax balance in accordance with this section.

20.5.183A.2

Subsection (3) applies where—

20.5.183A.2.a

the territory in which a member of a multinational group is located requires
that domestic losses are offset against relevant foreign income before foreign
tax credits can be applied against tax on foreign income,

20.5.183A.2.b

the territory limits the extent to which foreign tax credits can be applied
against tax in a taxable period,

20.5.183A.2.c

the territory allows foreign tax credits to be used to a greater extent where
a domestic loss has been used to offset (in whole or in part) relevant foreign
income in a prior period, and

20.5.183A.2.d

the member has used a domestic loss to offset (in whole or in part) relevant
foreign income.

20.5.183A.3

Where this subsection applies, the member has a special foreign tax asset
arising in the accounting period in which the loss was used.

20.5.183A.4

The amount of that special foreign tax asset is the amount of the domestic
loss used to offset relevant foreign income multiplied by the lesser of—

20.5.183A.4.a

the nominal rate of tax in the member’s territory for the taxable period in
which it was used, and

20.5.183A.4.b

15%.

20.5.183A.5

Where a member of a multinational group has a special foreign tax asset that
arose in any previous accounting period, the member is to use that amount to
increase its covered tax balance.

20.5.183A.6

The amount of the special foreign tax asset that is to be used in an
accounting period is the lesser of—

20.5.183A.6.a

the amount of the asset, and

20.5.183A.6.b

so much of the amount of foreign tax credits credited against tax in the
taxable period corresponding to that accounting period as is capable of being
credited only as a result of the prior use of the domestic loss.

Any remainder continues to be a special foreign tax asset (and is available
for use in subsequent account periods where subsection (5) applies).

###### Substance based income exclusion: leases

25

25.1

In section 195 (calculation of substance based income exclusion), after
subsection (7) insert—

25.1.7A

Section 197A sets out the treatment of operating leases.

25.2

After section 197 insert—

############ Operating leases

25.2.197A

25.2.197A.1

Subsection (2) applies where—

25.2.197A.1.a

a member of a multinational group holds property located in the same territory
as the member in an accounting period,

25.2.197A.1.b

that property is held for lease by the member, and

25.2.197A.1.c

the lease is accounted for in the underlying profits accounts of the member as
an operating lease for that period.

25.2.197A.2

The operating lease is to be regarded as an eligible tangible asset of the
member for that period (despite the exclusion in section 197(7)(a)).

25.2.197A.3

But where the property is not a short-term rental asset for that period, any
carrying value of the operating lease recorded at the start or the end of the
period is to be reduced by the right-of-use amount for the property at that
time for the purposes of carrying out the calculation in section 197(1).

25.2.197A.4

In a case where the lessee is a member of the same multinational group as the
lessor, the right-of-use amount in relation to the property at the start or
the end of the period is the carrying value of the lessee’s right-of-use asset
in relation to the property recorded at that time.

25.2.197A.5

Where the lessee is not a member of the same multinational group as the
lessor, the right-of-use amount in relation to the property at the start or
end of the period is the undiscounted value of any outstanding payments under
the lease at that time.

25.2.197A.6

In determining the value of those outstanding payments—

25.2.197A.6.a

apply the accounting standard used in determining the underlying profits of
the member,

25.2.197A.6.b

include the value of any outstanding payments that would be due under any
extension to the lease that would fall to be accounted for in accordance with
that standard.

25.2.197A.7

For the purposes of this section, property held for lease is a short-term
rental asset in an accounting period if—

25.2.197A.7.a

the property was leased regularly during that period to different lessees, and

25.2.197A.7.b

the average length of the periods for which it was leased does not exceed 30
days.

###### Substance based income exclusion: power to make further provision

26

After section 198 insert—

########## Power to make provision about treatment of payroll costs and assets

26.198A

26.198A.1

The Treasury may by regulations make provision about the treatment of payroll
costs and tangible assets in specified circumstances.

26.198A.2

Regulations may, in particular, provide that in determining the substance
based income exclusion for a territory—

26.198A.2.a

specified eligible tangible assets or eligible payroll costs are to be treated
as having a different value;

26.198A.2.b

specified eligible tangible assets or eligible payroll costs are to be
attributed to a different member of a multinational group or to a different
territory;

26.198A.2.c

specified eligible tangible assets or eligible payroll costs are to be
excluded from that determination;

26.198A.2.d

specified assets that are not eligible tangible assets are to be treated as
eligible tangible assets;

26.198A.2.e

specified costs that are not eligible payroll costs are to be treated as
eligible payroll costs.

26.198A.3

In this section “ specified ” means specified or described in regulations.

###### Meaning of country-by-country report

29

29.1

After section 251 insert—

############ Meaning of country-by-country report

29.1.251A

29.1.251A.1

In this Part “ country-by-country report ” means a country-by-country report
in respect of a multinational group that is prepared and filed in accordance
with legislation implementing the OECD’s guidance on country-by-country
reporting.

29.1.251A.2

But where the legislation of a territory permits the preparation and filing of
a partial country-by country report, such a partial report is not to be
regarded as country-by-country report for the purposes of this Part.

29.1.251A.3

Reference to a country-by-country report in respect of a multinational group
that is a multi-parent group is to a report in respect of all of the
constituent groups.

29.1.251A.4

“ The OECD’s guidance on country-by-country reporting ” means the guidance on
country-by-country reporting contained in the Organisation for Economic Co-
operation and Development (“ OECD ”) Guidance on Transfer Pricing
Documentation and Country-by-Country Reporting, published in 2014, as
modified, supplemented or replaced from time to time.

29.2

In Schedule 16 (transitional provision), in paragraph 3, for sub-paragraphs
(7) and (8) substitute—

29.2.7

For the purposes of this Part of this Schedule, a country-by-country report in
relation to a territory is “qualifying” if the information relating to the
territory is prepared on the basis of qualified financial statements of the
multinational group (see paragraph 4).

29.2.8

Where there is no requirement under the law of any territory for a country-by-
country report to be prepared and filed in respect of a multinational group,
the filling member may include, in the information return in which the
election is made, the information that would have been in such a report—

29.2.8.a

prepared in accordance with legislation implementing the OECD’s guidance on
country-by-country reporting under the law of the territory of the ultimate
parent, or

29.2.8.b

where there is no such legislation, prepared in accordance with that guidance.

29.2.9

Where such information has been included in that information return, that
information is to be treated as if it were a country-by-country report in
relation to the territory for the purposes of this Chapter (and where that
information complies with sub-paragraph (7), the condition in sub-paragraph
(2)(b) is to be treated as met).

29.3

In section 276(b)(i) (application of transitional provision for domestic top-
up tax purposes), for “and (8)” substitute  “to (9)” .
