###### Currency

33

33.1

For section 254 (use of currency) substitute—

############ Use of currency

33.1.254

33.1.254.1

Calculations under this Part in relation to a multinational group, or any
member of such a group, are to be carried out in the currency of the
consolidated financial statements of the ultimate parent (“the CFS currency”).

33.1.254.2

Where it is necessary to convert an amount into the CFS currency, that
conversion is to be made in accordance with the authorised accounting
standard—

33.1.254.2.a

that was used in preparing the consolidated financial statements of the
ultimate parent, or

33.1.254.2.b

where no such statements were prepared, that is used as the basis for the
statements that would have been prepared.

33.1.254.3

For the purpose of comparing an amount to a figure expressed in this Part in
euros, the amount is to be converted to euros for that purpose (from the CFS
currency) by reference to the average exchange rate for the month of December
that preceded the beginning of the accounting period to which the amount
relates.

33.1.254.4

Where the European Central Bank publishes exchange rates for the CFS currency,
use those rates for the purposes of the conversion under subsection (3) and
any conversion under step 4 in section 123 (amount charged by reference to
top-up amounts).

33.1.254.5

Otherwise—

33.1.254.5.a

where the Bank of England publishes exchange rates for the CFS currency, use
those rates for the purposes of that conversion, or

33.1.254.5.b

where the Bank of England does not publish exchange rates for that currency,
use such a rate as appears, on a just and reasonable basis, to reflect the
average exchange rate for the period in question.

33.2

In section 123 (amount charged by reference to “top-up amounts”), for Step 4
substitute—

      Step 4       Convert the result of Step 3 (which in accordance with
section 254 will be expressed in the CFS currency) to sterling using the
average exchange rate for the accounting period (if the CFS currency is not
sterling).

###### Qualifying domestic top-up tax not treated as accruing

35

35.1

After section 256 insert—

############ Qualifying domestic top-up tax treated as not accruing where contested etc

35.1.256A

35.1.256A.1

Subsection  (2)  applies for the purposes of sections 194(2) to (7), 203(3) to
(7) and 206(4) to (8) (application of QDT credits in determination of top-up
amounts).

35.1.256A.2

An amount of qualifying domestic tax accruing to a member of a multinational
group is to be treated as not accruing to the member where the enforceability
of the amount is in question.

35.1.256A.3

For the purposes of this section, the enforceability of an amount of
qualifying domestic top-up tax accruing to a member of a multinational group
is in question if—

35.1.256A.3.a

the member disputes its enforceability on any of the grounds set out in
subsection (4) , or

35.1.256A.3.b

the tax authority of the territory in which the qualifying domestic top-up tax
is imposed considers the amount unenforceable on the basis of any of those
grounds.

35.1.256A.4

Those grounds are that—

35.1.256A.4.a

the amount is unenforceable on constitutional grounds or as a result of other
superior law applying in the territory in which the qualifying domestic top-up
tax is imposed, or

35.1.256A.4.b

the amount is unenforceable as a result of a specific agreement with the
government of that territory as to the tax liability of the member or the
group.

35.1.256A.5

Subsection  (2)  ceases to apply where the enforceability of an amount of
qualifying domestic top-up tax ceases to be in question.

35.1.256A.6

Where the enforceability of an amount of qualifying domestic top-up tax was in
question, it ceases to be in question where—

35.1.256A.6.a

the amount has been paid, and

35.1.256A.6.b

the enforceability of the amount may no longer be disputed as a result of—

35.1.256A.6.b.i

a settlement,

35.1.256A.6.b.ii

the time for any appeal having passed and there being no reasonable prospect
of the time being extended, or

35.1.256A.6.b.iii

the exhaustion of any rights to appeal.

35.2

In section 194 (total top-up amount for a territory), in subsection (3), for
“section 256” substitute  “sections 256 and 256A” .

###### Consistency with Pillar Two rules

36

In section 262 (power to amend to ensure consistency with Pillar Two) after
subsection (1) insert—

36.1A

The provision that may be made by regulations under subsection (1) includes
provision designed to secure the effective implementation of the Pillar Two
rules including—

36.1A.a

provision to ensure consistency with commentaries or guidance published by the
OECD that has effect from a time before the commentary or guidance was
published;

36.1A.b

provision that the Treasury consider necessary to secure the effective
operation of multinational top-up tax or domestic top-up tax (see Part 4)
where—

36.1A.b.i

the provision does not, at the time of making it, reflect the Pillar Two
rules, but

36.1A.b.ii

it is reasonable for the Treasury to believe that changes will be made to the
rules that are consistent with, or are similar to, the provision.

36.1B

Provision made by regulations under subsection (1) may not have effect—

36.1B.a

in the case of provision falling within subsection (1A)(a), in relation to
accounting periods ending before the commentary or guidance was published, or

36.1B.b

in the case of any other provision, in relation to accounting periods ending
before the regulations are made.

36.1C

Provision that has effect in relation to accounting periods that begin before
the regulations are made may only be made if the Treasury consider that the
provision is generally beneficial to—

36.1C.a

persons affected by the implementation of the Pillar Two rules, or

36.1C.b

persons affected by the provision.

36.1D

The reference in subsection (1C) to provision being generally beneficial
includes the provision being beneficial by reference to it—

36.1D.a

simplifying, or reducing the costs of, compliance with—

36.1D.a.i

multinational top-up tax or domestic top-up tax, or

36.1D.a.ii

taxes imposed under the law of a territory outside the United Kingdom that
correspond to multinational top-up tax or domestic top-up tax;

36.1D.b

generally (but not necessarily in every case) resulting in a reduction or
elimination of a liability to—

36.1D.b.i

multinational top-up tax or domestic top-up tax, or

36.1D.b.ii

taxes imposed under the law of a territory outside the United Kingdom that
correspond to multinational top-up tax or domestic top-up tax.

###### Qualifying domestic top-up tax safe harbour

41

41.1

After Schedule 16 insert—

  Multinational top-up tax: safe harbours

Section 260

############## Qualifying domestic top-up tax safe harbour

############### Qualifying domestic top-up tax safe harbour election

################ Election for qualifying domestic top-up tax safe harbour

41.1.1

41.1.1.1

The filing member of a multinational group may make a qualifying domestic top-
up tax safe harbour election for an accounting period in respect of a
territory.

41.1.1.2

The effect of the election is that all of the standard members of the group
located in the territory are to be treated as not having top-up amounts or
additional top-up amounts for the purpose of determining the liability of any
member of the group to multinational top-up tax.

41.1.1.3

An election may only be made for an accounting period if—

41.1.1.3.a

a qualifying domestic top-up tax applies in that territory for that period,

41.1.1.3.b

that tax is accredited for the purposes of the election (see  paragraph 2 ),
and

41.1.1.3.c

none of the disqualifying conditions in  paragraph 3  apply for that period.

41.1.1.4

Paragraph 2 of Schedule 15 (annual elections) applies to an election under
this paragraph.

################ Accredited qualifying domestic top-up tax

41.1.2

A qualifying domestic top-up tax is accredited for the purposes of an election
under  paragraph 1  if that tax is specified as such in regulations made by
the Treasury.

################ Disqualifying conditions

41.1.3

41.1.3.1

Conditions A to D are disqualifying conditions for the purposes of  paragraph
1 (3) (c)  in relation to a multinational group and a territory.

41.1.3.2

Condition A is that—

41.1.3.2.a

the ultimate parent is located in the territory,

41.1.3.2.b

the ultimate parent is a flow-through entity, and

41.1.3.2.c

the qualifying domestic top-up tax applying in the territory—

41.1.3.2.c.i

does not generally impose a charge on the ultimate parent as a result of it
being a flow-through entity, and

41.1.3.2.c.ii

does not include provision for a charge to be imposed on the ultimate parent
in circumstances where there would otherwise be an amount of tax that was not
charged to any member of the group in that territory.

41.1.3.3

Condition B is that—

41.1.3.3.a

a responsible member of the group is located in the territory,

41.1.3.3.b

the member is not the ultimate parent of the group,

41.1.3.3.c

the member is a flow-through entity, and

41.1.3.3.d

the qualifying domestic top-up tax applying in the territory—

41.1.3.3.d.i

does not generally impose a charge on the member as a result of it being a
flow-through entity, and

41.1.3.3.d.ii

does not include provision for a charge to be imposed on the member in
circumstances where there would otherwise be an amount of tax that was not
charged to any member of the group in that territory.

41.1.3.4

Condition C is that—

41.1.3.4.a

the qualifying domestic top-up tax applying in the territory provides that it
does not apply to a multinational group in the initial phase of the group’s
international expansion,

41.1.3.4.b

that provision is not limited in application to circumstances where the
members of a multinational group in the territory are not subject to Pillar
Two rules, and

41.1.3.4.c

that provision applies to the group.

41.1.3.5

Condition D is that the enforceability of an amount of qualifying domestic
top-up tax accruing to a standard member of the group is in question.

41.1.3.6

Subsections  (3) ,  (4)  and  (6)  of section 256A (qualifying domestic top-up
tax treated as not accruing where contested) apply for the purpose of
determining whether the enforceability of an amount of qualifying domestic
top-up tax is in question.

############### Application to non-standard members of a multinational group

################ Application in the case of joint venture group

41.1.4

41.1.4.1

For the purpose of applying Chapter 1 of this Part of this Schedule to a joint
venture group (see section 227 which applies this Schedule generally, with
modifications, to joint venture groups), that Chapter has effect as if in
paragraph 3—

41.1.4.1.a

in sub-paragraph (1), for “Conditions A to D” there were substituted
“Conditions A to E” ,

41.1.4.1.b

after sub-paragraph (6), there were inserted—

41.1.4.1.b.7

Condition E is that the qualifying domestic top-up tax applying in the
territory—

41.1.4.1.b.7.a

does not generally impose a charge on members of the group that are members of
a joint venture group, and

41.1.4.1.b.7.b

does not include provision for a charge to be imposed on such members in
circumstances where there would otherwise be an amount of tax that was not
charged to any member of the group in that territory.

41.1.4.2

For that purpose ignore section 227(1)(a) (reference to ultimate parent
treated as reference to joint venture parent).

41.1.4.3

Accordingly, the filing member of a multinational group may make a separate
qualifying domestic top-up tax safe harbour election in respect of joint
venture members of a joint venture group in a territory.

################ Application in the case of investment entities

41.1.5

41.1.5.1

Chapter 1 of this Part of this Schedule to applies to investment entities and
has effect for that purpose as if—

41.1.5.1.a

references to standard members of a multinational group were to members of the
group that are investment entities, and

41.1.5.1.b

in paragraph 3—

41.1.5.1.b.i

in sub-paragraph (1), for “Conditions A to D” there were substituted
“Conditions A to E” ,

41.1.5.1.b.ii

after sub-paragraph (6), there were inserted—

41.1.5.1.b.ii.7

Condition E is that the qualifying domestic top-up tax applying in the
territory—

41.1.5.1.b.ii.7.a

does not generally impose a charge on members of the group that are investment
entities, and

41.1.5.1.b.ii.7.b

does not include provision for a charge to be imposed on such members in
circumstances where there would otherwise be an amount of tax that was not
charged to any member of the group in that territory.

41.1.5.2

Accordingly, the filing member of a multinational group may make a separate
qualifying domestic top-up tax safe harbour election in respect of members of
the group that are investment entities.

################ Application in the case of minority owned members

41.1.6

41.1.6.1

Chapter 1 of this Part of this Schedule to applies to minority owned members
of a multinational group and has effect for that purpose as if references to
standard members of a multinational group were to members of the group that
are minority owned members.

41.1.6.2

Accordingly, the filing member of a multinational group may make a separate
qualifying domestic top-up tax safe harbour election in respect of minority
owned members of the group.

41.2

(1), in the words before paragraph (a), for “Schedule 16” substitute
“Schedules 16 and 16A” .

###### Securitisation entities

42

42.1

42.1.a

after subsection (3) insert—

42.1.a.3A

A securitisation company that is not a member of a group for the purposes of
domestic top-up tax is a DTT excluded entity (and see section 267A).

42.1.b

in subsection (4)—

42.1.b.i

the words from ““qualifying” to the end become the first definition, and

42.1.b.ii

after that definition insert—

      “ securitisation company ” has the meaning it has in the Taxation of
Securitisation Companies Regulations 2006 (see regulation 4).

42.2

After section 267 insert—

############ Securitisation companies in a group treated as not consolidated

42.2.267A

42.2.267A.1

Subsection (2) applies to a securitisation company that is a member of a
group.

42.2.267A.2

The company is only to be regarded as a member of the group for the purposes
of applying Condition C in section 266 in relation to other members of the
group (revenue threshold for group).

42.2.267A.3

Otherwise, the company is to be treated as not being a member of any group for
the purposes of domestic top-up tax.

42.3

After section 272 insert—

############ Treatment of covered bond vehicles

42.3.272A

42.3.272A.1

This section applies where—

42.3.272A.1.a

a covered bond vehicle that is a member of a group would, ignoring this
section, have a top-up amount or an additional top-up amount for an accounting
period, and

42.3.272A.1.b

at least one of the other members of the group in that period—

42.3.272A.1.b.i

is located in the United Kingdom, and

42.3.272A.1.b.ii

is not a covered bond vehicle.

42.3.272A.2

For domestic purposes, section 193 (calculation of top-up amounts) has effect
for the purpose of determining the top-up amounts (and additional top-up
amounts) of—

42.3.272A.2.a

the covered bond vehicle, and

42.3.272A.2.b

the other members of the group that are located in the United Kingdom,

as if the adjusted profits of the covered bond vehicle were nil.

42.3.272A.3

But subsection (4) applies if none of the members of the group that are
located in the United Kingdom, and are not covered bond vehicles, have made a
profit for that period (and accordingly will not, ignoring that subsection,
have top-up amounts).

42.3.272A.4

Each of those members has a top-up amount equal to the amount given by
dividing—

42.3.272A.4.a

the sum of the top-up amounts and additional top-up amounts that, ignoring
subsection (2), each covered bond vehicle located in the United Kingdom would
otherwise have, by

42.3.272A.4.b

the number of those members.

42.3.272A.5

For the purposes of this section “ covered bond vehicle ” has the meaning
given by paragraph 53(7) of Schedule 19 to FA 2011.

An investment entity is a DTT excluded entity if—

43.1.b.3C.a

43.1.b.3C.b

(see also section 272(8)(e) which has the effect of attributing those amounts
to standard members of the group that are qualifying entities and are located

43.3.b.10.a

(8)(e), and

43.3.b.10.b

not, ignoring subsection  (11) , have top-up amounts).

43.3.b.11

by the number of qualifying entities that are standard members of the group.

###### Effect of becoming subject to Pillar Two rules

45

45.1

After section 273 insert—

############ References to Pillar Two rules

45.1.273A

45.1.273A.1

The provisions mentioned in subsection (2) apply to a qualifying entity, for
domestic or domestic entity purposes, as if the references to the first
accounting period for which the Pillar Two rules apply were to the first
accounting period for which the entity is a qualifying entity.

45.1.273A.2

Those provisions are—

45.1.273A.2.a

section 185;

45.1.273A.2.b

section 187;

45.1.273A.2.d

sub-paragraph (4) of paragraph 2 of Schedule 16 (but see also section
276(c)(iii) which omits that paragraph in the case of a qualifying entity that
is not a member of a group).

############ Effect of becoming subject to Pillar Two rules

45.1.273B

45.1.273B.1

This section applies where the Pillar Two rules did not apply to a qualifying
entity for one or more accounting periods (each a “pre-Pillar Two period”).

45.1.273B.2

Where—

45.1.273B.2.a

the entity has a recaptured deferred tax liability arising as a result of
section 184 (recaptured deferred tax liabilities),

45.1.273B.2.b

the initial period, in relation to that liability, is a pre-Pillar Two period,
and

45.1.273B.2.c

the first accounting period in which the Pillar Two rules apply to the entity
is earlier than the sixth accounting period after the initial period,

section 184(2) (recalculation in initial period taking account of recaptured
deferred tax liability) does not apply in relation to that recaptured deferred
tax liability.

45.1.273B.3

Where an election under section 187 (election for losses to be treated as
special loss deferred tax assets) applied to the entity in a pre-Pillar Two
period—

45.1.273B.3.a

the election ceases to have effect for the first accounting period in which
the Pillar Two rules apply, and

45.1.273B.3.b

subsection (2)(b) of section 187 does not apply to prevent the making of an
election under section 187 that applies to the entity and that has effect for
that period, but

45.1.273B.3.c

no remaining amount of special loss deferred tax assets that arose in a pre-
Pillar Two period may be used in that first accounting period or any
subsequent accounting period.

45.1.273B.4

Subsection (5) or (6) (as the case may be) applies where—

45.1.273B.4.a

a deferred tax asset arises to the entity in a pre-Pillar Two period,

45.1.273B.4.b

section 185(7)—

45.1.273B.4.b.i

applies to that asset for the purposes of multinational top-up tax, or

45.1.273B.4.b.ii

would, ignoring subsection (5) below, apply to that asset for those purposes,
and

45.1.273B.4.c

the asset is reflected in a collective additional amount for the purposes of
domestic top-up tax.

45.1.273B.5

Where—

45.1.273B.5.a

an election has been made under section 205 (election to carry forward) in
relation to the collective additional amount,

45.1.273B.5.b

the subtraction required by subsection (2)(a) of that section has not occurred
in a pre-Pillar Two period,

the amount to be subtracted as a result of that subsection is to be reduced by
so much of that amount as reflects the asset.

45.1.273B.6

Otherwise, section 185(7) does not apply to the asset for the purposes of
multinational top-up tax to the extent it was reflected in a collective
additional amount for the purposes domestic top-up tax.

45.2

In section 276 (application of transitional provision)—

45.2.a

after paragraph (a) insert—

45.2.a.aa

where a qualifying member is a member of a group, for paragraph 3(2)(c) there
were substituted—

45.2.a.aa.c

the election has been made in respect of the territory for each preceding
accounting period that commenced on or after 31 December 2023—

45.2.a.aa.c.i

in which the Pillar Two rules would, ignoring any transitional safe harbour
election, have applied to any member of the group in the territory, and

45.2.a.aa.c.ii

in which any member of the group is a qualifying entity for the purposes of
domestic top-up tax,

,

, and

45.2.b

in paragraph (c), after sub-paragraph (iii) insert—

45.2.b.iiia

for paragraph 3(2)(c) there were substituted—

45.2.b.iiia.c

the election has been made in respect of the territory for each preceding
accounting period that commenced on or after 31 December 2023 in which the
member was a qualifying entity for the purposes of domestic top-up tax,

,

  Promotion of tax avoidance schemes

Section 33

##### Disqualification for promoting tax avoidance

1

In CDDA 1986, after section 8ZE insert—

######### Disqualification for promoting tax avoidance

########## Disqualification following winding up under s.85 of Finance Act 2022

1.8ZF

1.8ZF.1

The court must make a disqualification order against a person if, on an
application under this section, it is satisfied—

1.8ZF.1.a

that the person has at any time after the coming into force of this section
been a director of a company while the company was a relevant body within the
meaning of section 85(4) of the Finance Act 2022 (winding up of promoters of
tax avoidance schemes), and

1.8ZF.1.b

that a court has made a winding-up order in respect of the company under
section 85(3) of that Act (whether while the person was a director or
subsequently).

1.8ZF.2

An officer of Revenue and Customs may make an application to the court for a
disqualification order against a person under this section if it appears to
the officer that it is expedient in the public interest for such an order to
be made.

1.8ZF.3

Except with the permission of the court, an application under  subsection (2)
may not be made after the end of the period of 3 years beginning with the day
on which the winding-up order in question is made.

1.8ZF.4

Under this section the minimum period of disqualification is 2 years, and the
maximum is 15 years.

1.8ZF.5

An officer of Revenue and Customs may accept a disqualification undertaking if
it appears to the officer—

1.8ZF.5.a

that the conditions mentioned in  subsection (1)  are satisfied in relation to
the person who has offered to give the disqualification undertaking, and

1.8ZF.5.b

that it is expedient in the public interest that the officer should accept the
undertaking (instead of applying, or proceeding with an application, for a
disqualification order).

1.8ZF.6

In this section—

      “ company ” includes overseas company;           “ court ” means—
the court having jurisdiction for the purposes of the Insolvency Act 1986, or
the High Court in Northern Ireland;                 “ director ” includes a
shadow director.

########## Disqualification on finding of unfitness: promoters of tax avoidance

1.8ZG

1.8ZG.1

The court may make a disqualification order against a person if, on an
application under this section, it is satisfied—

1.8ZG.1.a

that the person—

1.8ZG.1.a.i

is a director of a company that carries on business as a promoter within the
meaning of Part 5 of the Finance Act 2014 (promoters of tax avoidance
schemes), or

1.8ZG.1.a.ii

after the coming into force of this section, was a director of a company at a
time at which it did so, and

1.8ZG.1.b

that the person’s conduct in relation to the company (either taken alone or
taken together with the person’s conduct as a director of one or more other
companies) makes the person unfit to be concerned in the management of a
company.

1.8ZG.2

For the purposes of  subsection (1) (a) (i) , Part 5 of the Finance Act 2014
has effect as if, in section 234 of that Act—

1.8ZG.2.a

references to “tax” included value added tax and other indirect taxes, and

1.8ZG.2.b

the definition of “tax advantage” also included a tax advantage as defined for
VAT in paragraph 6, and for other indirect taxes in paragraph 7, of Schedule
17 to the Finance (No. 2) Act 2017 (disclosure of tax avoidance schemes: VAT
and other indirect taxes).

1.8ZG.3

References in  subsection (1) (b)  to a person’s conduct include conduct
occurring before, as well as after, the coming into force of this section.

1.8ZG.4

An officer of Revenue and Customs may make an application to the court for a
disqualification order against a person under this section if it appears to
the officer that it is expedient in the public interest for such an order to
be made.

1.8ZG.5

The maximum period of disqualification under this section is 15 years.

1.8ZG.6

An officer of Revenue and Customs may accept a disqualification undertaking if
it appears to the officer—

1.8ZG.6.a

that the conditions mentioned in  subsection (1)  are satisfied in relation to
the person who has offered to give the disqualification undertaking, and

1.8ZG.6.b

that it is expedient in the public interest that the officer should accept the
undertaking (instead of applying, or proceeding with an application, for a
disqualification order).

1.8ZG.7

In this section—

      “ company ” includes overseas company;           “ the court ” means—
in England and Wales, the High Court;           in Scotland, the Court of
Session;           in Northern Ireland, the High Court in Northern Ireland;
“ director ” includes a shadow director;           “ indirect tax ” has the
same meaning as in Schedule 17 to the Finance (No. 2) Act 2017 (see paragraph
2(1) of that Schedule).

##### Extent

4

4.1

The amendments made by  paragraph 1  extend to England and Wales, Scotland and
Northern Ireland.

4.2

The amendments made by  paragraph 2  extend to—

4.2.a

England and Wales and Scotland, and

4.2.b

Northern Ireland, so far as relating to applications and orders made, and
undertakings accepted, under sections  8ZF  or  8ZG  of CDDA 1986 (inserted by
paragraph 1 ).

4.3

The other provisions of CDDA 1986, except for sections 13 to 15 (consequences
of contravention), extend to Northern Ireland (as well as England and Wales
and Scotland) so far as relating to applications and orders made, and
undertakings accepted, under section  8ZF  or  8ZG .

##### Practice and procedure

5

5.1

The procedural rules for applications under section 8 of CDDA 1986 apply to
HMRC disqualification applications as they apply to applications by the
Secretary of State, subject to any necessary modifications.

5.2

The procedural rules for applications under Article 11 of the Company
Directors Disqualification (Northern Ireland) Order 2002 ( S.I. 2002/3150
(N.I. 4))  apply to HMRC disqualification applications as they apply to
applications by the Department for the Economy in Northern Ireland, subject to
any necessary modifications.

5.3

Sub-paragraphs  (1)  and  (2)  apply only if, and to the extent that, there
are not otherwise procedural rules for HMRC disqualification applications.

5.4

In this paragraph—

5.4.a

the “procedural rules” for applications of a particular kind are the rules,
regulations or practice directions for the time being governing the practice
and procedure (including fees) in respect of applications of that kind, and

5.4.b

an “HMRC disqualification application” is an application by an officer of
Revenue and Customs under section  8ZF  or  8ZG  of CDDA 1986.

##### Interpretation

6

In this Schedule, “ CDDA 1986 ” means the Company Directors Disqualification
Act 1986.
